Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
8 min
Wala of Manumission is 'Asabah (Residuary)
Ruling with proofs from Quran, hadith, and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that wala of manumission creates a residuary inheritance right and apply it to determine who inherits when a freed slave dies.

Core Idea
The manumittor inherits as residuary only if the freed slave has no agnatic blood relatives.

This lesson explores the Hanafi ruling on wala (patronage) — a unique bond created by manumission. In Islamic inheritance law, wala gives the manumittor a residuary right ('asabah) after Quranic shares, but only if the freed slave has no living agnatic relatives. We will examine the proofs from the Quran, hadith, and early practice that establish this rule, and understand its application in succession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
The passage states that wala of manumission is 'asabah (residuary). State what that means: the manumittor inherits as an 'asabah after the fixed Quranic shares are given.
2
Understand the priority order
The freed slave's agnatic blood relatives (e.g., sons, brothers, paternal uncles) are more entitled than the manumittor. Only if none exist does the manumittor take.
This reflects the principle that blood kinship (nasab) takes precedence over patronage (wala).
3
Analyze the specific case
If the freed slave dies first, then the manumittor dies, the inheritance goes to the sons of the freed slave, not his daughters. Why? Because residuary inheritance passes to males, not females.
Daughters are not 'asabah; they receive fixed shares.
4
Examine the proofs
The passage cites several proofs: Quran 4:11 (general male preference), the hadith 'Give the fixed shares to their recipients, and whatever remains is for the nearest male relative' (Bukhari and Muslim), and narrations from az-Zuhri and al-Hasan indicating that wala follows the nearest male relative of the manumittor.
Identify how each proof supports the 'asabah nature of wala.
5
Note cross-madhhab considerations
The Shafi'i school agrees that wala creates a residuary right, but they differ in the order of inheritance when both agnatic relatives and the manumittor exist.
In the Hanafi school, the manumittor only inherits when there are no agnatic relatives at all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْوَلَاءِ وَوَلَاءُ الْعَتَاقَةِ تَعْصِيبٌ فَإِنْ كَانَ لِلْمُعْتِقِ عَصَبَةٌ مِنْ النَّسَبِ فَهُمْ أَوْلَى مِنْهُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ عَصَبَةٌ مِنْ النَّسَبِ فَمِيرَاتُهُ لِلْمُعْتِقِ فَإِنْ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى ثُمَّ مَاتَ الْمُعْتَقُ فَمِيرَاثُهُ لِبَنِي الْمَوْلَى دُونَ بَنَاتِهِ وَجْهُ الْآيَةِ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَاءُ الْعَتَاقَةِ تَعْصِيبٌ يُوصِيكُمُ اللَّهُ فِي أَوْلَدِكُمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَةِ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ (سورة النساء 11) وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَاءُ الْعَتَاقَةِ تَعْصِيبٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: أَلْحِقُوا الْفَرَائِضَ بِأَهْلِهَا فَمَا بَقِيَ فَهُوَ لِأَوْلَى رَجُلٍ ذَكَرٍ (رواه البخاري ومسلم) وَجْهُ قَوْلِ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَاءُ الْعَتَاقَةِ تَعْصِيبٌ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: الْمَوْلَى أَخٌ فِي الدِّينِ وَنِعْمَةٌ وَأَحَقُّ النَّاسِ عِيرَائِهِ أَقْرَبُهُمْ مِنَ الْمُعْتِقِ (رواه الدارمي) وَجْهُ قَوْلِ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَاءُ الْعَتَاقَةِ تَعْصِيبٌ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: أَرَادَ رَجُلٌ أَنْ يَشْتَرِيَ عَبْدًا فَلَمْ يُقْضَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ صَاحِبِهِ بَيْعٌ فَحَلِفَ رَجُلٌ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ بِعِتْقِهِ فَاشْتَرَاهُ فَأَعْتَقَهُ فَذَكَرَهُ لِلنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: فَكَيْفَ بِصُحْبَتِهِ؟ فَقَالَ: هُوَ لَكَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ لَهُ عُصْبَةٌ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ عُصْبَةٌ فَهُوَ لَكَ (رواه عبد الرزاق) وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَاءُ الْعَتَاقَةِ تَعْصِيبٌ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: أَحْقُوا الْفَرَائِضَ بِأَهْلِهَا فَمَا بَقِيَ فَهُوَ لِأَوْلَى رَجُلٍ ذَكَرٍ (رواه البخاري ومسلم)
Book of Patronage. The patronage of manumission is a tie of residuary inheritance. So if the freed one has agnatic relatives by lineage, they are more entitled than the manumittor. If he has no agnatic relatives by lineage, then his inheritance goes to the manumittor. If the freed slave dies then the manumittor dies, his inheritance goes to the sons of the freed slave, not his daughters. The aspect of the verse for establishing that the patronage of manumission is residuary: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male a share equal to that of two females' (Surah an-Nisa 11). The aspect of the hadith for establishing that the patronage of manumission is residuary: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'Give the fixed shares to their recipients, and whatever remains is for the nearest male relative' (narrated by Bukhari and Muslim). The aspect of the saying of a Tabi'i for establishing that the patronage of manumission is residuary: from az-Zuhri who said: the Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'The freed slave is a brother in religion and a blessing, and the most entitled of people to his inheritance is the closest relative of the manumittor' (narrated by ad-Darimi). The aspect of the saying of a Tabi'i for establishing that the patronage of manumission is residuary: from al-Hasan who said: a man wanted to buy a slave but a sale was not concluded between him and his owner, so a Muslim man swore to free him, then bought him and freed him. He mentioned that to the Prophet (ﷺ) who said: 'How about his companionship?' The Prophet (ﷺ) said: 'He is yours unless he has an agnatic relative; if he has no agnatic relative, then he is yours' (narrated by Abdur Razzaq). The aspect of the hadith for establishing that the patronage of manumission is residuary: from Ibn Abbas from the Prophet (ﷺ) who said: 'Give the fixed shares to their recipients, and whatever remains is for the nearest male relative' (narrated by Bukhari and Muslim).
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the book of Wala (patronage) with multiple proofs. The ruling states that the wala of manumission creates a residuary tie (ta'sib). This means that when the freed slave dies without a Quranic sharer, the manumittor inherits as an 'asabah (residuary heir). However, if the freed slave has agnatic blood relatives (e.g., his own sons, brothers, paternal uncles), they take precedence over the manumittor. The manumittor only inherits when there are no such agnatic relatives. Additionally, if the freed slave dies first, and then the manumittor dies, the inheritance goes to the sons of the freed slave (not his daughters), because males are prioritized in residuary inheritance. The passage then provides evidential proofs: a verse from Surah an-Nisa (11) about male-female shares in inheritance (though the primary proof here is the principle of 'asabah), the famous hadith 'Give the fixed shares to their recipients, and whatever remains is for the nearest male relative' (which establishes that after Quranic shares, the residue goes to the nearest male 'asabah), and narrations from az-Zuhri and al-Hasan indicating that the wala follows the nearest relative of the manumittor. The Hanafi school relies on these proofs to uphold that wala is a form of 'asabah, not a separate category. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, as it is the established position of the school.

Key Terms
الْوَلَاء (al-walā'): Patronage, a legal bond of allegiance and inheritance established through manumission or contract.
تَعْصِيب (ta‘ṣīb): The status of being an 'asabah (residuary heir) who inherits after the Quranic shares are given.
الْمُعْتِق (al-mu‘tiq): The manumittor, the person who frees a slave and thereby gains the wala over them.
الْمَوْلَى (al-mawlā): The freed slave; in this context, the person who has been manumitted and is subject to the wala.
عَصَبَة (‘aṣabah): Agnatic male relative who inherits as a residuary heir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who inherits from a freed slave who dies without any agnatic relatives?
A) His daughters
B) His manumittor
C) His wife
D) The state treasury

Key Takeaway
Wala of manumission is a residuary right ('asabah) for the manumittor, but it is subordinate to the freed slave's agnatic blood relatives.

Women's Wala and Wala by Conversion
Rulings on women's wala and validity of wala by conversion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling on women's wala and EXPLAIN the validity conditions for wala by conversion.

Core Idea
Women only inherit wala from their own manumissions; wala by conversion is valid with contract.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses two aspects of wala (patronage): women's limited right to inherit wala, and the establishment of wala through conversion to Islam. Understanding these rules is essential because wala determines inheritance and bloodwit liability. We will examine the textual proof from the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Extract the ruling on women's wala
Identify the precise limitation: women only acquire wala from slaves they personally freed, or from those freed by their own freed slaves, or through kitabah/tadbir related to their own slaves.
This excludes wala from the manumissions of their husbands or other male relatives.
2
Extract the ruling on wala by conversion
Identify that wala al-muwalah (wala by conversion) is valid when a person becomes Muslim at the hands of another and contracts a wala agreement, making the patron the heir and bloodwit payer.
The contract can be made with the converter or with someone else.
3
Identify the primary proof
The passage cites the practice of Ali, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zaid ibn Thabit, who gave wala to the eldest 'asabah and did not let women inherit wala except from their own manumissions.
This is a qawl sahabi (saying of a Companion) and constitutes a dalil for the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the additional proofs
The passage also includes a Tabi'i saying from Ibrahim an-Nakha'i, Quranic verses (al-Anfal 75, an-Nisa 33), and a hadith from Tamim ad-Dari to support wala al-muwalah.
These serve as corroborative evidence for the validity of wala by conversion.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
Combine the rulings: women's wala is limited to their own manumissions, and wala al-muwalah is valid with a contract. These positions are part of the Zahir al-Riwayah.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is mentioned in this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ لِلنِّسَاءِ مِنَ الْوَلَاءِ إِلَّا مَا أَعْتَقْنَ أَوْ أَعْتَقَ مَنْ أَعْتَقْنَ أَوْ كَاتَبْنَ أَوْ كَاتَبَ مَنْ كَاتَبْنَ أَوْ دَبَّرَتْ أَوْ دَبَّرَ مَنْ دَبَّرْنَ فَإِنْ تَرَكَ الْمَوْلَى ابْنًا وَأَوْلَادَ ابْنٍ آخَرَ فَمِيرَاثُ الْمُعْتَقِ لِلِابْنِ دُونَ بَنِي الِابْنِ وَالْوَلَاءُ لِلْكَبِيرِ وَإِذَا أَسْلَمَ رَجُلٌ عَلَى يَدِ رَجُلٍ وَوَالَاهُ عَلَى أَنْ يَرِثَهُ وَيَعْقِلَ عَنْهُ أَوْ أَسْلَمَ عَلَى يَدِ غَيْرِهِ وَوَالَاهُ فَالْوَلَاءُ صَحِيحٌ وَعَقْلُهُ عَلَى مَوْلَاهُ وَجْهُ قَوْلِ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ مَا ذُكِرَ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ وَعَبْدِ اللَّهِ وَزَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا يَجْعَلُونَ الْوَلَاءَ لِلْكُبْرِ مِنَ الْعَصَبَةِ وَلاَ يُوَرِّثُونَ النِّسَاءَ إِلَّا مَا أَعْتَقْنَ أَوْ أَعْتَقَ مَنْ أَعْتَقْنَ (رَوَاهُ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ وَالدَّارِمِيُّ) وَجْهُ قَوْلِ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَاءِ الْإِسْلَامِ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ فِي الرَّجُلِ يُوَالِي الرَّجُلَ فَيُسْلِمُ عَلَى يَدَيْهِ قَالَ يَعْقِلُ عَنْهُ وَيَرِثُهُ (رَوَاهُ عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ) وَجْهُ الْآيَةِ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَاءِ الْإِسْلَامِ وَأُولُوا الْأَرْحَامِ بَعْضُهُمْ أَوْلَى بِبَعْضٍ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ (الْأَنْفَال 75) وَالَّذِينَ عَقَدَتْ أَيْمَانُكُمْ فَآتُوهُمْ نَصِيبَهُمْ (النِّسَاء 33) وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَاءِ الْإِسْلَامِ عَنْ تَمِيمٍ الدَّارِيِّ قَالَ سَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ هُوَ أَحَقُّ النَّاسِ بِمَحْيَاهُ وَمَمَاتِهِ (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ)
Women have no share in wala except from those they have freed, or those freed by those they freed, or those they made a kitabah with, or those who made kitabah with those they made kitabah with, or those they made a tadbir with, or those who made tadbir with those they made tadbir with. If the freed slave leaves a son and children of another son, the inheritance of the manumittor goes to the son, not to the children of the son, and the wala goes to the eldest. When a man becomes Muslim at the hands of another and contracts wala with him on the condition that he inherits from him and pays his bloodwit, or if he becomes Muslim at the hands of someone else and contracts wala, the wala is valid and his bloodwit is upon his patron. The aspect of the saying of a Companion for establishing what was mentioned: from Ali, Abdullah, and Zaid ibn Thabit that they used to give wala to the eldest of the asabah and did not let women inherit wala except from those they freed or those freed by those they freed (narrated by al-Bayhaqi and ad-Darimi). The aspect of the saying of a Tabi'i for establishing the wala of Islam: from Ibrahim concerning the man who contracts wala with a man and becomes Muslim at his hands – he said: he pays bloodwit for him and inherits from him (narrated by Abdur Razzaq). The aspect of the verse for establishing the wala of Islam: 'And those of kinship are more entitled to each other in the decree of Allah' (Surah al-Anfal 75) and 'And those your right hands have pledged – give them their share' (Surah an-Nisa 33). The aspect of the hadith for establishing the wala of Islam: from Tamim ad-Dari who said: I asked the Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) and he said: 'He is the most entitled of people to his life and his death' (narrated by Abu Dawud).
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage contains several rulings. First, women do not inherit wala from the freed slaves of their male relatives; they only get wala from slaves they personally freed or from those freed by their own freed slaves (e.g., their former slave's manumissions). They also acquire wala through kitabah (contract of manumission) and tadbir (bequest of freedom). Second, inheritance distribution: if the freed slave dies leaving a son and also grandchildren from another son, the manumittor's share (if he is the heir) goes to the son, not to the grandchildren. The wala itself goes to the eldest among the asabah (the son). Third, a man who becomes Muslim at the hands of another and contracts wala (wala al-muwalah) validly establishes that wala, so the patron inherits from him and is liable for his bloodwit. The proofs include the practice of Ali, Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, and Zaid ibn Thabit, a statement of Ibrahim an-Nakha'i, and Quranic verses about kinship and pledges, plus a hadith from Tamim ad-Dari. These rulings are part of the Hanafi school's position on wala.

Key Terms
الْوَلَاء (al-walā'): Patronage, including both wala al-itaqah (by manumission) and wala al-muwalah (by conversion and contract).
الْكِتَابَة (al-kitābah): A contract between a master and a slave for the slave to earn and pay for freedom in installments.
التَّدْبِير (al-tadbīr): A master's declaration that a slave will be free after the master's death.
وَلَاءُ الْإِسْلَام (walā' al-islām): Patronage established when a person becomes Muslim at the hands of another and contracts a wala agreement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling regarding women inheriting wala?
A) Women inherit wala from all male relatives
B) Women do not inherit wala at all
C) Women inherit wala only from those they personally freed or their freed slaves
D) Women inherit wala equally with men

Key Takeaway
Women's right to wala is strictly limited to their own manumissions, while wala by conversion is valid when contracted, supported by multiple proofs.

Rulings of Wala' (Clientage) with Proofs
Rulings on wala' with naqli proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three main rulings on wala' in Hanafi fiqh, identify the proofs for each, and explain the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding inheritance of a convert.

Core Idea
Wala' is an exclusive bond that prioritizes blood relatives and cannot be freely transferred.

This lesson examines the Hanafi rulings on wala' (clientage) as presented in Al-Quduri's matn with supporting proofs. Wala' arises from emancipation (ʿitq) or contract (muwālāt), creating inheritance and blood-money obligations. The text clarifies who inherits when a freed slave dies, the limited right to transfer wala', and the prohibition for the emancipator to reassign it. A key disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i on the inheritance of a convert is also addressed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings
Read the first part of the matn (from 'kitab al-wala'' to 'laysa li-mawla al-ʻitāqati an yuwāliya ahadā'). Identify three distinct rulings: inheritance priority, transfer conditions, and prohibition for the emancipator.
These are the core legal rules.
2
Link each ruling to its proof
For each ruling, find the corresponding hadith or companion saying cited. Note the reference (e.g., Tirmidhi, Bukhari).
Proofs are marked with 'wajh' ( وجه ) in the text.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
For each proof, identify the key phrase that indicates the ruling. For example, 'innamā al-walā'u liman aʻtaqa' uses 'innamā' for restriction.
Focus on linguistic and legal reasoning.
4
Identify the Shafi'i dispute
Locate the debate about the inheritance of a person who accepts Islam at someone's hands. Understand the opposing argument from al-Hasan's saying.
This is part of the ruling on inheritance when there is no heir.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
See how the Hanafi school interprets the proof differently, prioritizing the one who facilitated Islam over the public treasury.
This shows the interplay of dalil and tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْوَلَاءِ
فَإِنْ مَاتَ وَلَا وَارِثَ لَهُ فَمِيرَاثُهُ لِلْمَوْلَى وَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ وَارِثْ فَهُوَ أَوْلَى مِنْهُ
وَلِلْمَوْلَى أَنْ يَنْتَقِلَ عَنْهُ بِوِلايَةٍ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ مَا لَمْ يَعْقِلْ عَنْهُ الْأَعْلَى فَإِنْ عَقَلَ عَنْهُ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ أَنْ يَتَحَوَّلَ بِوَلائِهِ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ
وَلَيْسَ لِمَوْلَى الْعَتَاقَةِ أَنْ يُوَاليَ أَحَدًا
اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مَا السُّنَّةُ فِي الرَّجُلِ مِنْ أَهْلِ الشَّرْكِ يُسْلِمُ عَلَى يَدَيْ رَجُلٍ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ؟ فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ : «هُوَ أَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِمَحْيَاهُ وَمَاتِهِ»، سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مِيرَاتِ الَّذِي يُسْلِمُ عَلَى يَدَيِ الرَّجُلِ، نمبر 2112)
وجه : (۱) دليل الشافعى قول التابعى الثبوت وَإِذَا أَسْلَمَ رَجُلٌ عَلَى يَدِ رَجُلٍ \ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ قَالَا: مِيرَاثُهُ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ»، مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ النَّصْرَانِي يُسْلِمُ عَلَى يَدِ رَجُلٍ، نمبر 16274) وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت فَإِنْ مَاتَ وَلَا وَارِثَ لَهُ وَأُوْلُوا الْأَرْحَامِ بَعْضُهُمْ أَوْلَى بِبَعْضٍ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ (سورة الانفال، 8 آية، نمبر 75)
وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ مَاتَ وَلَا وَارِثَ لَهُ \ وَالشَّعْيَ «أَنَّ الرَّجُلَ إِذَا مَاتَ وَتَرَكَ مَوَالِيَهُ الَّذِينَ أَعْتَقُوهُ وَلَمْ يَدَعْ ذَا رَحِمٍ إِلَّا أُمَّا أَوْ خَالَةً دَفَعُوا مِيرَاثَهُ إِلَيْهَا، وَلَمْ يُوَرِّثُوا مَوَالِيَهُ مَعَهَا وَإِنَّهُمْ لَا يُوَرِّثُونَ مَوَالِيَهُ مَعَ ذِي رَحِمٍ»، (مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ ذِي الْقَرَابَةِ، نمبر 16203)
وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَلِلْمَوْلَى أَنْ يَنْتَقِلَ عَنْهُ بِوِلايَةٍ إِلَى غَيْرِهِ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، مِثْلَ حَدِيثِ مَعْمَرٍ وَزَادَ: وَلَهُ أَنْ يُحَوّلَ وَلَاءَهُ حَيْثُ شَاءَ مَا لَمْ يَعْقِلْ عَنْهُ،»،(مصنف عبد الرزاق، بَابُ النَّصْرَانِي يُسْلِمُ عَلَى يَدِ رَجُلٍ، نمبر 16275)
ها وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ لِمَوْلَى الْعَتَاقَةِ أَنْ يُوَالِيَ أَحَدًا \ عَنْ نَافِعٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِنَّمَا الْوَلَاءُ لِمَنْ أَعْتَقَ.»،(بخاري شريف، بَابٌ: الْوَلَاءُ لِمَنْ أَعْتَقَ وَمِيرَاتُ اللَّقِيطِ وَقَالَ عُمَرُ اللَّقِيطُ حُقٌّ، نمبر 6752)
وجه: (٢) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَيْسَ لِمَوْلَى الْعَتَاقَةِ أَنْ يُوَالِيَ أَحَدًا \ قَالَ عَلِيٌّ : وَمَنْ وَالَى قَوْمًا بِغَيْرِ إِذْنِ مَوَالِيهِ، فَعَلَيْهِ لَعْنَةُ اللهِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ لَا يُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ صَرْفٌ وَلَا عَدْلٌ. وَذِمَّةُ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَاحِدَةٌ ، يَسْعَى بِمَا أَدْنَاهُمْ، فَمَنْ أَخْفَرَ مُسْلِمًا فَعَلَيْهِ لَعْنَةُ اللهِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ وَالنَّاسِ أَجْمَعِينَ لا يُقْبَلُ مِنْهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ صَرْفٌ وَلا عَدْلٌ.» (بخاري شريف بَابُ إِثْمِ مَنْ تَبَرَّأَ مِنْ مَوَالِيهِ، نمبر 6755)
اصول: مولی عتاقہ اور مولی الموالات پر ذوی الارحام کو مقدم رکھا جائے گا۔
اصول : آزاد شده غلام ولاء کسی دوسرے کو نہیں منتقل کر سکتا ہے۔
Book of Wala'. If he dies and has no heir, his inheritance goes to the master. If he has an heir, then the heir is more deserving than the master. The master has the right to transfer his wala' to someone else as long as the higher [relative] does not pay blood money on his behalf. If [the higher relative] does pay blood money, then he does not have the right to transfer his wala' to others. The master of emancipation is not allowed to contract wala' with anyone. ... (then hadith and proofs)
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi rulings on wala' (clientage) as found in Al-Quduri's matn, with proofs from hadith and sayings of the Companions. The rulings cover three main areas: (1) inheritance through wala' when the freed slave dies without blood relatives; (2) the right of the master to transfer the wala' to another before the payment of 'aql (blood money); and (3) the prohibition for the emancipating master to contract wala' with another person. The commentator provides evidence from the Sunnah and the actions of the Companions to support each ruling. Notably, there is a mention of a Shafi'i proof (وجه ۱) for the first ruling, indicating a disagreement with Imam Shafi'i. The Hanafi position emphasizes that wala' is an exclusive bond that cannot be arbitrarily transferred, and that blood relatives take precedence over the master in inheritance.

Key Terms
الْوَلَاء (al-walā'): Clientage relationship established by emancipation (ʿitq) or by contract (walā' al-muwālāt), entailing mutual inheritance rights and obligations of 'aql (blood money).
مَوْلَى الْعَتَاقَة (mawlā al-ʿitāqah): The master who emancipates a slave, thereby acquiring walā' rights over the freed person.
ذَوُو الْأَرْحَام (dhawū al-arhām): Blood relatives who are not entitled to a fixed share (fard) and are not residuaries (ʿaṣabah), such as maternal uncles and aunts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, who inherits from a freed slave who dies without any blood relatives?
A) The master of emancipation (mawlā al-ʿitāqah)
B) The Muslim in whose presence he accepted Islam
C) The public treasury (bayt al-māl)
D) His former owner's relatives

Key Takeaway
Wala' is an exclusive bond: blood relatives always take precedence over the master, and the master of emancipation cannot transfer his wala' to another.

Faraid — Inheritance

Order of Payment from the Deceased's Estate
Usul principle on estate priority

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct order of distribution from a deceased Muslim's estate: debt, bequests (within one-third), and inheritance.

Core Idea
Debt must be paid before any bequest or inheritance can be executed.

This lesson introduces a foundational principle in Islamic inheritance law (faraid). The estate of a deceased Muslim is not immediately divided among heirs; it is subject to prior claims. Understanding this priority is crucial for correct distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories
Identify the three types of claims on the estate: debts, bequests (wasiyyah), and inheritance shares.
2
State the priority order
The text states that debt is paid first, then bequests from one-third of the remaining estate, and finally inheritance to the heirs.
3
Understand the one-third limit
Bequests are limited to one-third of the estate after debts. If bequests exceed one-third, they are reduced proportionally.
4
Apply the order
Given an estate, always calculate debts, then bequests within the limit, then distribute the remainder to heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصول: میت کے مال سے اولا قرض ادا کیا جائے، ثانیا تہائی مال سے وصیتوں کا نفاذ بعد ازاں مال ورثامیں مال تقسیم ہو گا۔
Principle: From the property of the deceased, first debt is paid, secondly bequests are executed from one-third of the property, then the property is distributed among the heirs.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This is a foundational principle in Islamic inheritance law (faraid). The estate is charged in order: 1) debts owed to people, 2) expenses of funeral, 3) bequests up to one-third, 4) remaining to heirs by shares. This Urdu note summarizes the priority that appears in the main text.

Key Terms
قرض (qarḍ): Debts owed by the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the correct order of distribution from a deceased's estate in Hanafi fiqh?
A) Bequests, then debt, then inheritance
B) Debt, then bequests (up to one-third), then inheritance
C) Inheritance, then debt, then bequests
D) All equally from the start

Key Takeaway
Debt must be settled before any bequest is executed, and bequests are limited to one-third of the remaining estate.

Faraid — Inheritance
beginner

The Ten Male and Seven Female Inheritors in Faraid
Listing of inheritors and non-inheritors with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ten male and seven female inheritors as per Hanafi faraid, and identify the four persons who are permanently barred from inheritance.

Core Idea
Only ten specific male and seven specific female relatives inherit; four persons are permanently barred.

This foundational passage from al-Quduri's matn opens the Book of Inheritances. It establishes the core list of relatives who always inherit (as long as not excluded by a closer heir) and those who are permanently prevented. Memorizing this list is essential before learning the calculation of shares and the rules of exclusion (hajb).

Guided Path
1
Memorize the ten male inheritors
Recite the list: son, son's son (however low), father, grandfather (however high), brother, brother's son, paternal uncle, paternal uncle's son, the manumitter, and husband. Note that 'however low' means any descendant through males, and 'however high' means any ascendant through males.
This list excludes maternal relatives and uncles from the mother's side.
2
Memorize the seven female inheritors
Recite the list: daughter, son's daughter (however low), mother, grandmother, sister, wife, and the manumitress. Note that 'however low' applies similarly to son's daughter descending through males.
The paternal grandmother is included in 'grandmother'.
3
Identify the four absolute preventers
Learn the four persons who never inherit: the slave (lacks ownership capacity), the killer of the deceased (to prevent reward from crime), the apostate (leaves Islam), and two people of different religions (Muslim and non-Muslim do not inherit from each other).
These are universal impediments, not situational exclusions.
4
Recognize the primary proofs
The main proof is Quran 4:11, which establishes the shares of children. The hadith encouraging learning fara'id (Tirmidhi) shows the importance of this knowledge. Other proofs support the non-inheritance of slaves, killers, and non-Muslims.
These proofs ground the rulings in revelation and practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ. قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - الْمُجْمَعُ عَلَى تَوْرِيثِهِمْ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ عَشَرَةُ: الِابْنُ، وَابْنُ الْابْنِ وَإِنْ سَفَلَ، وَالْأَبُ، وَالْجَدُّ أَبُو الْأَبِ وَإِنْ عَلَا، وَالْأَخُ، وَابْنُ الْأَخِ، وَالْعَمُّ، وَابْنُ الْعَمِّ، وَمَوْلَى النِّعْمَةِ، وَالزَّوْجُ. وَمِنَ الْإِنَاثِ سَبْعَةٌ: الْابْنَةُ، وَبِنْتُ الِابْنِ وَإِنْ سَفَلَتْ، وَالْأُمُّ، وَالْجَدَّةُ، وَالْأُخْتُ، وَالزَّوْجَةُ، وَمَوْلَاةُ النِّعْمَةِ. وَلَا يَرِثُ أَرْبَعَةٌ: الْمَمْلُوكُ، وَالْقَاتِلُ مِنَ الْمَقْتُولِ، وَالْمُرْتَدُّ، وَأَهْلُ الْمِلَّتَيْنِ. وَجْهُ: (١) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ: {يُوصِيكُمُ اللَّهُ فِي أَوْلَادِكُمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ} [النساء: 11]. وَجْهُ: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «تَعَلَّمُوا الْقُرْآنَ وَالْفَرَائِضَ وَعَلِّمُوا النَّاسَ فَإِنِّي مَقْبُوضٌ» (سنن الترمذي، رقم 2091). وَجْهُ: (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: {وَأُولُو الْأَرْحَامِ بَعْضُهُمْ أَوْلَى بِبَعْضٍ فِي كِتَابِ اللهِ} [سورة التوبة: 75]. وَجْهُ: (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ سَالِمِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللهِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «مَنِ ابْتَاعَ نَخْلًا بَعْدَ أَنْ تُؤَبَّرَ فَثَمَرَتُهَا لِلْبَائِعِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشْتَرِطَ الْمُبْتَاعُ، وَمَنِ ابْتَاعَ عَبْدًا وَلَهُ مَالٌ فَمَالُهُ لِلَّذِي بَاعَهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشْتَرِطَ الْمُبْتَاعُ» (صحيح البخاري، رقم 2379). وَجْهُ: (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ: أَنَّ عَلِيًّا، كَانَ يَقُولُ فِي الْمَمْلُوكِينَ وَأَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ: «لَا يَحْجُبُونَ وَلَا يَرِثُونَ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، رقم 31146). وَجْهُ: (٣) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُقَوِّمُ دِيَةَ الْخَطَإِ...
Book of Inheritances. He (al-Quduri) said - may Allah have mercy on him - those unanimously agreed upon to be given inheritance from males are ten: son, son's son however low, father, grandfather (father's father) however high, brother, brother's son, paternal uncle, paternal uncle's son, master of favor (manumitter), husband. And from females are seven: daughter, son's daughter however low, mother, grandmother, sister, wife, and mistress of favor (manumitress). And four do not inherit: the slave, the killer from the killed, the apostate, and those of two different religions. Evidence (1): The verse for proof: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male is like the share of two females' [Quran 4:11]. Evidence (2): The hadith for proof: from Abu Hurayrah, the Prophet said: 'Learn the Quran and the obligations (fara'id) and teach the people, for I am leaving.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 2091). Evidence (3): The hadith for proof: 'But those of kinship are closer to one another in the decree of Allah.' [Quran 9:75]. Evidence (1): The hadith for proof: from Salim ibn Abdullah, from his father, he said: I heard the Prophet say: 'Whoever buys a palm tree after it has been pollinated, its fruit belongs to the seller unless the buyer stipulated it. And whoever buys a slave who has property, his property belongs to the one who sold him unless the buyer stipulated it.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 2379). Evidence (2): The saying of the Companion for proof: Ali used to say about slaves and people of the book: 'They do not prevent (hajb) nor inherit.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 31146). Evidence (3): The hadith for proof: from Amr ibn Shu'ayb, from his father, from his grandfather, he said: The Prophet used to assess the blood money for accidental killing...
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Fara'id (Book of Inheritances) from al-Quduri's matn. It lists the ten male and seven female relatives who always inherit (the 'agreed upon' inheritors) as long as they exist and are not excluded by binding impediments. The ten males are: son, son's son (however low), father, grandfather (however high), brother, brother's son, paternal uncle, paternal uncle's son, the manumitter (mawla al-ni'mah), and husband. The seven females are: daughter, son's daughter (however low), mother, grandmother, sister, wife, and the manumitress (mawlatu al-ni'mah). The passage then lists four persons who never inherit: (1) a slave (because he lacks property ownership capacity), (2) the killer of the deceased (to prevent taking reward from the crime), (3) an apostate (as he leaves the community of Muslims), and (4) two people of different religions (i.e., a Muslim and a non-Muslim do not inherit from each other). The proofs include Quran verses on inheritance (4:11), hadith encouraging learning fara'id, and a hadith about buying palm trees and slaves which is used analogically to show that ownership transfer cuts off inheritance rights. The saying of Ali reinforces that slaves and non-Muslims do not inherit. The last hadith about blood money is incomplete in the OCR but supports the rule that a killer does not inherit.

Key Terms
مَوْلَى النِّعْمَة (mawla al-ni'mah): The manumitter (master who freed a slave); the slave becomes a client, and the manumitter inherits if no other blood relatives.
مَوْلَاةُ النِّعْمَة (mawlatu al-ni'mah): The female manumitress; she inherits from her freed female slave similarly.
أَهْلُ الْمِلَّتَيْنِ (ahl al-millatayn): Two people from different religions; they do not inherit from each other in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT among the ten male inheritors?
A) Brother
B) Son's son
C) Maternal uncle
D) Paternal uncle

Key Takeaway
The list of inheritors is fixed: only ten specific males and seven specific females inherit; four persons are permanently barred.

Faraid — Inheritance
beginner
8 min
Ten Male Heirs and Seven Female Heirs in Hanafi Fara'id
Enumeration of agreed-upon inheritors with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ten male and seven female heirs in Hanafi fara'id and identify which proofs (Quran and hadith) establish this consensus.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school recognizes ten male and seven female heirs whose shares are fixed by divine text and consensus.

In this lesson, we begin the Book of Inheritance (fara'id) from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The text opens with a clear enumeration of the ten male and seven female relatives who inherit by consensus. Understanding this list is foundational for all subsequent inheritance calculations. We will also examine the primary proofs that establish these heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ten male heirs
Memorize the list: son, son's son however low, father, grandfather (father's father) however high, brother, brother's son, paternal uncle, paternal uncle's son, master who freed a slave (mawla al-ni'mah), and husband.
Note that 'however low' refers to any direct male descendant through sons.
2
Identify the seven female heirs
Memorize the list: daughter, son's daughter however low, mother, grandmother, sister, wife, and mistress who freed a female slave (mawla al-ni'mah).
3
Understand the scope of 'however low' and 'however high'
These terms include descendants and ascendants regardless of generation. For example, a great-grandson is included as 'son's son however low'.
4
Review the proofs
The text provides three proofs: Quranic verse (al-Nisa 4:11) about children's shares, a hadith urging learning of Quran and fara'id (Sunan al-Tirmidhi), and Quranic verse (al-Tawbah 9:75) about blood relatives being more entitled.
These proofs establish the consensus on inheritance for these relatives.
5
Distinguish the two types of mawla
Mawla al-ni'mah is the master who freed a slave and inherits from the freed slave if the latter has no heirs. Mawla al-muwalat is one at whose hand a person becomes Muslim and stays with him for life; this category is mentioned in the Urdu notes but not in the main list.
Only mawla al-ni'mah is among the ten male heirs.

كِتَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - الْمُجْمَعُ عَلَى تَوْرِيثِهِمْ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ عَشْرَةٌ: الابْنُ، وَابْنُ الابْنِ وَإِنْ سَفَلَ، وَالْأَبُ، وَالْجَدُّ أَبُو الْأَبِ وَإِنْ عَلَا، وَالْأَخُ، وَابْنُ الْآخِ، وَالْعَمُّ، وَابْنُ الْعَمِّ، وَمَوْلَى النِّعْمَةِ، وَالزَّوْجُ. وَمِنَ الْإِنَاثِ سَبْعٌ: الابْنَةُ، وَابْنَةُ الابْنِ وَإِنْ سَفَلَتْ، وَالْأُمُّ، وَالْجَدَّةُ، وَالْأُخْتُ، وَالزَّوْجَةُ، وَمَوْلَاةُ النِّعْمَةِ. وَلَا يَرِثُ أَرْبَعَةٌ: الْمَمْلُوكُ، وَالْقَاتِلُ مِنَ الْمَقْتُولِ، وَالْمُرْتَدُّ، وَأَهْلُ الْمِلَّتَيْنِ.

وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت الْمُجْمَعُ عَلَى تَوْرِيثِهِمْ: "يُوصِيكُمُ اللَّهُ فِي أَوْلَادِكُمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ فَإِن كُنَّ نِسَاءَ فَوْقَ اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُنَّ ثُلُثَا مَاتَرَكَ" (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 11). وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت الْمُجْمَعُ عَلَى تَوْرِيثِهِمْ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ: عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «تَعَلَّمُوا القُرْآنَ وَالفَرَائِضَ وَعَلِمُوا النَّاسَ فَإِنّى مَقْبُوضٌ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي تعليم الفَرَائِض، نمبر 2091). وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت الْمُجْمَعُ عَلَى تَوْرِيثِهِمْ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ: "وَأُوْلُوا الْأَرْحَامِ بَعْضُهُمْ أَوْلَى بِبَعْضٍ فِي كِتَابِ الله" (سورة التوبة، 8 آيت نمبر 75).

وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَرِثُ أَرْبَعَةٌ الْمَمْلُوكُ وَالْقَاتِلُ مِنَ الْمَقْتُولِ: عَنْ سَالِمِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «مَنِ ابْتَاعَ فَخَلًا بَعْدَ أَنْ تُؤَبَّرَ فَثَمَرَتُهَا لِلْبَائِعِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشْتَرِطَ الْمُبْتَاعُ، وَمَنِ ابْتَاعَ عَبْدًا وَلَهُ مَالٌ فَمَالُهُ لِلَّذِي بَاعَهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشْتَرِطَ الْمُبْتَاعُ» (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يَكُونُ لَهُ مَمَرٌّ أَوْ شِرْبٌ فِي حَائِطِ أَوْ فِي نَخْلِ، نمبر 2379). وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا يَرِثُ أَرْبَعَةُ الْمَمْلُوكُ وَالْقَاتِلُ مِنَ الْمَقْتُولِ: أَنَّ عَلِيًّا، كَانَ يَقُولُ فِي الْمَمْلُوكِينَ وَأَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ: «لَا يَحْجُبُونَ وَلَا يَرِثُونَ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الْمَمْلُوكِ وَأَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ مَنْ قَالَ لا يَحْجُبُونَ وَلا يُوَرَّثُونَ، نمبر 31146). وجه : ((۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَرِثُ أَرْبَعَةُ الْمَمْلُوكُ وَالْقَاتِلُ مِنَ الْمَقْتُولِ: عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُقَوِمُ دِيَةَ الْخَطَ عَلَى أَهْلِ الْقُرَى أَرْبَعَ مِائَةِ دِينَارٍ،

اصول: فرائض کے معنی متعین کرنا، چونکہ اس میں ورثہ کے حصے اللہ نے متعین فرمایا ہے۔ اصول: مولی الموالات: جسکے ہاتھ پر مسلمان ہو ایازندگی بھر ساتھ رہے، مولی العتاقہ : جس نے آزاد کیا۔
Book of Inheritance. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The ten males upon whose inheritance there is consensus are: son, son's son however low, father, grandfather (father's father) however high, brother, brother's son, paternal uncle, paternal uncle's son, master of favor (freed slave), and husband. And seven females: daughter, son's daughter however low, mother, grandmother, sister, wife, and mistress of favor (freed female slave). And four do not inherit: the slave, the murderer from the murdered, the apostate, and the people of two different religions.
Proof (1) the verse for establishing the consensus on their inheritance: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male, what is equal to the share of two females...' (Surah al-Nisa 4:11). Proof (2) the hadith for establishing the consensus on inheritance from males: from Abu Hurairah, the Messenger of Allah said: 'Learn the Quran and the laws of inheritance and teach them to the people, for I am about to be taken.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on teaching inheritance, no. 2091). Proof (3) the hadith for establishing the consensus on inheritance from males: 'But those of [blood] relationship are more entitled [to inheritance] in the decree of Allah.' (Surah al-Tawbah 9:75).
Proof (1) the hadith for establishing that four do not inherit: the slave and the murderer from the murdered: from Salim ibn Abdullah from his father, he heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Whoever buys a palm tree after it has been pollinated, its fruit belongs to the seller unless the buyer stipulates otherwise, and whoever buys a slave who has property, his property belongs to the one who sold him unless the buyer stipulates otherwise.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on a man having a passage or right to water in a garden or palm trees, no. 2379). Proof (2) the statement of a companion for establishing that four do not inherit: the slave and the murderer from the murdered: Ali used to say concerning slaves and People of the Book: 'They do not prevent (others from inheritance) and they do not inherit.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on slaves and People of the Book, no. 31146). Proof (3) the hadith for establishing that four do not inherit: the slave and the murderer from the murdered: from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather: The Messenger of Allah would assess the blood money for accidental killing upon the people of towns as four hundred dinars.
Principle: The meaning of fara'id is to fix (shares), because Allah has fixed the shares of the heirs. Principle: Mawla al-muwalat: one at whose hand a person becomes Muslim and stays with him for life. Mawla al-'itaqah: one who frees (a slave).
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the beginning of the Book of Inheritance in Quduri's Mukhtasar. It opens with a consensus-based enumeration of the ten male and seven female heirs recognized in the Hanafi school. The list includes primary and secondary heirs such as son, grandson, father, grandfather, brother, nephew, uncle, cousin, the master who freed a slave (mawla al-ni'mah), and the husband. Female heirs include daughter, son's daughter, mother, grandmother, sister, wife, and the mistress who freed a female slave. The text then states that four categories of people do not inherit: a slave (due to lack of ownership), a murderer (who killed the deceased), an apostate (who left Islam), and people of two different religions (i.e., Muslim and non-Muslim do not inherit from each other). Following the rulings, the author provides multiple proofs: a Quranic verse establishing inheritance shares for children, a hadith urging learning of Quran and inheritance laws, and another Quranic verse on blood relatives being more entitled. For the non-inheritors, a hadith about ownership of slaves and property, a companion's statement (qawl sahabi) from Ali, and another hadith about blood money are cited. The Urdu marginal notes explain the meaning of fara'id as fixed shares and define mawla al-muwalat (one who helps a person become Muslim) and mawla al-'itaqah (one who frees a slave). This lesson establishes the foundational list of inheritors and the absolute bars to inheritance in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الفرائض (al-fara'id): The fixed shares of inheritance determined by Allah; the science of inheritance law.
مَوْلَى النِّعْمَةِ (mawla al-ni'mah): The master who freed a slave and thus has a right of inheritance from the freed slave if the latter has no heirs.
مَوْلَى الْمُوَالَاةِ (mawla al-muwalat): One at whose hand a person becomes Muslim and stays with him for life; this does not create inheritance rights in Hanafi fara'id.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school enumerates ten male and seven female heirs whose inheritance rights are established by the Quran and Sunnah.

Faraid — Inheritance
beginner
6 min
Four Prevented from Inheritance: Slave, Murderer, Apostate, and People of Two Religions
Enumeration of four prevented categories with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four categories of people who are prevented from inheriting in Hanafi fara'id and explain the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Four categories — slave, murderer, apostate, and people of two different religions — are completely barred from inheritance.

After listing the heirs, al-Quduri states the four categories of people who do not inherit under any circumstances. Each bar has a clear legal basis: lack of ownership, prohibition of benefiting from the crime, loss of faith, and mutual exclusion between religions. We will examine these bars and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the four categories
The four are: slave (mamluk), murderer (qatil), apostate (murtadd), and people of two different religions (ahl al-millatayn).
Ahl al-millatayn refers specifically to the difference of religion between the deceased and the heir.
2
Understand the rationale for each bar
Slave: lacks ownership. Murderer: cannot benefit from his crime. Apostate: leaves the Muslim community. People of two religions: mutual exclusion between Muslim and non-Muslim.
3
Review the proofs for the slave and murderer
The text provides a hadith about the slave's property belonging to the owner (Sahih al-Bukhari), and a companion statement from Ali that slaves and People of the Book 'do not prevent and do not inherit' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah). A third hadith about blood money indirectly supports the bar for the slave.
The hadith about the palm tree and slave is used to derive that a slave cannot own property, hence cannot inherit.
4
Understand the bar for apostate and people of two religions
The apostate is excluded because he has left Islam; the principle is that a Muslim cannot inherit from a non-Muslim and vice versa. The proofs for these are not directly cited in the text but are known from other sources; the text focuses on slave and murderer proofs.
The companion statement from Ali includes 'People of the Book' which covers the two religions bar.
5
Distinguish between mawla al-ni'mah and a slave
A slave is a living human who is owned and cannot own property. Mawla al-ni'mah is a free person who freed a slave and thus inherits from the freed slave. They are opposite categories.

كِتَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - الْمُجْمَعُ عَلَى تَوْرِيثِهِمْ مِنَ الرِّجَالِ عَشْرَةٌ: الابْنُ، وَابْنُ الابْنِ وَإِنْ سَفَلَ، وَالْأَبُ، وَالْجَدُّ أَبُو الْأَبِ وَإِنْ عَلَا، وَالْأَخُ، وَابْنُ الْآخِ، وَالْعَمُّ، وَابْنُ الْعَمِّ، وَمَوْلَى النِّعْمَةِ، وَالزَّوْجُ. وَمِنَ الْإِنَاثِ سَبْعٌ: الابْنَةُ، وَابْنَةُ الابْنِ وَإِنْ سَفَلَتْ، وَالْأُمُّ، وَالْجَدَّةُ، وَالْأُخْتُ، وَالزَّوْجَةُ، وَمَوْلَاةُ النِّعْمَةِ. وَلَا يَرِثُ أَرْبَعَةٌ: الْمَمْلُوكُ، وَالْقَاتِلُ مِنَ الْمَقْتُولِ، وَالْمُرْتَدُّ، وَأَهْلُ الْمِلَّتَيْنِ.

وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَرِثُ أَرْبَعَةٌ الْمَمْلُوكُ وَالْقَاتِلُ مِنَ الْمَقْتُولِ: عَنْ سَالِمِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَقُولُ: «مَنِ ابْتَاعَ فَخَلًا بَعْدَ أَنْ تُؤَبَّرَ فَثَمَرَتُهَا لِلْبَائِعِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشْتَرِطَ الْمُبْتَاعُ، وَمَنِ ابْتَاعَ عَبْدًا وَلَهُ مَالٌ فَمَالُهُ لِلَّذِي بَاعَهُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَشْتَرِطَ الْمُبْتَاعُ» (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ الرَّجُلِ يَكُونُ لَهُ مَمَرٌّ أَوْ شِرْبٌ فِي حَائِطِ أَوْ فِي نَخْلِ، نمبر 2379). وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَا يَرِثُ أَرْبَعَةُ الْمَمْلُوكُ وَالْقَاتِلُ مِنَ الْمَقْتُولِ: أَنَّ عَلِيًّا، كَانَ يَقُولُ فِي الْمَمْلُوكِينَ وَأَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ: «لَا يَحْجُبُونَ وَلَا يَرِثُونَ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي الْمَمْلُوكِ وَأَهْلِ الْكِتَابِ مَنْ قَالَ لا يَحْجُبُونَ وَلا يُوَرَّثُونَ، نمبر 31146). وجه : ((۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَرِثُ أَرْبَعَةُ الْمَمْلُوكُ وَالْقَاتِلُ مِنَ الْمَقْتُولِ: عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُقَوِمُ دِيَةَ الْخَطَ عَلَى أَهْلِ الْقُرَى أَرْبَعَ مِائَةِ دِينَارٍ،

اصول: فرائض کے معنی متعین کرنا، چونکہ اس میں ورثہ کے حصے اللہ نے متعین فرمایا ہے۔ اصول: مولی الموالات: جسکے ہاتھ پر مسلمان ہو ایازندگی بھر ساتھ رہے، مولی العتاقہ : جس نے آزاد کیا۔
Book of Inheritance. He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The ten males upon whose inheritance there is consensus are: son, son's son however low, father, grandfather (father's father) however high, brother, brother's son, paternal uncle, paternal uncle's son, master of favor (freed slave), and husband. And seven females: daughter, son's daughter however low, mother, grandmother, sister, wife, and mistress of favor (freed female slave). And four do not inherit: the slave, the murderer from the murdered, the apostate, and the people of two different religions.
Proof (1) the verse for establishing the consensus on their inheritance: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male, what is equal to the share of two females...' (Surah al-Nisa 4:11). Proof (2) the hadith for establishing the consensus on inheritance from males: from Abu Hurairah, the Messenger of Allah said: 'Learn the Quran and the laws of inheritance and teach them to the people, for I am about to be taken.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on teaching inheritance, no. 2091). Proof (3) the hadith for establishing the consensus on inheritance from males: 'But those of [blood] relationship are more entitled [to inheritance] in the decree of Allah.' (Surah al-Tawbah 9:75).
Proof (1) the hadith for establishing that four do not inherit: the slave and the murderer from the murdered: from Salim ibn Abdullah from his father, he heard the Messenger of Allah say: 'Whoever buys a palm tree after it has been pollinated, its fruit belongs to the seller unless the buyer stipulates otherwise, and whoever buys a slave who has property, his property belongs to the one who sold him unless the buyer stipulates otherwise.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on a man having a passage or right to water in a garden or palm trees, no. 2379). Proof (2) the statement of a companion for establishing that four do not inherit: the slave and the murderer from the murdered: Ali used to say concerning slaves and People of the Book: 'They do not prevent (others from inheritance) and they do not inherit.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on slaves and People of the Book, no. 31146). Proof (3) the hadith for establishing that four do not inherit: the slave and the murderer from the murdered: from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather: The Messenger of Allah would assess the blood money for accidental killing upon the people of towns as four hundred dinars.
Principle: The meaning of fara'id is to fix (shares), because Allah has fixed the shares of the heirs. Principle: Mawla al-muwalat: one at whose hand a person becomes Muslim and stays with him for life. Mawla al-'itaqah: one who frees (a slave).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the beginning of the Book of Inheritance in Quduri's Mukhtasar. It opens with a consensus-based enumeration of the ten male and seven female heirs recognized in the Hanafi school. The list includes primary and secondary heirs such as son, grandson, father, grandfather, brother, nephew, uncle, cousin, the master who freed a slave (mawla al-ni'mah), and the husband. Female heirs include daughter, son's daughter, mother, grandmother, sister, wife, and the mistress who freed a female slave. The text then states that four categories of people do not inherit: a slave (due to lack of ownership), a murderer (who killed the deceased), an apostate (who left Islam), and people of two different religions (i.e., Muslim and non-Muslim do not inherit from each other). Following the rulings, the author provides multiple proofs: a Quranic verse establishing inheritance shares for children, a hadith urging learning of Quran and inheritance laws, and another Quranic verse on blood relatives being more entitled. For the non-inheritors, a hadith about ownership of slaves and property, a companion's statement (qawl sahabi) from Ali, and another hadith about blood money are cited. The Urdu marginal notes explain the meaning of fara'id as fixed shares and define mawla al-muwalat (one who helps a person become Muslim) and mawla al-'itaqah (one who frees a slave). This lesson establishes the foundational list of inheritors and the absolute bars to inheritance in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
مَمْلُوك (mamluk): A slave; a person who is owned by another and lacks legal capacity to own property.
قَاتِل (qatil): A murderer; the killer of the deceased, whether intentional or accidental.
مُرْتَدّ (murtadd): An apostate; a person who has left the religion of Islam.
أَهْلُ الْمِلَّتَيْنِ (ahl al-millatayn): People of two different religions; specifically a Muslim and a non-Muslim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four prevented from inheriting in Hanafi fara'id?
A) Slave
B) Murderer
C) Apostate
D) Adopted son

Key Takeaway
Slaves, murderers, apostates, and people of two religions are completely barred from inheriting in the Hanafi school.

Faraid — Inheritance

The Six Fixed Shares of Inheritance and Their Proofs
Lists the six Quranic fixed shares and provides proofs for inheritance rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six fixed shares in inheritance, cite the Quranic and hadith proofs for them, and identify the barriers to inheritance (murder and religious difference).

Core Idea
Six fixed fractions from the Quran determine inheritance; murder and differing religion block it.

Inheritance in Islam is built on precise fractions revealed in the Quran. This lesson introduces the six fixed shares (al-furud al-mahduda) and the fundamental proofs that establish them. You will also learn crucial barriers that prevent inheritance, such as murder and religious difference, as taught by the Prophet and his Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six fractions
Read the opening statement listing the six shares: half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, and sixth. Memorize these fractions as they form the core of faraid.
These are the only fixed fractions; other shares are residuals.
2
Examine the Quranic proof
The verse from Surah al-Nisa (4:11) is cited as proof. Note how it specifies the shares for daughters, which establishes the concept of fixed fractions.
The verse also includes the rule for sons and daughters (male twice female).
3
Analyze the hadith on murder
The Prophet (peace be upon him) declared that a murderer has no share in the victim's inheritance. This is a barrier (mani) to inheritance.
This rule is universally agreed upon in the Hanafi school.
4
Understand religious difference as a barrier
Two hadiths and a companion practice establish that a Muslim does not inherit from a non-Muslim and vice versa. The evidence is clear and definitive.
This barrier applies to all non-Muslim relatives.
5
Review companion rulings
The rulings of Ali and Mu'adh illustrate how these principles were applied in early Islamic practice. They confirm the fixed shares and the barriers.
Companion rulings (qawl al-sahabi) are a source of Hanafi law when no contrary text exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالْفُرُوضُ الْمَحْدُودَةُ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى سِتَّةُ: النِّصْفُ وَالرُّبْعُ وَالثُّمْنُ وَالثُّلُثَانِ وَالثُّلُثُ وَالسُّدُسُ.

وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَيْسَ لِلْقَاتِل شَيْءٌ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ وَارِثٌ فَوَارِثُهُ أَقْرَبُ النَّاسِ إِلَيْهِ، وَلَا يَرِثُ الْقَاتِلُ شَيْئًا» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ دِيَاتِ الْأَعْضَاءِ، نمبر 4564).

وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَالْفُرُوضُ الْمَحْدُودَةُ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ: "يُوصِيكُمُ اللَّهُ فِي أَوْلَدِكُمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ فَإِن كُنَّ نِسَاءَ فَوْقَ اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُنَّ ثُلُثَا مَا تَرَكَ" (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 11). وجه (۲) الآية لثبوت وَالْفُرُوضُ الْمَحْدُودَةُ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ: "وَمَن يَرْتَدِدْ مِنكُمْ عَن دِينِهِ فَيَمُتْ وَهُوَ كَافِرٌ فَأُولَئِكَ حَبِطَتْ أَعْمَالُهُمْ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالْآخِرَةِ وَأُولَئِكَ أَصْحَابُ النَّارِ هُمْ فِيهَا خَالِدُونَ" (سورة البقرة، 2 آيت نمبر 217). وجه : (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالْفُرُوضُ الْمَحْدُودَةُ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ: عَنْ عَلِيٍّ، أَنَّهُ أَتَى بِمُسْتَوْرِدِ الْعِجْلِي وَقَدِ ارْتَدَّ فَعَرَضَ عَلَيْهِ الْإِسْلَامَ فَأَبَى قَالَ: «فَقَتَلَهُ وَجَعَلَ مِيرَاثَهُ بَيْنَ وَرَثَتِهِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، مَا قَالُوا فِي الْمُرْتَدِ مَا جَاءَ فِي مِيرَاثِهِ، نمبر 32764). وجه : (۴) الحديث لثبوت وَالْفُرُوضُ الْمَحْدُودَةُ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ: عَنْ أُسَامَةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ رضي الله عنهما: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا يَرِثُ الْمُسْلِمُ الْكَافِرَ وَلَا الْكَافِرُ الْمُسْلِمَ» (صحيح البخاري، بَابٌ : لَا يَرِثُ الْمُسْلِمُ الْكَافِرَ وَلَا الْكَافِرُ الْمُسْلِمَ، نمبر 6764). وجه:(۵) الحديث لثبوت وَالْفُرُوضُ الْمَحْدُودَةُ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ: عَنْ جَابِرٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ «لَا يَتَوَارَثُ أَهْلُ مِلَّتَيْنِ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ لَا يَتَوَارَثُ أَهْلُ مِلَّتَيْنِ، نمبر 2108). وجه : (1) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالْفُرُوضُ الْمَحْدُودَةُ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ: عَنِ الْأَسْوَدِ بْنِ يَزِيدَ قَالَ: «أَتَانَا مُعَاذُ بْنُ جَبَلٍ بِالْيَمَنِ مُعَلِّمًا وَأَمِيرًا، فَسَأَلْنَاهُ عَنْ رَجُلٍ: تُوُفِّيَ وَتَرَكَ ابْنَتَهُ وَأُخْتَهُ، فَأَعْطَى الابْنَةَ النِّصْفَ وَالْأُخْتَ النِّصْفَ» (صحيح البخاري بَابُ مِيرَاثِ الْبَنَاتِ، نمبر 6734).

اصول : دو مختلف دین والے ایک دوسرے کے وارث نہیں ہونگے۔
اصول: اگر صرف ایک بیٹی ہو اور کوئی اولاد نہ ہو تو نصف یعنی آدھا ملے گا۔
Book of Inheritance: The fixed shares in the Book of Allah the Exalted are six: half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, and sixth.

And the Messenger of Allah said: 'There is nothing for the murderer, and if there is no heir for him, his heir is the closest people to him, and the murderer does not inherit anything.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on blood money for limbs, no. 4564).

Proof (1) the verse for establishing the fixed shares in the Book of Allah: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children...' (Surah al-Nisa 4:11). Proof (2) the verse for establishing the fixed shares in the Book of Allah: 'And whoever among you turns back from his religion and dies while he is a disbeliever...' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:217). Proof (3) the statement of a companion for establishing the fixed shares in the Book of Allah: from Ali, that he brought Mustawrid al-'Ijli who had apostatized, he presented Islam to him but he refused, so he killed him and made his inheritance among his Muslim heirs (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 32764). Proof (4) the hadith for establishing the fixed shares in the Book of Allah: from Usamah ibn Zayd, the Prophet said: 'The Muslim does not inherit from the disbeliever nor the disbeliever from the Muslim' (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 6764). Proof (5) the hadith for establishing the fixed shares in the Book of Allah: from Jabir, from the Prophet: 'People of two different religions do not inherit from each other' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 2108). Proof (1) the statement of a companion for establishing the fixed shares in the Book of Allah: from al-Aswad ibn Yazid, he said: 'Mu'adh ibn Jabal came to us in Yemen as a teacher and governor. We asked him about a man who died leaving a daughter and a sister; he gave the daughter half and the sister half' (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on inheritance of daughters, no. 6734).

Principle: People of two different religions will not inherit from each other.
Principle: If there is only one daughter and no other children, she gets half.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage continues the Book of Inheritance and lists the six fixed shares (al-furud al-mahduda) that appear in the Quran: half (1/2), quarter (1/4), eighth (1/8), two-thirds (2/3), third (1/3), and sixth (1/6). These are the prescribed fractions that certain heirs receive. The text then quotes a hadith stating that a murderer does not inherit, reinforcing the rule from the previous lesson. Multiple proofs are then provided for the fixed shares and related inheritance rules. These include the Quranic verse on children's shares, a verse on apostasy, a companion's ruling from Ali about an apostate's inheritance going to Muslim heirs, the well-known hadith that Muslim and non-Muslim do not inherit from each other, and another hadith that people of two religions do not inherit mutually. Finally, a companion's practice from Mu'adh ibn Jabal is cited, where he gave half to a daughter and half to a sister when no other heir existed. The Urdu marginal notes reiterate that two different religions prevent inheritance and that a sole daughter receives half. This lesson establishes the six possible fractional shares and reaffirms the barriers to inheritance based on religion and murder.

Key Terms
الفروض المحدودة (al-furud al-mahduda): The six fixed fractional shares prescribed by the Quran for inheritance.
النصف (al-nisf): One-half, the share of a daughter when alone, sister when alone, etc.
القاتل (al-qatil): The murderer, who is barred from inheriting from the victim.
مختلف الدين (mukhtalif al-din): People of different religions; they do not inherit from each other.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many fixed shares are mentioned in the Book of Allah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Four
B) Six
C) Eight
D) Ten

Key Takeaway
The six fixed shares (half, quarter, eighth, two-thirds, third, sixth) are the Quranic basis for inheritance; barriers like murder and religious difference also affect inheritance.

The Five Heirs Who Inherit Half (Nisf)
Lists five heirs of half share with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five heirs who receive the half share and state the condition that activates or blocks their entitlement.

Core Idea
Five specific heirs are entitled to half the estate when certain conditions are met.

The half share (nisf) is one of the six fixed Quranic shares in inheritance. This passage from Al-Quduri names the five heirs who receive half under specific conditions. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correct distribution, as each heir's entitlement depends on the presence or absence of other relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five heirs
Read the matn and list the five categories of heirs who receive the half share. Note that some have conditional status: the son's daughter inherits half only when there is no direct daughter, and the half-sister inherits half only when there is no full sister. The husband's half is conditional on the deceased having no child or son's child.
Memorize these five: daughter, son's daughter, full sister, consanguine sister, husband.
2
Understand the conditions
For each heir, identify the condition that must be met for them to receive half. For example, the daughter gets half if there is no son (to block her from becoming an 'asabah). The husband gets half only if the deceased left no child or son's child.
If the condition is not met, the heir either receives a different share or is excluded.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The passage cites Quran 4:12 which explicitly gives the husband half when his wife dies without children. This verse is the primary evidence for the husband's half. The other half shares are derived from other Quranic verses (e.g., daughter's half in 4:11) and hadith.
The Quranic proof has qat'i thubut (certain transmission) but the dalala (indication) for the other heirs is supported by other texts.
4
Reflect on the companion's statement
Ibn Abbas's statement in Sahih al-Bukhari summarizes the inheritance system after abrogation, confirming the half share for the husband and implying the shares for others. This hadith reinforces the practice of the early community.
This is a mawquf hadith (statement of a companion) used as support, not as primary proof.
5
Apply to a scenario
Consider a deceased woman who leaves a husband, a daughter, and no other heirs. The husband gets half (since no child), and the daughter gets half. If there were also a son, the husband would get only a quarter and the children would divide the remainder as 'asabah.
The half share can change: the husband's half becomes a quarter if a child exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَالنِّصْفُ فَرْضُ خَمْسَةِ الِابْنَةُ وَابْنَةُ الابْنِ إِذَا لَمْ تَكُنْ ابْنَةُ الصُّلْبِ وَالْأُخْتُ لِلْأَبِ وَلِلْأُمّ وَالْأُحْتُ لِلْآبِ إِذَا لَمْ تَكُنْ أُخْتٌ لِأَبِ وَأُمَ وَالزَّوْجُ إذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْمَيِّتِ وَلَدٌ وَلَا وَلَدُ ابْنِ. وجه: (۱) الآية لثبوت فَالنِّصْفُ فَرْضُ خَمْسَةِ الِابْنَةُ وَابْنَةُ الابْنِ ﴿وَلَكُمْ نِصْفُ مَا تَرَكَ أَزْوَاجُكُمْ إِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُنَّ وَلَدٌ فَإِن كَانَ لَهُنَّ وَلَدٌ فَلَكُمُ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْنَ مِنْ بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِينَ بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ وَلَهُنَّ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْتُمْ إِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّكُمْ وَلَدٌ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 أيت نمبر 12). وجه: (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت فَالنِّصْفُ فَرْضُ خَمْسَةِ الاِبْنَةُ وَابْنَةُ الْابْنِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «كَانَ الْمَالُ لِلْوَلَدِ، وَكَانَتِ الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ، فَنَسَخَ اللَّهُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مَا أَحَبَّ، فَجَعَلَ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلَ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ، وَجَعَلَ لِلْأَبَوَيْنِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ، وَجَعَلَ لِلْمَرْأَةِ الثُّمُنَ وَالرُّبُعَ، وَلِلزَّوْجِ الشَّطْرَ وَالرُّبُعَ.» (صحيح البخاري بَابُ مِيرَاثِ الزَّوْجِ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ وَغَيْرِهِ، نمبر 6739)
The half is the prescribed share of five: the daughter, the son's daughter when there is no direct daughter, the full sister (for both parents), the half-sister (for father) when there is no full sister, and the husband when the deceased has no child or son's child. Proof (1): The verse for establishing the half as prescribed share of five: the daughter and son's daughter [Surah An-Nisa 4:12]. Proof (2): Saying of a companion establishing the half as prescribed share of five: the daughter and son's daughter - from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them both) who said: 'The wealth used to be for the child, and the bequest was for the parents, then Allah abrogated what He wished, and made for the male the share of two females, and made for the parents each one-sixth, and made for the woman one-eighth and one-quarter, and for the husband half and quarter.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter on inheritance of husband with child and others, no. 6739)
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from Al-Quduri's Faraid. The matn lists the five heirs who receive a half share: daughter, son's daughter (in absence of daughter), full sister, consanguine half-sister (in absence of full sister), and husband (when no child or descendant). The commentator then provides two proofs: first, the Quranic verse (4:12) which specifies the half for the husband when there is no child, and similarly the other half shares are derived from context and other verses. Second, a hadith from Ibn Abbas showing that the Prophet (peace be upon him) established these shares as part of the inheritance system. Note that the half for the husband is conditional upon no children or sons' children; otherwise he gets a quarter.

Key Terms
نصف (nisf): The share of half the estate, prescribed for specific heirs.
ابنة الابن (ibnat al-ibn): Son's daughter; inherits half when there is no direct daughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following heirs receives half of the estate under the condition stated in the passage?
A) Wife when no children
B) Husband when no children
C) Mother when no children
D) Full brother when no siblings

Key Takeaway
The half share is prescribed for five specific heirs under well-defined conditions; these are fixed Quranic shares.

Quarter and Eighth Shares for Spouses: Rulings and Proofs
States spousal shares with child condition and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the husband's and wives' prescribed shares in inheritance based on the presence of children, and identify the Quranic proof for each.

Core Idea
Spousal shares shift between half and quarter for husbands, and between quarter and eighth for wives, depending on children.

In this lesson, we examine the prescribed shares (fard) for spouses in Islamic inheritance. The Qur'an explicitly sets the husband's share at one-quarter when the deceased wife leaves a child, and the wife's share at one-eighth when the husband leaves a child. Without children, the husband takes half (covered in a previous lesson) and wives take one-quarter. These rulings are universally agreed upon across schools of thought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the spouse and presence of a child
Determine whether the deceased left behind a child (or son's child). This condition triggers the specific share.
Child includes both son and daughter, and also the son's child (grandchild) in place of the son.
2
Apply the share from the matn
For the husband: if there is a child, he gets one-quarter. For the wife/wives: if there is no child, they get one-quarter; if there is a child, they get one-eighth.
The husband's share without child is one-half, taught in a separate lesson.
3
Confirm with the Quranic proof
Recite the verse from Surah An-Nisa 4:12 which explicitly states these shares and the condition of having a child.
The verse is qati' al-thubut and qati' al-dalalah, so there is no ikhtilaf on these shares.
4
Note the cross-madhhab consensus
All four madhahib agree on these spousal shares; they are from the clear text of the Quran.
This is a rare case of complete agreement (ijma' 'amali) in faraid.

وَالرُّبْعُ فَرْضٌ لِلزَّوْجِ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ وَلِلزَّوْجَاتِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْمَيِّتِ وَلَدٌ وَلَا وَلَدُ ابْنِ. وَالتَّمْنُ لِلزَّوْجَاتِ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ. وجه: (۱) الآية لثبوت وَالرُّبْعُ فَرْضٌ لِلزَّوْجِ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ ﴿فَإِن كَانَ لَهُنَّ وَلَدٌ فَلَكُمُ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْنَ مِنْ بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِينَ بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ وَلَهُنَّ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْتُمْ إِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّكُمْ وَلَدٌ فَإِن كَانَ لَكُمْ وَلَدٌ فَلَهُنَّ الثَّمُنُ مِمَّا تَرَكْتُم مِّنْ بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ تُوصُونَ بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنِ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 أيت نمبر 12). وجه: (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالرُّبْعُ فَرْضٌ لِلزَّوْجِ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما قَالَ: «كَانَ الْمَالُ لِلْوَلَدِ، وَكَانَتِ الْوَصِيَّةُ لِلْوَالِدَيْنِ، فَنَسَخَ اللهُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مَا أَحَبَّ، فَجَعَلَ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلَ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ، وَجَعَلَ لِلْأَبَوَيْنِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ، وَجَعَلَ لِلْمَرْأَةِ الثُّمُنَ وَالرُّبُعَ، وَلِلزَّوْجِ الشَّطْرَ وَالرُّبُعَ.» (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ الزَّوْجِ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ وَغَيْرِهِ، نمبر 6739)
And the quarter is a prescribed share for the husband with a child or son's child, and for wives when the deceased has no child or son's child. And the eighth is for wives with a child or son's child. Proof (1): The verse for establishing the quarter as prescribed share for the husband with child: [Surah An-Nisa 4:12]. Proof (2): Saying of a companion establishing the quarter as prescribed share for the husband with child: from Ibn Abbas...
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage continues the faraid rulings, covering the shares of spouses. The matn states: the husband gets one-quarter if the deceased wife leaves a child or son's child; wives get one-quarter if the husband dies without children; and wives get one-eighth if the husband leaves children. The commentator provides the same Quranic verse (4:12) which explicitly states these shares, and the same hadith of Ibn Abbas. Note that the husband's share when there is no child is half (covered in previous lesson), and here when there is child it is quarter. For wives, the Quran alternates between quarter (no child) and eighth (with child). All these are established by clear texts.

Key Terms
ربع (rub'): One-quarter share.
ثمن (thumn): One-eighth share.

Key Takeaway
Spousal shares in inheritance are explicitly fixed by the Quran: husband gets quarter with child, wives get quarter without child and eighth with child.

Two-Thirds and One-Third Shares
States two-thirds for multiple half-share heirs and one-third for mother under conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two-thirds share rule for multiple half-share heirs and identify the conditions for the mother to receive one-third instead of one-sixth.

Core Idea
Two or more half-share heirs collectively receive two-thirds; the mother gets one-third only when no children or two siblings block her.

In inheritance (faraid), certain shares are fixed by the Quran. This passage explains two key rules: the two-thirds share, which applies when there are two or more heirs whose individual share would be half (e.g., two daughters, two sisters), and the one-third share for the mother under specific conditions. The exception for the husband (who never takes two-thirds even if multiple) is also noted. The proofs come directly from the Quran and the practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rules
The passage states two rules: (1) two-thirds for every two or more of those whose fard is half (except the husband), and (2) one-third for the mother when the deceased has no child or son's child and no two siblings (brothers/sisters).
The 'half-share heirs' include daughter, full sister, consanguine sister, son's daughter; the husband's share is half individually but he never gets two-thirds.
2
Understand the condition for the mother
The mother receives one-third only if there is no child (son or daughter) and no two or more siblings. If either exists, her share drops to one-sixth (Quran 4:11).
'Child' includes son's child (grandchild). 'Two brothers or sisters' means two or more siblings, regardless of gender, but they exclude the existence of children.
3
Examine the dalil for two-thirds
The author presents three proofs: (a) Quran 4:11 for daughters, (b) the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (via Bukhari) extending the rule to son's daughter and sister, and (c) Quran 4:176 for sisters (kalalah). These establish that any group of two or more half-share heirs (except husband) takes two-thirds.
The analogical extension from daughters to other half-share heirs is through qiyas.
4
Examine the dalil for the mother's one-third
Quran 4:11 is the proof: the mother gets one-third if no child, but if the deceased has siblings, she gets one-sixth. The condition of 'no two siblings' arises from the interpretation that when siblings are present, they block the higher share (hajb nuqsan).
The number 'two' is derived from the text; one sibling does not reduce the mother's share.
5
Apply the rules to a scenario
Consider a deceased woman leaving a husband, a mother, and a brother. The mother gets one-third? No, because there is at least one sibling (but not two). Actually, one sibling does not block; the mother gets one-third if no two siblings. So with one brother, mother gets one-third (provided no children). However, the husband takes half, so the remainder is half, which is one-third of the estate? Wait, careful: the husband's share is half, mother's share is one-third of the whole estate? Actually, shares are fractions of the whole. So calculation: husband 1/2, mother 1/3, the residue goes to the brother as asabah. But the denominator: LCM of 2 and 3 is 6. Husband 3/6, mother 2/6, brother 1/6.
This step shows how the rules combine in practice.

وَالثُّلُثَانِ لِكُلِّ اثْنَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا مِمَّنْ فَرْضُهُ النِّصْفُ إِلَّا الزَّوْجَ فِي. وَالقُلْتُ لِلْأُمَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْمَيِّتِ وَلَدٌ وَلَا وَلَدُ ابْن وَلَا اثْنَانِ مِنْ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ. وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت وَالثُّلُتَانِ لِكُلِ اثْنَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا ﴿فَإِن كُنَّ نِسَاءَ فَوْقَ اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُنَّ ثُلُنَا مَا تَرَكَ وَإِن كَانَتْ وَاحِدَةً فَلَهَا النِّصْفُ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 أيت نمبر 11). وجه (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت والظُّلُتَانِ لِكُلِ اثْنَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا «سُئِلَ أَبُو مُوسَى عَنِ ابْنَةٍ وَابْنَةِ ابْنِ وَأُخْتِ، فَقَالَ: لِلابْنَةِ النِّصْفُ، وَلِلْأُخْتِ النِّصْفُ، وَأتِ ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ فَسَيُتَابِعُنِي، فَسُئِلَ ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ، وَأُخْبِرَ بِقَوْلِ أَبِي مُوسَى فَقَالَ: لَقَدْ ضَلَلْتُ إِذَا وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ الْمُهْتَدِينَ، أَقْضِي فِيهَا بِمَا قَضَى النَّبِيُّ : لِلابْنَةِ النِّصْفُ، وَلابْنَةِ ابْنِ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةَ الثَّلُثَيْنِ، وَمَا بَقِيَ فَلِلْأُخْتِ» (صحيح البخاري بَابُ مِيرَاثِ ابْنَةِ ابْنِ مَعَ ابْنَةٍ، نمبر 6736). وجه : (۳) الآية لثبوت وَالظُّلُتَانِ لِكُلِ اثْنَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا ﴿يَسْتَفْتُونَكَ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِي الْكَلَالَةِ إِنِ امْرُؤٌاً هَلَكَ لَيْسَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ وَلَهُ أُخْتٌ فَلَهَا نِصْفُ مَا تَرَكَ وَهُوَ يَرِثُهَا إِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهَا وَلَدٌ فَإِن كَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُمَا الظُّلُتَانِ مِمَّا تَرَكَ وَإِن كَانُوا إِخْوَةَ رِجَالًا وَنِسَآءَ فَلِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 176). وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَالقُلتُ لِلْأُمَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْمَيِّتِ ﴿وَلِأَبَوَيْهِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ مِمَّا تَرَكَ إِن كَانَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُ وَلَدٌ وَوَرِثَهُ أَبَوَاهُ فَلِأُمِّهِ الثُّلُثُ فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 11)
And the two-thirds is for every two or more of those whose prescribed share is half, except the husband in [a special case]. And the one-third is for the mother when the deceased has no child or son's child and no two brothers or sisters. Proof (1): The verse for establishing two-thirds for every two or more [Surah An-Nisa 4:11]. Proof (2): Saying of a companion for establishing two-thirds for every two or more: Abu Musa was asked about a daughter, a son's daughter, and a sister... and Ibn Mas'ud said: 'I would not be guided, I judge in it as the Prophet judged: for the daughter half, for the son's daughter one-sixth to complete two-thirds, and what remains is for the sister.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 6736). Proof (3): The verse for establishing two-thirds for every two or more [Surah An-Nisa 4:176]. Proof (1) for establishing the one-third for the mother when the deceased has no child [Surah An-Nisa 4:11].

Commentary
This passage covers two rules: two-thirds share applies when there are two or more heirs whose individual share would be half (e.g., two daughters, two full sisters, etc.), except the husband (who does not get two-thirds even if multiple). The mother gets one-third when there is no child or son's child and no two siblings (brothers or sisters) to block her from the higher share; otherwise she gets one-sixth. The commentator provides three proofs for the two-thirds rule: Quran 4:11 (daughters get two-thirds if more than two), the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud establishing that two daughters get two-thirds (via daughter and son's daughter), and Quran 4:176 (sisters get two-thirds if two). For the mother's one-third, the proof is Quran 4:11 which says mother gets one-third if no child, but if there are siblings she gets one-sixth. Note the exception for 'husband in' - it says 'except the husband in' but the text is cut; it means the husband does not get two-thirds even if multiple husbands (impossible) or in the case of two wives? Actually the phrase 'إلا الزوج في' likely means except the husband in the case of wives? But the matn is unclear. Usually the rule is: those whose individual share is half (e.g., daughter, sister) when two or more, they get two-thirds, but the husband's share is half individually, but when there are multiple husbands? There is only one husband. So the exception may refer to a situation where the husband is among multiple half-share heirs? But it's not applicable. The commentator does not elaborate. We'll note the text.

Key Terms
ثلثان (thuluthan): Two-thirds share, applicable to multiple half-share heirs.
ثلث (thuluth): One-third share, specifically for mother under conditions.
نصف (nisf): Half share, which is the individual fard of certain heirs (e.g., daughter, sister) that becomes two-thirds when grouped.
