The Collective Two-Thirds Share for Multiple Half-Share Heirs
States a faraid rule with proofs from Quran and Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that two or more female heirs with a prescribed half-share inherit two-thirds collectively, identify the heirs to whom this applies, and explain the exception of the husband.

Core Idea
Two or more heirs whose fard is half collectively inherit two-thirds, not half each.

In the Book of Inheritance, al-Quduri states a key rule: any heir whose fixed Quranic share is half, when there are two or more of them, they share two-thirds. This lesson unpacks the rule, its evidence from Quran and Sunnah, and its exception — the husband. Understanding this rule is essential for correctly distributing shares in cases involving multiple daughters, granddaughters, or sisters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs with a prescribed half-share
List the heirs whose fard is half: daughter, son's daughter, full sister, consanguine sister. The husband also has a half-share but is excluded from this rule.
The husband's half applies only when there is no child, but he never gets two-thirds.
2
State the collective rule
When two or more of these heirs exist, they collectively receive two-thirds of the estate, not half each. For example, two daughters receive two-thirds together, not one-half each.
This rule applies only when there is no asabah (like a son) to change their status.
3
Note the exception: the husband
The husband is explicitly excluded from this rule. Even if there are two or more husbands (impossible in Islam), the husband's share never reaches two-thirds.
The husband's share is either half or one-fourth, never two-thirds.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
First proof: Quran 4:11 gives two-thirds to 'women more than two' (daughters). Second proof: Quran 4:176 gives two-thirds to 'two sisters'. Both verses establish the two-thirds share for multiple female heirs.
The general principle is derived from these specific cases and extended by scholarly consensus.
5
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and Abu Musa (narrated by Bukhari) shows the ruling for a daughter, son's daughter, and sister: the daughter gets half, son's daughter gets one-sixth (completing two-thirds), and sister gets the remainder. This demonstrates that the two-thirds limit applies to the combination of such heirs.
The hadith confirms that when multiple female heirs co-exist, their collective share does not exceed two-thirds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالثُّلُثَانِ لِكُلِّ اثْنَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا مِمَّنْ فَرْضُهُ النِّصْفُ إِلَّا الزَّوْجَ. الدَّلِيلُ: قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {فَإِن كُنَّ نِسَاء فَوْقَ اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُنَّ ثُلُثَا مَا تَرَكَ} [النِّسَاءِ: 11]. وَعَنْ أَبِي مُوسَى وَابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: فِي ابْنَةٍ وَابْنَةِ ابْنٍ وَأُخْتٍ، قَالَ: لِلابْنَةِ النِّصْفُ، وَلابْنَةِ الابْنِ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةَ الثُّلُثَيْنِ، وَمَا بَقِيَ فَلِلأُخْتِ. رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ. وَقَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {فَإِن كَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُمَا الثُّلُثَانِ} [النِّسَاءِ: 176].
And two-thirds for every two or more from those whose prescribed share is half, except the husband. The evidence: His statement the Exalted: 'If there are women more than two, then for them two-thirds of what he left' [Quran 4:11]. And from Abu Musa and Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with them, concerning a daughter, a son's daughter, and a sister: 'For the daughter half, for the son's daughter one-sixth completing two-thirds, and what remains is for the sister.' Narrated by al-Bukhari. And His statement the Exalted: 'If they are two, then for them two-thirds' [Quran 4:176].
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Book of Inheritance. The rule: any heir whose normal prescribed share (fard) is half—such as a daughter, son's daughter, full sister, or consanguine sister—when there are two or more of them, collectively inherit two-thirds instead of half each. The husband is excluded because his share is never two-thirds. The first proof is Quran 4:11, which explicitly gives two-thirds to more than two daughters. The second proof is the famous hadith of Ibn Mas'ud and Abu Musa, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) ruled for a case involving a daughter, a son's daughter, and a sister: the daughter gets half, the son's daughter gets one-sixth to complete two-thirds, and the sister gets the remainder. This shows that the two-thirds limit applies to the combination of daughters and son's daughters. The third proof is Quran 4:176, which gives two-thirds to two sisters. Thus, the rule is established for all female heirs with half-share except the husband.

Key Terms
الثلثان (al-thuluthān): The prescribed share of two-thirds for two or more female heirs whose original fard is half.
فرضه النصف (farduhu al-nisf): Heirs whose Quranic share is half: daughter, son's daughter, full sister, consanguine sister.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half for each daughter
B) Two-thirds collectively
C) One-third collectively
D) The whole estate

Key Takeaway
The collective two-thirds share for two or more heirs with half-share is a fixed Quranic rule, confirmed by Sunnah, with no dispute among schools.

Mother's Share: One-Sixth, One-Third, and One-Third of Remainder
Explains mother's inheritance share under different circumstances including two exceptional cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the mother's inheritance share in three scenarios: with children/siblings, without, and in the two exceptional spouse+parents cases, applying the correct fraction and citing the evidence.

Core Idea
Mother's share: one-sixth with children or two siblings, one-third otherwise, or one-third of remainder after spouse.

The mother's inheritance share is one of the fixed Quranic portions, but its exact fraction changes based on the presence of other heirs. Understanding the conditions—children, siblings, or the unique spouse+parents situation—is essential for correct distribution. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories
The mother's share depends on three scenarios: (1) deceased has a child or son's child, or two or more siblings; (2) deceased has none of these; (3) deceased has a spouse and both parents (two exceptional cases).
Siblings include full, consanguine, and uterine, as long as there are at least two.
2
Apply the share fractions
In scenario 1: one-sixth. In scenario 2: one-third of the total estate. In scenario 3: one-third of what remains after the spouse's share (half for husband, quarter for wife).
The exceptional cases are: husband + parents, or wife + parents.
3
Examine the evidence
The Quranic verse (4:11) provides the one-sixth rule when siblings exist. The two exceptional cases are based on the practice of Zayd ibn Thabit and Umar (may Allah be pleased with them).
This is a case where Companion practice supplements the primary text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلِلْأُمِّ السُّدُسُ إِذَا كَانَ لِلْمَيِّتِ وَلَدٌ أَوْ وَلَدُ ابْنٍ، أَوِ اثْنَانِ مِنَ الْإِخْوَةِ فَصَاعِدًا. فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ وَلَدٌ وَلَا وَلَدُ ابْنٍ وَلَا اثْنَانِ مِنَ الْإِخْوَةِ فَلِلْأُمِّ الثُّلُثُ. وَيَفْرِضُ لَهَا فِي مَسْأَلَتَيْنِ ثُلُثَ مَا بَقِيَ: زَوْجٌ وَأَبَوَانِ، أَوْ زَوْجَةٌ وَأَبَوَانِ، فَلِلْأُمِّ ثُلُثُ مَا بَقِيَ بَعْدَ فَرْضِ الزَّوْجِ أَوِ الزَّوْجَةِ. الدَّلِيلُ: قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ} [النِّسَاءِ: 11]. وَعَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ وَعُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا فِي الْأُمِّ مَعَ الزَّوْجِ وَالْأَبَوَيْنِ: لِلزَّوْجِ النِّصْفُ، وَلِلْأُمِّ ثُلُثُ مَا بَقِيَ، وَلِلْأَبِ الْبَاقِي.
And for the mother: one-sixth if the deceased has a child or a son's child, or two or more siblings. If he does not have a child nor a son's child nor two siblings, then for the mother one-third. And he prescribes for her in two cases one-third of what remains: a husband and parents, or a wife and parents, so for the mother one-third of what remains after the share of the husband or wife. The evidence: His statement the Exalted: 'If he has siblings, for his mother one-sixth' [Quran 4:11]. And from Zayd ibn Thabit and 'Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, concerning the mother with the husband and parents: for the husband half, for the mother one-third of what remains, and for the father the rest.
Source pages p. 436

Commentary
This passage details the mother's inheritance. She receives one-sixth if the deceased has a child (son or daughter) or a son's child (grandchild through son), or if there are two or more siblings (full, consanguine, or uterine, at least two). If none of these exist, she gets one-third of the entire estate. However, in two exceptional cases, she gets one-third of the remainder after the spouse's share: (1) when the heirs are a husband and both parents, and (2) when they are a wife and both parents. In both cases, the father also inherits, and the mother's share is one-third of what remains after the spouse's fard. The proof is Quran 4:11, which mentions one-sixth when siblings exist, and the practice of the Companions Zayd ibn Thabit and 'Umar for the two exceptional cases. This is an established ruling in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
ثلث ما بقي (thuluth ma baqiya): One-third of the remainder after the spouse's share, in the two exceptional cases.
إخوة (ikhwah): Siblings of any type (full, consanguine, uterine) who reduce mother's share when two or more.
السدس (al-sudus): One-sixth: the mother's share when there are children or two siblings.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third: the mother's share when no children or two siblings exist, but not in the exceptional spouse+parents cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased leaves a husband, mother, and father. What is the mother's share?
A) One-sixth
B) One-third of the total estate
C) One-third of the remainder after the husband's share
D) One-fourth

Key Takeaway
Mother's share is one-sixth with children or two siblings, one-third otherwise, and one-third of remainder in the two exceptional spouse+parent cases.

Uterine Siblings' Shares: One-Sixth and One-Third
States the shares of uterine siblings with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Quranic shares for uterine siblings and apply the rule of equal distribution among them.

Core Idea
Uterine siblings share equally in one-third when multiple, regardless of gender.

This lesson covers the fixed shares of uterine siblings (half-siblings sharing only the mother) as established by Quran 4:12. Unlike full or consanguine siblings, uterine siblings do not follow the male-double rule; instead, all share equally. We will examine the Quranic evidence and the practical application of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their relationship
Uterine siblings are those who share only the mother with the deceased. They are distinct from full or consanguine siblings.
They are also called 'walad al-umm'.
2
State the share for a single uterine sibling
If there is only one uterine brother or sister, the share is one-sixth of the estate.
The Quran explicitly says 'for each one of them one-sixth'.
3
State the share for multiple uterine siblings
If there are two or more uterine siblings, they collectively inherit one-third of the estate, divided equally among them.
The Quran terms them 'partners in one-third'.
4
Note the equal distribution rule
Males and females receive equal shares. This differs from full and consanguine siblings where males take double.
The evidence is the word 'partners' implying equality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلِوَلَدِ الْأُمِّ: لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ، فَإِنْ كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلُثِ، ذُكُورُهُمْ وَإِنَاثُهُمْ فِيهِ سَوَاءٌ. الدَّلِيلُ: قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {وَإِن كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلَالَةً أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ وَلَهُ أَخٌ أَوْ أُخْتٌ فَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ فَإِن كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلُثِ} [النِّسَاءِ: 12]. وَعَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ نَحْوُهُ.
And for children of the mother: for each one of them one-sixth, if they are more than that then they are partners in one-third, their males and females are equal therein. The evidence: His statement the Exalted: 'If a man is inherited as a kalala or a woman, and he has a brother or a sister, for each one of them one-sixth; if they are more than that, then they are partners in one-third' [Quran 4:12]. And from Zayd ibn Thabit similar to it.
Source pages p. 437

Commentary
This passage covers the inheritance of uterine siblings (those sharing only the mother). For a single uterine brother or sister, the share is one-sixth. If there are two or more, they collectively share one-third, divided equally among them regardless of gender—males and females receive the same amount. This is based on Quran 4:12, which explicitly gives one-sixth to one sibling and one-third to multiple siblings as partners, with no distinction between male and female. The practice of the Companion Zayd ibn Thabit confirms this. Uterine siblings are excluded by the presence of a child or a son's child, or by the father or grandfather.

Key Terms
ولد الأم (walad al-umm): Uterine siblings: half-siblings who share only the mother with the deceased.
شركاء في الثلث (shurakā' fī al-thuluth): They are partners in one-third, sharing equally among themselves.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The whole estate

Key Takeaway
Uterine siblings inherit one-sixth if one, and share one-third equally if two or more, regardless of gender.

The Sixth as a Share for Seven Categories
Ruling on the sixth share for seven categories of heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven categories of heirs entitled to the sixth share and apply the conditions under which each receives it.

Core Idea
Sixth is prescribed for parents with child, mother with siblings, and grandfather with child — all from Quran and Sunnah.

In inheritance law, certain shares are fixed by divine decree. One such share is the sixth, which applies to seven distinct categories of heirs. Understanding these categories and their conditions is essential for correct distribution. This lesson clarifies who inherits a sixth and under what circumstances, drawing directly from the Quran and the authoritative practice of the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven categories
List the seven heirs mentioned: father (with child/grandchild), mother (with child/grandchild), mother (with siblings), grandfather (with child/grandchild), and the four cases of uterine siblings? Actually careful: The text says 'فرض سبعة' and enumerates: each parent when there is a child or grandchild (that's two), mother with siblings (one), grandfather with child or grandchild (one). That makes four categories. But it says seven; perhaps it counts each parent separately and the mother with siblings as separate, and then the four? Actually the original Arabic from the source: 'والسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْأَبَوَيْنِ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ، وَهُوَ لِلْأُمِّ مَعَ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ، وَلِلْجَدِّ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ'. That lists: father (1), mother (2) — both with child/grandchild — mother with siblings (3), grandfather with child/grandchild (4). That's four. But then it says 'سبعة'? Possibly it includes the four cases plus the three cases of the mother? Actually in classical faraid, the seven are: father, mother, grandfather, mother with siblings, and then the three? Wait, more common list: the six categories that receive the sixth are: father (when child exists), mother (when child exists), mother (when siblings exist), grandfather (when child exists), grandmother (when no mother), and the maternal siblings? Actually the text says 'سبعة' but only lists four. Possibly it counts the father (1), mother (2), mother with siblings (3), grandfather (4) and then the three? That doesn't add up. Let's check: In Hanafi faraid, the recipients of the sixth are: 1. father (with child), 2. mother (with child), 3. mother (with siblings), 4. grandfather (with child), 5. grandmother (when father is not inheriting), 6. maternal uterine siblings (if they are two or more they get a third, not a sixth; so not sixth). Hmm. Actually the common list in Hanafi texts: the sixth is for seven: 1. father, 2. mother, 3. grandfather (when no father), 4. grandmother, 5. mother's mother, 6. uterine siblings, and 7. others? Let's stick with what the passage says: it explicitly says 'سبعة' but only mentions four cases. Perhaps it includes the two parents separately and the mother with siblings as two? But the source might have omitted the rest. Given the ambiguity, we'll guide the student to identify the four explicitly mentioned and note that there are more in the school. However, for the lesson, we focus on the mentioned ones.
The text mentions four cases: father, mother (each with child/grandchild), mother (with siblings), and grandfather (with child/grandchild).
2
Understand the conditions for each
For each heir, note the specific condition: father and mother receive a sixth only if the deceased left a child or a son's child (grandchild). Mother receives a sixth if siblings of the deceased exist. Grandfather receives a sixth if the deceased left a child or son's child.
The grandfather's share is specific to the Hanafi school; others may differ.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The Quran 4:11 explicitly states: 'And for his parents, for each of them, a sixth of what he left if he has a child; ... if he has siblings, then for his mother a sixth.' This provides direct textual evidence for the mother's and father's shares.
The verse is clear (qati' al-dalala) on these shares.
4
Consider the companion's statement
The passage cites Zayd ibn Thabit's interpretation, which reaffirms the conditions. This demonstrates the early application and consensus among the Companions.
Zayd ibn Thabit was a prominent authority on inheritance.
5
Apply the ruling to a hypothetical
Example: A deceased leaves a daughter and both parents. Since there is a child, both parents get a sixth. If the deceased leaves two siblings and a mother but no child, the mother gets a sixth (because of siblings) and the siblings (uterine) share one-third equally.
Ensure correct application of conditions.

كِتَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ
وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْأَبَوَيْنِ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ، وَهُوَ لِلْأُمِّ مَعَ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ، وَلِلْجَدِّ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ، ذَلِكَ يُفْرَضُ لِلْوَاحِدِ مِنْهُمُ السُّدُسَ ذَكَرًا كَانَ أَوْ أُنْثَى، فَإِنْ كَانُوا اثْنَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا ذُكُورًا أَوْ إِنَاثًا فُرِضَ لَهُمُ الثُّلُثُ يَقْتَسِمُونَهُ بِالسَّوَاءِ (السُنن الكبرى للبيهقي، باب فرض الإخوة والأخوات للأم، رقم 12324)
وَجْهٌ: (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْأَبَوَيْنِ... ﴿وَلِأَبَوَيْهِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ مِمَّا تَرَكَ إِن كَانَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُ وَلَدٌ وَوَرِثَهُ أَبَوَاهُ فَلِأُمِّهِ الثُّلُثُ فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ﴾ (سُورَةُ النِّسَاءِ، 4، آيَة 11)
وَجْهٌ: (2) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْأَبَوَيْنِ... عَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ، وَأَمَّا التَّفْسِيرُ فَتَفْسِيرُ أَبِي الزَّنَادِ عَلَى مَعَانِي زَيْدٍ قَالَ: "وَمِيرَاثُ الْأُمِّ مِنْ وَلَدِهَا إِذَا تُوُفِّيَ ابْنُهَا وَابْنَتُهَا فَتَرَكَ وَلَدًا أَوْ وَلَدَ ابْنٍ ذَكَرًا أَوْ أُنْثَى، أَوْ تَرَكَ الاثْنَيْنِ مِنَ الْإِخْوَةِ فَصَاعِدًا ذُكُورًا أَوْ إِنَاثًا مِنْ أَبٍ وَأُمٍّ، أَوْ مِنْ أَبٍ، أَوْ مِنْ أُمٍّ السُّدُسُ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَتْرُكِ الْمُتَوَفَّى وَلَدًا وَلَا وَلَدَ ابْنٍ وَلَا اثْنَيْنِ مِنَ الْإِخْوَةِ فَصَاعِدًا فَإِنَّ لِلْأُمِّ الثُّلُثَ كَامِلًا، إِلَّا فِي فَرِيضَتَيْنِ فَقَطْ وَهُمَا أَنْ يُتَوَفَّى رَجُلٌ وَيَتْرُكَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَأَبَوَيْهِ، فَيَكُونَ لِامْرَأَتِهِ الرُّبُعُ، وَلِأُمِّهِ الثُّلُثُ مِمَّا بَقِيَ، وَهُوَ الرُّبُعُ مِنْ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ، وَإِنْ تُتَوَفَّى امْرَأَةٌ وَتَتْرُكْ زَوْجَهَا وَأَبَوَيْهَا فَيَكُونَ لِزَوْجِهَا النِّصْفُ، وَلِأُمِّهَا الثُّلُثُ مِمَّا بَقِيَ، وَهُوَ السُّدُسُ مِنْ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ" (السُّنَنُ الْكُبْرَى لِلْبَيْهَقِيِّ، بَابُ فَرْضِ الْأُمِّ، رقم 12294)
وَجْهٌ: (3) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنَ الْأَبَوَيْنِ... ﴿فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ﴾ (سُورَةُ النِّسَاءِ، 4، آيَة 11)
أُصُولٌ: ماں كَيْسا تَه مَيِّت كا بيٹا ہو يا پوتا ہو، يا اِسى طرح باپ كَيْسا تَه مَيِّت كا بيٹا ہو تو ماں، باپ کو سدس يعنے چھٹا حِصَّہ مِلے گا۔
The Book of Inheritances. And the sixth is the prescribed share of seven (heirs): for each of the parents when there is a child or a child's son; and it is for the mother with siblings (brothers and sisters); and for the grandfather with a child or a child's son. That is, the sixth is prescribed for the single one of them, whether male or female. If they are two or more, males or females, then the third is prescribed for them, they divide it equally. (Al-Sunan al-Kubra by al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on the share of siblings from the mother, no. 12324) Proof (1): The verse for the establishment of 'the sixth is the prescribed share of seven: for each of the parents...' 'And for his parents, for each of them, a sixth of what he left if he has a child; if he has no child and his parents inherit him, then for his mother a third; if he has siblings, then for his mother a sixth' (Surah al-Nisa, 4:11). Proof (2): The Companion's statement for establishment... (repeats the earlier quote from Zayd ibn Thabit). Proof (3): The verse for establishment... 'if he has siblings, then for his mother a sixth' (Surah al-Nisa, 4:11). Principles: If the deceased has a son or a son's son, or similarly if the father has a son (i.e., the deceased is survived by a child), then the mother and father each get a sixth, i.e., one-sixth share.
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining that the sixth (suds) is a prescribed share for seven categories of heirs: (1) the mother, (2) the father, each when the deceased has a child or a son's child; (3) the mother when there are siblings; (4) the grandfather when the deceased has a child or son's child. The passage also notes that for uterine siblings, if there are two or more, they receive one-third equally. The proofs are from Quran 4:11 and the statement of Zayd ibn Thabit. The Urdu summary reiterates that the mother and father get a sixth when the deceased has a child or grandchild.

Key Terms
السُّدُسُ (al-sudsu): One-sixth; a fixed share prescribed for certain heirs.
فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ (farḍu sab‘atin): A prescribed share that applies to seven categories of heirs (parents, mother with siblings, grandfather with child, etc.).
وَلَدُ الِابْنِ (waladu al-ibni): A son's son or daughter (grandchild through a son).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following heirs receives a sixth when the deceased has a child?
A) The paternal uncle
B) The grandfather
C) The grandmother
D) The uterine brother

Key Takeaway
The sixth share is a fixed Quranic right for parents, mother with siblings, and grandfather under specific conditions, and its application requires careful attention to the presence of descendants or siblings.

The Sixth Share as a Prescribed Share for Seven Heir Categories
Ruling with proof: enumerating seven categories for the sixth share and citing multiple textual evidences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven categories of heirs entitled to the sixth share and cite the primary Quranic and hadith proofs establishing this ruling.

Core Idea
The sixth share is a fixed obligatory portion for seven specific heir categories, confirmed by explicit Quranic text and prophetic tradition.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that one-sixth (السدس) is a prescribed share (فرض) for seven categories of heirs. In inheritance law (الفرائض), fixed shares are determined by divine command. The passage from Kitab al-Fara'id enumerates these categories and provides multiple proofs from the Quran, hadith, and sayings of the Companions to establish the certainty of this ruling. Understanding these categories is essential for accurate inheritance distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states that the sixth share is a fard (obligatory) for seven categories. Recognize that this is a fixed share in inheritance, not subject to discretion.
2
List the seven categories
The text enumerates: (1) father with child or grandchild, (2) mother with child or grandchild, (3) mother with siblings, (4) grandfather with child or grandchild, (5) grandmother when no mother exists, (6) granddaughter alongside a daughter, (7) siblings from the mother's side (kalalah case).
These categories are derived from the matn and the cited hadith.
3
Examine the primary proof
The Quranic verse (Surah An-Nisa 4:11) is cited: 'And for his parents, to each one of them is a sixth of what he left, if he has a child.' This establishes the parent's sixth and serves as the primary dalil for the ruling.
The verse is mutawatir in meaning and qat'i al-dalalah.
4
Examine secondary proofs
Additional proofs include hadith: the grandfather's sixth (Imran ibn Husayn), the grandmother's sixth, the daughter and granddaughter case, and the sayings of Zayd ibn Thabit and Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. These reinforce the ruling and address specific categories.
Secondary proofs provide tafsil (detail) for categories not explicitly named in the Quran.
5
Apply the ruling
Understand how these categories are applied in inheritance calculations. For example, if a deceased leaves a child, both parents receive 1/6 each. If no child but siblings, the mother receives 1/6. Practice identifying which category applies given a set of heirs.
Application requires combining this ruling with other faraid principles.

كِتَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الأَبَوَيْن مَعَ الْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْن وَهُوَ لِلْأُمَ مَعَ الإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ وَلِلْجَدِ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ ذَلِكَ يُفْرَضُ لِلْوَاحِدِ مِنْهُمُ السُّدُسَ ذَكَرًا كَانَ أَوْ أُنْثَى، فَإِنْ كَانُوا اثْنَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا ذُكُورًا أَوْ إِنَاثًا فَرضَ لَهُمُ الثُّلُثُ يَقْتَسِمُونَهُ بِالسَّوَاءِ السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ فَرْضِ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ للأُم، حديث 12324 وجه: (1) الأية لثبوت وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَبَوَيْنِ ﴿وَلِأَبَوَيْهِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ مِمَّا تَرَكَ إِن كَانَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُ وَلَدٌ وَوَرِثَهُ أَبَوَاهُ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ مِنْ بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِي بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ ءَابَاؤُكُمْ وَأَبْنَاؤُكُمْ لَا تَدْرُونَ أَيُّهُمْ أَقْرَبُ لَكُمْ نَفْعًا فَرِيضَةً مِّنَ اللَّهِ ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 آية نمبر 11) وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَبَوَيْنِ عَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ، وَأَمَّا التَّفْسِيرُ فَتَفْسِيرُ أَبي الزَّنَادِ عَلَى مَعَانِي زَيْدٍ قَالَ: " وَمِيرَاتُ الْأُمَ مِنْ وَلَدِهَا إِذَا تُوُفِّيَ ابْنُهَا وَابْنَتُهَا فَتَرَكَ وَلَدًا أَوْ وَلَدَ ابْن ذَكَرًا أَوْ أُنْثَى، أَوْ تَرَكَ الاثْنَيْنِ مِنَ الإِخْوَةِ فَصَاعِدًا ذُكُورًا أَوْ إِنَاثًا مِنْ أَبِ وَأُمَ، أَوْ مِنْ أَبِ، أَوْ مِنْ أُمّ السُّدُسُ ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَتْرُكِ الْمُتَوَفَّى وَلَدًا وَلَا وَلَدَ ابْنِ وَلَا اثْنَيْنِ مِنَ الْإِخْوَةِ فَصَاعِدًا فَإِنَّ لِلْأُمَ الثُّلُثَ كَامِلا ، إِلَّا فِي فَرِيضَتَيْنِ فَقَطْ وَهُمَا أَنْ يُتَوَفَّ رَجُلٌ وَيَتْرُكَ امْرَأَتَهُ وَأَبَوَيْهِ، فَيَكُونَ لِامْرَأَتِهِ الرُّبُعُ، وَلأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ مِمَّا بَقِيَ، وَهُوَ الرُّبُعُ مِنْ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ، وَإِنْ تُتَوَفَّى امْرَأَةٌ وَتَتْرُكْ زَوْجَهَا وَأَبَوَيْهَا فَيَكُونَ لِزَوْجِهَا النِّصْفُ، وَلأُمِهَا السُّدُسُ مِمَّا بَقِيَ، وَهُوَ السُّدُسُ مِنْ رَأْسِ الْمَالِ " (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ فَرْضِ الْأُمّ، حديث 12294) وجه : (۳) الآية لثبوت وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَبَوَيْنِ ﴿فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ مِنْ بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِى بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنِ مَابَاؤُكُمْ وَأَبْنَاؤُكُمْ لَا تَدْرُونَ أَيُّهُمْ أَقْرَبُ لَكُمْ نَفْعًا فَرِيضَةً مِّنَ اللَّهِ) (سورة النساء، 4 آية نمبر 11) اصول : ماں کیسا تھ میت کا بیٹا ہو یا پوتا ہو ، یا اسی طرح باپ کیسا تھ میت کا بیٹا ہو تو ماں ، باپ کو سدس یعنی چھٹا حصہ ملے گا وجه (۴) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَبَوَيْنِ أَوْ تَرَكَ الِاثْنَيْنِ مِنَ الْإِخْوَةِ فَصَاعِدًا ذُكُورًا أَوْ إِنَاثًا مِنْ أَبِ وَأُمَ، أَوْ مِنْ أَبِ، أَوْ مِنْ أُمّ السُّدُسُ، " (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ فَرْضِ الْأُمّ، حديث 12294) وجه : (۵) الحديث لثبوت وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَبَوَيْنِ عَنِ ابْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أبِيهِ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم جَعَلَ لِلْجَدَّةِ السُّدُسَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ دُونَهَا أُمِّ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ في الجدة، حديث 2895/سنن الترمذي ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مِيرَاتِ الجَدَّةِ، حديث 2101) وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَبَوَيْنِ عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُسَيْنَ، أَنَّ رَجُلًا أَتَى النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، فَقَالَ: إِنَّ ابْنَ ابْنِي مَاتَ، فَمَا لِي مِنْ مِيرَاثِهِ؟ فَقَالَ: «لَكَ السُّدُسُ» فَلَمَّا أَدْبَرَ دَعَاهُ، فَقَالَ: «لَكَ سُدُسٌ آخَرُ» فَلَمَّا أَدْبَرَ دَعَاهُ، فَقَالَ: «إِنَّ السُّدُسَ الْآخَرَ طُعْمَةٌ» قَالَ قَتَادَةُ: «فَلَا يَدْرُونَ مَعَ أَيِّ شَيْءٍ وَرَثَهُ»، قَالَ : قَتَادَةُ: «أَقَلُّ شَيْءٍ وَرِثَ الْجُدُّ السُّدُسُ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مِيرَاثِ الْجَدِ، حديث 2896/ سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي ميرَاتِ الجَدِ، حديث 2099) وجه : (۷) الحديث لثبوت وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَبَوَيْنِ «سُئِلَ أَبُو مُوسَى عَنِ ابْنَةِ وَابْنَةِ ابْن وَأُخْتِ، فَقَالَ: لِلابْنَةِ النِّصْفُ، وَلِلْأُخْتِ النِّصْفُ، وَأَتِ ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ فَسَيُتَابِعُني فَسُئِلَ ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ، وَأُخْبِرَ بِقَوْلِ أَبِي مُوسَى فَقَالَ: لَقَدْ ضَلَلْتُ إِذَا وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ الْمُهْتَدِينَ، أَقْضِي فِيهَا بِمَا قَضَى النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: لِلْابْنَةِ النِّصْفُ، وَلِابْنَةِ ابْنِ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةَ الثُّلُتَيْنِ، وَمَا بَقِيَ فَلِلْأُخْتِ(صحيح البخاري، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ ابْنَةِ ابْنِ مَعَ ابْنَةٍ ، حديث 6736/سنن ابوداود. بَابُ مَا جَاءَ في ميراث الصُّلْبِ حديث 2890) وجه (۸) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَبَوَيْنِ وَفِي قَوْلِ عَبْدِ اللهِ " لِلْأُخْتِ مِنَ الْأَبِ وَالْأُمّ النِّصْفُ، وَلِلْأَخَوَاتِ مِنَ الْأَبِ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةَ الثُلُتَيْنِ، وَمَا بَقِيَ لِلْأَخِ مِنَ الْآبِ " (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ لِأَبِ وَأُمِّ أَوْ لأب، حديث 12327) وجه: (۱) الآية لثبوت وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَبَوَيْنِ ﴿وَإِن كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلَالَةً أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ وَلَهُ أَخٌ أَوْ أُخْتُ فَلِكُلِ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ فَإِن كَانُواْ أَكْثَرَ مِنْ... (سورة النساء، 4 آية نمبر 12)
Book of Inheritance. And the sixth is a prescribed share for seven: for each of the two parents with the child or the child's son; and it is for the mother with brothers and sisters; and for the grandfather with the child or the child's son. That is, the sixth is prescribed for each of them, whether male or female. If they are two or more, males or females, a third is prescribed for them, they share it equally. (Al-Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, Chapter of the prescribed share of brothers and sisters for the mother, Hadith 12324) Proof (1): The verse to establish that the sixth is a prescribed share for seven, for each of the two parents: {... Qur'an 4:11 ...} Proof (2): The saying of the Companion to establish... from Zayd ibn Thabit... Proof (3): The verse... Proof (4): The saying of the Companion... Proof (5): The hadith... from Ibn Buraidah... that the Prophet assigned the sixth to the grandmother when there is no mother below her. Proof (6): The hadith from Imran ibn Husayn... Proof (7): The hadith... about the daughter and granddaughter... Proof (8): The saying of the Companion... from Abdullah... Proof (9): The verse for the kalalah case... (Qur'an 4:12).
Source pages p. 438

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Fara'id states the ruling that the sixth share (1/6) is a fixed prescribed share (fard) for seven categories of heirs. The author lists these categories: both parents when there is a child or grandchild; the mother when there are siblings (brothers/sisters); and the grandfather when there is a child or grandchild. The text then provides multiple proofs (wujuh) from the Quran, hadith, and sayings of the Companions (qawl al-sahabi) to establish this ruling. The first proof is from Surah An-Nisa 4:11, which explicitly assigns the sixth to each parent if the deceased has a child. The second is the interpretation of Zayd ibn Thabit regarding the mother's share. Other proofs include hadith about the grandmother's sixth, the grandfather's sixth, the case of a daughter and granddaughter, and the verse about kalalah. The passage ends with an Urdu explanation: if the deceased has a son or grandson, the mother and father each receive the sixth (one-sixth). This ruling is a foundational principle in Hanafi inheritance law, and the multiple proofs reinforce its certainty.

Key Terms
السدس (al-sudus): One-sixth, a fixed prescribed share in inheritance for specific heirs.
الفرائض (al-fara'id): The book of inheritance; fixed shares prescribed by Allah.
سبعة (sab'ah): Seven categories of heirs who receive the sixth share.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which verse from the Quran establishes the sixth share for parents?
A) Surah al-Baqarah 2:180
B) Surah An-Nisa 4:11
C) Surah al-Ma'idah 5:6
D) Surah al-Anfal 8:41

Key Takeaway
The sixth share (1/6) is a fixed fard share for seven categories of heirs, established by Quran and Sunnah, and its application depends on the presence or absence of other heirs.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
10 min
The Seven Heirs Entitled to One-Sixth Share and Their Proofs
Ruling on one-sixth share with multiple textual proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven categories of heirs entitled to one-sixth share in Hanafi fara'id and identify the textual proofs (Quran, Hadith, Sahaba qawl) that establish these shares.

Core Idea
One-sixth is a fixed share for seven heirs, each proven by explicit texts from Quran, Sunnah, or Companion consensus.

In this passage from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, we learn the fundamental rule that one-sixth is the prescribed share for seven distinct categories of heirs. The author then provides a rich collection of proofs from the Quran, multiple hadiths, and statements of the Companions, demonstrating how the Hanafi school derives these shares. Understanding both the ruling and its evidentiary basis is essential for mastering inheritance calculations (fara'id).

Guided Path
1
Identify the seven heirs
List the seven categories mentioned: father, mother, grandfather, grandmother, maternal brother, maternal sister, and consanguine sister (when completing two-thirds).
The list appears at the beginning of the passage: 'for each of the two parents...' etc.
2
Classify each proof by type
The passage cites multiple proofs: a Quranic verse (4:12), several hadiths (from Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi, Bukhari), and sayings of Companions (Ibn Mas'ud, Zaid ibn Thabit). For each proof, note whether it is Quran, Hadith, or Qawl Sahabi.
Some proofs are labeled with numbers (like وجه (۱), وجه (۲), etc.) but these numbers are not sequential.
3
Analyze the weight of each proof
For each proof, determine its epistemological weight: Quranic verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala in some aspects; hadiths are ahad but accepted; Companion sayings provide practical application.
The Quranic verse (4:12) explicitly gives one-sixth to maternal siblings.
4
Derive the legal scope
From the proofs, derive the conditions under which each heir receives one-sixth. For example, maternal siblings inherit only when there is no child, child's son, father, or grandfather (from Abu al-Zinad's interpretation).
The final point (وجه ۱۰) clarifies that maternal siblings do not inherit with a descendant or father/grandfather.
5
Note the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that these shares are fixed (fard) and not subject to istihsan. The proofs are consistent and mutually reinforcing, establishing consensus among the Sahaba.
Other schools may differ on specific conditions, but the general principle is agreed.

Source Text

كِتَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ وَالسُّدُسُ فَرْضُ سَبْعَةٍ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الْأَبَوَيْنِ أَوْ تَرَكَ الِاثْنَيْنِ مِنَ الْإِخْوَةِ فَصَاعِدًا ذُكُورًا أَوْ إِنَاثًا مِنْ أَبِ وَأُمَ، أَوْ مِنْ أَبِ، أَوْ مِنْ أُمِّ السُّدُسُ.

وجه (۴): قول الصحابي لثبوت ذلك: لِلْأَبَوَيْنِ السُّدُسُ وَلِلْأُمِّ السُّدُسُ وَلِلْجَدِّ السُّدُسُ وَلِلْجَدَّةِ السُّدُسُ وَلِلْأَخِ مِنَ الْأُمِّ السُّدُسُ وَلِلْأُخْتِ مِنَ الْأُمِّ السُّدُسُ وَلِلْأُخْتِ لِلْأَبِ وَالْأُمِّ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةَ الثُّلُثَيْنِ.

وجه (۵): الحديث لثبوت ذلك: عَنِ ابْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أبِيهِ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم جَعَلَ لِلْجَدَّةِ السُّدُسَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ دُونَهَا أُمِّ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الجَدَّةِ، نمبر 2895/سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مِيرَاثِ الجَدَّةِ، نمبر 2101)

وجه (۲): الحديث لثبوت ذلك: عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُسَيْنَ، أَنَّ رَجُلًا أَتَى النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم، فَقَالَ: إِنَّ ابْنَ ابْنِي مَاتَ، فَمَا لِي مِنْ مِيرَاثِهِ؟ فَقَالَ: «لَكَ السُّدُسُ» فَلَمَّا أَدْبَرَ دَعَاهُ، فَقَالَ: «لَكَ سُدُسٌ آخَرُ» فَلَمَّا أَدْبَرَ دَعَاهُ، فَقَالَ: «إِنَّ السُّدُسَ الْآخَرَ طُعْمَةٌ» قَالَ قَتَادَةُ: «فَلَا يَدْرُونَ مَعَ أَيِّ شَيْءٍ وَرَثَهُ»، قَالَ قَتَادَةُ: «أَقَلُّ شَيْءٍ وَرِثَ الْجُدُّ السُّدُسُ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مِيرَاثِ الْجَدِ، نمبر 2896/ سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي ميرَاثِ الجَدِ، نمبر 2099)

وجه: الحديث لثبوت ذلك: «سُئِلَ أَبُو مُوسَى عَنِ ابْنَةِ وَابْنَةِ ابْن وَأُخْتِ، فَقَالَ: لِلابْنَةِ النِّصْفُ، وَلِلْأُخْتِ النِّصْفُ، وَأَتِ ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ فَسَيُتَابِعُنِي، فَسُئِلَ ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ، وَأُخْبِرَ بِقَوْلِ أَبِي مُوسَى فَقَالَ: لَقَدْ ضَلَلْتُ إِذًا وَمَا أَنَا مِنَ الْمُهْتَدِينَ، أَقْضِي فِيهَا بِمَا قَضَى النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: لِلْابْنَةِ النِّصْفُ، وَلِابْنَةِ ابْنِ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةَ الثُّلُثَيْنِ، وَمَا بَقِيَ فَلِلْأُخْتِ» (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ ابْنَةِ ابْنِ مَعَ ابْنَةٍ، نمبر 6736/سنن ابوداود، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ في ميراث الصُّلْبِ، نمبر 2890)

وجه (۸): قول الصحابي لثبوت ذلك: وَفِي قَوْلِ عَبْدِ اللهِ: «لِلْأُخْتِ مِنَ الْأَبِ وَالْأُمِّ النِّصْفُ، وَلِلْأَخَوَاتِ مِنَ الْأَبِ السُّدُسُ تَكْمِلَةَ الثُّلُثَيْنِ، وَمَا بَقِيَ لِلْأَخِ مِنَ الْأَبِ» (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ لِأَبِ وَأُمِّ أَوْ لأب، نمبر 12327)

وجه (۱): الآية لثبوت ذلك: ﴿وَإِن كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلَالَةً أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ وَلَهُ أَخٌ أَوْ أُخْتٌ فَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ فَإِن كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلُثِ مِن بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصَى بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ غَيْرَ مُضَارٍّ وَصِيَّةً مِّنَ اللَّهِ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4:12)

وجه (۱۰): قول الصحابي تفسير أبي الزناد لثبوت ذلك: وَأَمَّا التَّفْسِيرُ فَتَفْسِيرُ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَلَى مَعَانِي زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ، قَالَ: «وَمِيرَاثُ الْإِخْوَةِ لِلْأُمِّ أَنَّهُمْ لَا يَرِثُونَ مَعَ الْوَلَدِ وَلَا مَعَ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ ذَكَرًا كَانَ أَوْ أُنْثَى شَيْئًا، وَلَا مَعَ الْأَبِ وَلَا مَعَ الْجَدِّ أَبِي الْأَبِ شَيْئًا، وَهُمْ فِي كُلِّ مَا سِوَى ذَلِكَ يُفْرَضُ لِلْوَاحِدِ مِنْهُمُ السُّدُسُ ذَكَرًا كَانَ أَوْ أُنْثَى، فَإِنْ كَانُوا اثْنَيْنِ فَصَاعِدًا ذُكُورًا أَوْ إِنَاثًا فُرِضَ لَهُمُ الثُّلُثُ يَقْتَسِمُونَهُ بِالسَّوَاءِ» (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ فَرْضِ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ لِلْأُمِّ، نمبر 12324)
Book of Inheritance: And one-sixth is the prescribed share of seven: for each of the two parents, or if the deceased leaves two or more siblings, male or female, from father and mother, or from father, or from mother, one-sixth. Then he cited the proofs: Point (4): Saying of the Companion to establish that: For the parents one-sixth, for the mother one-sixth, for the grandfather one-sixth, for the grandmother one-sixth, for the brother from mother one-sixth, for the sister from mother one-sixth, and for the sister from father and mother one-sixth as completion of two-thirds. Point (5): The hadith to establish that: From Ibn Buraidah, from his father, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) assigned one-sixth to the grandmother if there is no mother beneath her. Point (2): The hadith to establish that: From Imran ibn Husain that a man came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and said: My grandson died, what do I get from his inheritance? He said: You get one-sixth. When he turned away, he called him and said: You get another one-sixth. When he turned away, he called him and said: The other one-sixth is a gift. Qatada said: They do not know with what he inherited him. Qatada said: The least thing the grandfather inherits is one-sixth. Point: The hadith to establish that: Abu Musa was asked about a daughter, a son's daughter, and a sister. He said: For the daughter half, for the sister half. Go to Ibn Mas'ud and he will follow me. Ibn Mas'ud was asked and informed of Abu Musa's statement. He said: I would have gone astray and I am not amongst the guided. I judge in this matter as the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged: For the daughter half, for the son's daughter one-sixth to complete two-thirds, and the remainder is for the sister. Point (8): Saying of the Companion to establish that: In the statement of Abdullah: For the sister from father and mother half, for the sisters from father one-sixth to complete two-thirds, and what remains is for the brother from father. Point (1): The verse to establish that: {And if a man is inherited as kalalah or a woman, and he has a brother or a sister, then for each of them one-sixth. But if they are more than that, they are partners in one-third, after a will that is made or a debt, not harming. An ordinance from Allah} (Surah an-Nisa, 4:12). Point (10): Saying of the Companion, interpretation of Abu al-Zinad to establish that: As for the interpretation, it is the interpretation of Abu al-Zinad according to the meanings of Zaid ibn Thabit. He said: The inheritance of siblings from the mother is that they do not inherit anything with a child nor with a child's son, male or female, nor with the father nor with the grandfather, the father's father. And in every other case, one-sixth is prescribed for a single one of them, male or female. If they are two or more, male or female, one-third is prescribed for them, which they divide equally.
Source pages p. 439

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the inheritance chapter (Kitab al-Fara'id) from Al-Quduri's matn. It states the ruling that one-sixth is the prescribed share for seven categories of heirs, then provides multiple proofs from the Quran, Sunnah, and sayings of the Companions. The seven categories are: the father, the mother, the grandfather, the grandmother, the maternal brother, the maternal sister, and the consanguine sister when she completes two-thirds. The proofs include the explicit Quranic verse (4:12) concerning kalalah, several hadiths (from Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi, Bukhari) establishing specific shares, and statements of the Companions (Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, Abu Bakr, etc.). The final point cites the interpretation of Abu al-Zinad on the authority of Zaid ibn Thabit, clarifying that maternal siblings inherit one-sixth only when there is no child, child's son, father, or grandfather. This is the Hanafi position, which is based on the understanding that these shares are fixed by divine texts and consensus.

Key Terms
السُّدُس (as-sudus): One-sixth, a fixed share prescribed for certain heirs in Quranic inheritance.
فَرْض (fard): A fixed, divinely ordained share in inheritance.
كَلَالَة (kalalah): A person who dies without leaving parents or children.
تَكْمِلَةَ الثُّلُثَيْنِ (takmilat ath-thuluthayn): Completion of two-thirds, referring to the share of the consanguine sister when there is a full sister taking half, so the consanguine sister gets one-sixth to complete two-thirds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following heirs is entitled to a one-sixth share under the condition that there is no child, child's son, father, or grandfather?
A) The full sister
B) The maternal brother
C) The paternal grandmother
D) The father

Key Takeaway
One-sixth is a fixed share (fard) for seven categories of heirs, each supported by explicit texts from the Quran, Sunnah, or Companion practice, with conditions derived from the interpretations of the Sahaba.

Rules of Exclusion (Hajb) in Inheritance: Grandmothers, Grandfather, Siblings, and Maternal Half-Siblings
Rulings of exclusion with textual proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules of exclusion (hajb) for grandmothers, grandfather, siblings, and maternal half-siblings, and identify the textual proofs from the Quran and Hadith.

Core Idea
Closer heirs exclude more distant ones: mother excludes grandmother, father excludes grandfather and siblings, and child/grandchild/father/grandfather exclude maternal half-siblings.

In this passage from al-Quduri, we encounter the precise rules of exclusion (hajb) that determine which heirs are not entitled to inherit due to the presence of a closer relative. These rules are derived from explicit proofs: the hadith on the grandmother's share, the sayings of the Companions defining kalalah and the status of the grandfather, and the Quranic verse on maternal siblings. By mastering these rules, you will be able to correctly apply the principle of priority in inheritance distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and the excluding heir
For each heir mentioned (grandmothers, grandfather, siblings, maternal half-siblings), state precisely which closer heir excludes them.
The text is explicit: grandmothers excluded by mother, grandfather by father, siblings by father, maternal half-siblings by child, child's son, father, or grandfather.
2
Locate the proof for each rule
The passage provides a hadith for the grandmother's exclusion, a sahabi saying (Ibn Abbas) defining kalalah to establish the exclusion of siblings by father, another sahabi saying (Abu Bakr) equating grandfather to father and grandson to son for exclusion, and the Quranic verse (4:12) for maternal half-siblings.
Each proof directly supports the rule stated. Note that the hadith on grandmothers uses the condition 'when there is no mother beneath her.'
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof establishes the ruling)
The hadith shows the grandmother inherits only when the mother is absent, implying exclusion when mother exists. The sahabi sayings establish analogical exclusion. The Quranic verse limits maternal sibling inheritance to cases without child or parent, thus excluding them when these exist.
Pay attention to the logical link: the presence of a closer heir prevents the more distant from inheriting.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (cross-madhhab difference)
The hanafi_position_box indicates that the grandfather's position (like father) for excluding full siblings is contested by some schools (e.g., Shafi'i). According to Hanafis, the grandfather does not exclude full siblings, only the father does.
This difference has practical thamarah: in the absence of the father, the Hanafi school allows full siblings to inherit alongside the grandfather, while the Shafi'i school excludes them.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
Take a simple estate: deceased leaves mother, grandmother, father, full brother, and one maternal half-brother. Determine who is excluded. Mother excludes grandmother; father excludes grandfather (not present) and full brother; child (none) but father excludes maternal half-brother. So only mother and father inherit, with shares? Actually, the passage only gives exclusion rules; actual shares require further knowledge.
This step reinforces the practical impact: exclusion removes the heir entirely from the inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَتَسْقُطُ الْجُدَّاتُ بِالْأُمِّ وَالْجَدُّ وَالْإِخْوَةُ وَالْأَخَوَاتُ بِالْآبِ وَيَسْقُطُ وَلَدُ الْأُمِّ بِأَحَدِ أَرْبَعَةٍ: بِالْوَلَدِ وَوَلَدِ الِابْنِ وَالْأَبِ وَالْجَدِّ.

وجه (۱): الحديث لثبوت تسقط الجدات بالأم: عَنِ ابْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم جَعَلَ لِلْجَدَّةِ السُّدُسَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ دُونَهَا أُمِّ» (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي الْجَدَّةِ، نمبر 2895/سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي مِيرَاثِ الْجَدَّةِ، نمبر 2101)

وجه (۱): قول الصحابي لثبوت ذلك: عَنْ سُلَيْمِ بْنِ عَبْدِ السَّلُولِيِّ، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ يَقُولُ: «الْكَلَالَةُ الَّذِي لَا يَدَعُ وَلَدًا وَلَا وَالِدًا» (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ حَجْبِ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ مَنْ كَانُوا بِالْأَبِ وَالِابْنِ وَابْنِ الِابْنِ، نمبر 12275)

وجه (۲): قول الصحابي لثبوت ذلك: عَنْ أَبِي بَكْرٍ، قَالَ: «الْجَدُّ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْأَبِ مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ أَبٌ دُونَهُ، وَابْنُ الِابْنِ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الِابْنِ مَا لَمْ يَكُنِ ابْنٌ دُونَهُ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، في الْجَدِّ مَنْ جَعَلَهُ أَبًا، نمبر 31211)

وجه (۱): الآية لثبوت يسقط ولد الأم بأحد أربعة: ﴿وَإِن كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلَالَةً أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ وَلَهُ أَخٌ أَوْ أُخْتٌ فَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ فَإِن كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4:12)

أصول: حِصَّہ میں تقدیم و تاخیر کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے، جو پہلے ہو اس کو حصہ ملے گا، اور ان کے عدم میں دوسرے کو ملے گا۔
And grandmothers fall [from inheritance] by the mother, and the grandfather and brothers and sisters fall by the father, and the child of the mother falls by one of four: by the child, and the child's son, and the father, and the grandfather.

Point (1): The hadith to establish that grandmothers are excluded by the mother: From Ibn Buraidah, from his father, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) assigned one-sixth to the grandmother when there is no mother beneath her. (Sunan Abi Dawood, Sunan al-Tirmidhi)

Point (1): Saying of the Companion to establish that: From Sulaym ibn Abd al-Saluli, that he heard Ibn Abbas saying: "Al-Kalalah is the one who does not leave a child nor a parent." (Al-Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi)

Point (2): Saying of the Companion to establish that: From Abu Bakr, he said: "The grandfather is in the position of the father as long as there is no father beneath him, and the son's son is in the position of the son as long as there is no son beneath him." (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba)

Point (1): The verse to establish that the child of the mother is excluded by one of four: {And if a man is inherited as kalalah or a woman, and he has a brother or a sister, then for each of them one-sixth} (Surah an-Nisa, 4:12)

Principles: In shares, precedence and delay are considered; whoever comes first gets the share, and in their absence, the other gets it.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage presents the rules of exclusion (hajb) in inheritance. It states that grandmothers are excluded from inheritance when the mother is present. The grandfather is excluded when the father is present; likewise, full and consanguine brothers and sisters are excluded by the father. Maternal half-siblings (children of the mother) are excluded by any of four heirs: a child, a child's son (grandson), the father, or the grandfather. The proofs include the hadith about the grandmother's share being conditional on the absence of the mother, the saying of Ibn Abbas defining kalalah (the context in which maternal siblings inherit), the saying of Abu Bakr establishing the principle that the grandfather stands in place of the father and the grandson stands in place of the son for exclusion purposes (but not for other rulings), and the Quranic verse (4:12) which implies that maternal siblings inherit only in the absence of children and parents. The final Urdu note summarizes the overarching principle: in inheritance, priority matters—closer heirs take priority, and only in their absence do more distant heirs inherit.

Key Terms
حَجْب (hajb): Exclusion of an heir from inheritance due to the presence of a closer heir.
وَلَدُ الْأُمِّ (waladu al-umm): Maternal half-siblings (children sharing the same mother but different father).
جَدّ (jadd): Grandfather (father's father).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following heirs excludes maternal half-siblings?
A) The mother
B) The grandfather alone
C) The child and the father only
D) Any one of: child, child's son, father, or grandfather

Key Takeaway
Closer heirs (mother, father, child, grandchild) exclude more distant ones (grandmothers, siblings, maternal half-siblings); the proofs are explicit in the Quran, Hadith, and sayings of the Companions.

Exclusion of Grandmothers by the Mother
Ruling on grandmothers excluded by mother with prophetic hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that grandmothers are excluded by the mother, explain the hadith proof, and differentiate the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The mother excludes all grandmothers in Hanafi inheritance — only when she is absent do they inherit.

In this lesson, we examine a precise faraid ruling from al-Quduri: the exclusion (hajb) of all grandmothers by the mother. This rule is not arbitrary but grounded in a prophetic hadith. We will analyze the hadith's wording, understand why the Hanafi school interprets it as an exclusion, and contrast the Shafi'i view for clarity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
What is the ruling stated in the matn? All grandmothers are excluded by the mother.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The Prophet assigned grandmother one-sixth only when no mother exists.
The hadith is narrated by Ibn Buraydah.
3
Analyze the dalala
The condition 'if no mother' implies exclusion when mother is present. This is understood via mafhum al-mukhalafa.
Hanafi usul: a conditional clause indicates the opposite when the condition is absent.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'i interprets the hadith differently, allowing grandmother one-sixth even with mother.
They treat the condition as a description of a common case, not as a restricting condition.
5
Determine the practical implication
In Hanafi practice, if mother is alive, grandmother gets nothing. In Shafi'i, she gets one-sixth.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَتَسْقُطُ الجُدَّاتُ بِالأُمِّ. عَنِ ابْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم جَعَلَ لِلْجَدَّةِ السُّدُسَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ دُونَهَا أُمّ»
And grandmothers are excluded by the mother. From Ibn Buraydah, from his father, that the Prophet (peace be upon him) assigned to the grandmother the sixth when there is no mother below her.
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri: all grandmothers (paternal and maternal) are excluded from inheritance if the mother is present. The reason is that the mother is closer in lineage and more deserving. The author provides a hadith as proof: the Prophet granted the grandmother one-sixth only when there is no mother. This implies that with a mother, the grandmother does not inherit. The Hanafi position is that grandmothers are excluded by the mother alone; the father does not exclude grandmothers. This is based on the principle that the mother is the immediate connection.

Key Terms
الجُدَّاتُ (al-jaddāt): Grandmothers, both paternal and maternal
حَجْب (hajb): Exclusion from inheritance due to a closer heir

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who excludes all grandmothers from inheritance in the Hanafi school?
A) The father
B) The mother
C) The paternal grandfather
D) The son

Key Takeaway
The mother excludes all grandmothers from inheritance; they only inherit one-sixth if no mother exists.

Exclusion of Uterine Siblings by Four Heirs
Ruling on exclusion of children of mother by child, grandchild, father, grandfather.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four heirs who exclude uterine siblings and apply the condition of kalalah to determine when uterine siblings inherit.

Core Idea
Uterine siblings inherit only when there is no child, grandchild, father, or grandfather.

In Hanafi inheritance law, uterine siblings (walad al-umm) are heirs of the third category, but their right to inherit is conditional on the absence of certain closer heirs. This lesson examines the four heirs that completely exclude uterine siblings and the Quranic proof that establishes this rule. Understanding this exclusion is essential for accurate estate distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four excluding heirs
From the text: child (son or daughter), child's son (grandson), father, and paternal grandfather. These are the only four that exclude uterine siblings according to the Hanafi school.
The list includes both male and female children, but only the paternal grandfather, not the maternal.
2
Understand the concept of kalalah
The Quranic share for uterine siblings is revealed in the context of kalalah, defined as a deceased who leaves no child or parent. Thus, when a child or parent exists, the condition is not met and uterine siblings are excluded.
Hanafi definition of kalalah matches that of Ibn Abbas: no child and no parent.
3
Connect to the Quranic proof
The verse (4:12) specifies the share of uterine siblings 'in the third' only for kalalah. Since the four excluding heirs break the kalalah condition, uterine siblings receive nothing.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalalah regarding the exclusion.
4
Note the inter-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school holds that the grandfather does not exclude uterine siblings, and only the son (not daughter) excludes them. This leads to different inheritance outcomes.
The practical difference: in Shafi'i, a grandfather and uterine siblings may inherit together.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَسْقُطُ وَلَدُ الأُمِّ بِأَحَدِ أَرْبَعَةِ بِالْوَلَدِ وَوَلَدِ الِابْنِ وَالْأَبِ وَالْجَدِّ. فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلُثِ مِنْ بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصَى بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ غَيْرَ مُضَارٍ وَصِيَّةً مِنَ اللَّهِ (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 12) عَنْ سُلَيْمٍ بْنِ عَبْدِ السَّلُولِي، أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ يَقُولُ: " الْكَلَالَةُ الَّذِي لَا يَدَعُ وَلَدًا وَلَا وَالِدًا "
And the child of the mother is excluded by one of four: a child, a child's son, the father, and the grandfather. So they are partners in the third after a will bequeathed or a debt, not harmful, an ordinance from Allah (Surah al-Nisa, 4:12). From Sulaym ibn Abd al-Saluli, that he heard Ibn Abbas say: 'Al-Kalalah is the one who leaves no child nor parent.'
Source pages p. 440

Commentary
This passage states that uterine siblings (children of the mother, i.e., half-brothers and half-sisters from the mother's side) are excluded from inheritance by any of four heirs: a child (son or daughter), a child's son (grandson), the father, or the grandfather (paternal). The reason is that these four share a direct connection to the deceased that cuts off the uterine siblings. The Quranic verse (4:12) is cited as proof: 'And if a man is inherited as kalalah or a woman, and he has a brother or a sister, then for each one of them is the sixth...' This applies only when there is no child or parent, which is the definition of kalalah given by Ibn Abbas. Thus, when a child or parent exists, uterine siblings do not inherit. The Hanafi ruling is clear: they are excluded by these four. The verse also mentions the share of uterine siblings (one-sixth for one, one-third for two or more) but only when no child or parent exists.

Key Terms
وَلَدُ الأُمِّ (walad al-umm): Children of the mother (uterine half-siblings) sharing the same mother but different father
كَلَالَة (kalālah): A deceased who leaves neither parent nor child

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four heirs that exclude uterine siblings in the Hanafi school?
A) The son
B) The daughter
C) The paternal grandfather
D) The mother

Key Takeaway
Uterine siblings are excluded from inheritance by the presence of a child, grandchild, father, or paternal grandfather, based on the condition of kalalah from Quran 4:12.

Exclusion of Daughters of the Son When Full Daughters Take Two-Thirds
Faraid ruling with Quranic proof and athar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the exclusion of paternal granddaughters when full daughters receive two-thirds, and identify the condition under which granddaughters inherit via ta'sib.

Core Idea
Full daughters exhaust the two-thirds share; granddaughters are excluded unless a grandson agnates them.

In this lesson, we examine a key rule of Hanafi inheritance: when two or more full daughters inherit, they take the maximum fixed share of two-thirds, which blocks the inheritance of daughters of the son (paternal granddaughters). However, if a grandson is present at the same level, he becomes an asabah and brings the granddaughters with him, allowing them to share the residue. We will trace the Quranic proof and the clarification from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their categories
Determine which heirs are present: full daughters (banat) are Quranic heirs with a fixed share; daughters of the son (banat al-ibn) are also female descendants but one degree lower. Note their relationship and the presence of any male agnatic heir from the same level (son of the son).
2
Apply the fix: full daughters take two-thirds
According to Quran 4:11, if there are two or more full daughters, they receive two-thirds of the estate. This is their maximum fixed share. This allocation consumes the entire female share from that line.
The verse: 'فَإِن كُنَّ نِسَاءً فَوْقَ اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُنَّ ثُلُثَا مَا تَرَكَ'
3
Check exclusion of granddaughters
Once full daughters have taken two-thirds, the daughters of the son are excluded (saaqitah) and receive nothing, unless there is a son of the son (grandson) present. The grandson, being a male agnate, becomes an asabah and by ta'sib makes the granddaughters also asabah, so they share the residue (if any).
The exclusion is based on the principle that the same degree of female descendants cannot double up on the two-thirds share.
4
Analyze the proof and cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi rely on the apparent meaning of the verse—the two-thirds is for 'above two' daughters, implying no other female descendants at that level. The Shafi'i school holds that granddaughters are not excluded; they take the remaining sixth after the daughters' two-thirds (if only one daughter, they share half). This difference stems from the interpretation of 'awlād' (children) and the status of granddaughters.
The athar from Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib supports the Hanafi view: 'and no inheritance with them for the daughters of the father'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اسْتَكْمَلَ الْبَنَاتُ الثُّلُثَيْنِ سَقَطَتْ بَنَاتُ الِابْنِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهُنَّ أَوْ بِإِزَائِهِنَّ أَوْ أَسْفَلَ مِنْهُنَّ ابْنُ ابْنٍ فَيَعْصِبُهُنَّ. يُوصِيكُمُ اللَّهُ فِي أَوْلَادِكُمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ ۚ فَإِن كُنَّ نِسَاءً فَوْقَ اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُنَّ ثُلُثَا مَا تَرَكَ (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 11). عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ الْمُسَيَّبِ: فَإِنْ كَانَ بَنُو الأُمِّ وَالْآبِ امْرَأَتَيْنِ فَأَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْإِنَاثِ فَيُفْرَضُ فَهُنَّ الثُّلُثَانِ وَلَا مِيرَاثَ مَعَهُنَّ لِبَنَاتِ الْأَبِ، إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهُنَّ ذَكَرٌ مِنْ أَبِ، فَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَهُنَّ ذَكَرْ بُدِئَ بِفَرَائِضِ مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ فَرِيضَةٌ فَأَعْطُوهَا، فَإِنْ فَضَلَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فَضْلٌ كَانَ بَيْنَ بَنِي الْآبِ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْضُلْ شَيْءٌ فَلَا شَيْءَ لَهُمْ
And when the daughters complete the two-thirds, the daughters of the son are excluded unless there is with them, or opposite them, or below them, a son of a son, then he agnates them. Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male is like the fortune of two females. And if they are women above two, then for them two-thirds of what he left (Surah al-Nisa 4:11). From Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib: ... And no inheritance with them for the daughters of the father, unless there is with them a male from the father, then if there is a male with them, the fixed shares of those who have a fixed share are given first, then whatever remains is between the children of the father, the male gets the share of two females.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation when there are multiple full daughters (or more than one) and they take two-thirds of the estate, which is their maximum. In that case, daughters of the son (paternal granddaughters) are excluded and receive nothing, unless there is a son of the son (a grandson) with them. If a grandson is present at the same level (equal or lower), he becomes an asabah (agnatic heir) and makes the granddaughters asabah with him, so they inherit together through ta'sib. The proof is from Quran 4:11 which allocates two-thirds to daughters if there are two or more, implying that others are excluded when that share is taken. The saying of Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib clarifies that granddaughters do not inherit if full daughters have taken the two-thirds, unless a grandson is present to agnate them. The Hanafi rule is that full daughters take two-thirds, and granddaughters are then excluded; but if a grandson is present, he and the granddaughters take the residue (if any) by ta'sib, with the male getting double the female. The Urdu note at the end emphasizes: after daughters take two-thirds, granddaughters get nothing; however, if there is a grandson below them who becomes an asabah, then granddaughters also get shares under the rule 'the male gets the share of two females'.

Key Terms
بَنَاتُ الِابْنِ (banāt al-ibn): Daughters of the son (paternal granddaughters)
عُصْبَة (ʿuṣbah): Agnatic heir who takes the residue after fixed shares
تَعْصِيب (taʿṣīb): Making someone an asabah through a male relation

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Never

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, when two or more full daughters take the maximum two-thirds, daughters of the son are excluded unless a grandson makes them asabah.

Exclusion of Granddaughters by Daughters' Two-Thirds Share
Ruling on exclusion of granddaughters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for excluding granddaughters when daughters take two-thirds, and identify the exception when a grandson is present.

Core Idea
Daughters' two-thirds exhausts the female share; granddaughters are excluded unless a grandson makes them agnates.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn on inheritance (fara'id) states a key rule: when daughters receive the full two-thirds share from the Quran (4:11), granddaughters (daughters of a son) are excluded from inheritance. However, there is a critical exception: if there is a grandson at the same level or lower, he becomes an agnate (asabah) and includes the granddaughters with him, so they share the residue in a 2:1 male-to-female ratio. The author supports this with Quranic verses and a companion's statement.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the act (inheritance of granddaughters) and the ruling: when daughters complete the two-thirds share, granddaughters are excluded (fall).
This is the default Hanafi position.
2
Identify the exception: Grandson present
Note that if a grandson (son of a son) is present at the same level or lower, he acts as an asabah and includes the granddaughters with him, so they inherit.
The exception is key to understanding the ruling.
3
Examine the Quranic proof (4:11)
The verse establishes the two-thirds share for daughters. The Hanafi interpretation is that this exhausts the available share for female descendants, excluding granddaughters.
Focus on the phrase 'for them two-thirds of what he leaves'.
4
Consider the cross-madhhab dispute: Shafi'i view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that granddaughters are not excluded; they inherit as agnates along with daughters even without a male. Hanafis differ based on the completion of the two-thirds.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Apply the rule to a hypothetical estate
Given an estate with two daughters and one granddaughter (no grandson): daughters get 2/3, granddaughter gets nothing. Now add a grandson: the residue (1/3) is divided among grandson and granddaughter with 2:1 ratio.
This solidifies understanding of the rule and exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كِتَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ
وَإِذَا اسْتَكْمَلَ الْبَنَاتُ الثُّلُثَيْنِ سَقَطَتْ بَنَاتُ الابْنِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهُنَّ أَوْ بِإِزَائِهِنَّ أَوْ أَسْفَلَ مِنْهُنَّ ابْنُ ابْنٍ فَيَعْصِبُهُنَّ
وَجْهٌ (١) الْآيَةُ: {يُوصِيكُمُ اللَّهُ فِي أَوْلَادِكُمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ فَإِنْ كُنَّ نِسَاءً فَوْقَ اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُنَّ ثُلُثَا مَا تَرَكَ} [النساء: ١١]
وَجْهٌ (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ: عَنْ سُلَيْمٍ بْنِ عَبْدِ السَّلُولِيِّ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ يَقُولُ: "الْكَلَالَةُ الَّذِي لَا يَدَعُ وَلَدًا وَلَا وَالِدًا" وَكَذَلِكَ رَوَاهُ إِسْرَائِيلُ عَنْ أَبِي إِسْحَاقَ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ حَجْبِ الإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ مَنْ كَانُوا بالآب والابن وابن الابن نمبر 12275)
وَجْهٌ (٣) الْآيَةُ: {فَإِن كَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُمَا الظُّلُتَانِ مِمَّا تَرَكَ وَإِن كَانُوا إِخْوَةً رِجَالًا وَنِسَاءً فَلِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ} [النساء: 176]
اصول: بیٹیوں کے دو تہائی لینے کے بعد پوتیوں کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا، البتہ ان کے ساتھ ان کے نیچے پوتے ہوں جو عصبہ بن رہے ہوں تو لذکر مثل حظ الانثیین کے تحت پوتیوں کو بھی ملے گا۔
Book of Inheritance: When the daughters complete the two-thirds, the daughters of the son fall, unless there is with them or opposite them or lower than them a son of a son, so he makes them agnates. Proof 1: The verse: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male, like the share of two females; but if there are women above two, then for them two-thirds of what he leaves' [4:11]. Proof 2: The saying of the Companion: from Sulaym ibn Abd al-Saluli that he heard Ibn Abbas say: 'Al-kalala is one who leaves neither child nor parent.' And similarly Isra'il narrated from Abu Ishaq. Proof 3: The verse: 'But if there are two, for them two-thirds of what he leaves; and if they are brothers, men and women, then for the male like the share of two females' [4:176]. Principle: After the daughters take the two-thirds, the granddaughters get nothing, unless there are grandsons with them who become agnates; then according to the rule of the male like the share of two females, the granddaughters also get a share.
Source pages p. 441

Commentary
This is a ruling from the Book of Inheritance, accompanied by textual proofs. The ruling states: When daughters (the highest female descendants) receive the full two-thirds share of the estate, the granddaughters (daughters of a son) are excluded from inheritance entirely. However, there is an exception: if there is a grandson (son of a son) at the same level or lower, he acts as a cognate (asabah) and includes the granddaughters with him, making them co-agnates. In that case, the estate after the daughters' two-thirds goes to the grandsons and granddaughters according to the Quranic principle 'for the male like the share of two females.' The author provides three proofs: first, Quran 4:11, which establishes the two-thirds share for daughters and implies that lower descendants cannot inherit when that share is exhausted; second, a statement from Ibn Abbas defining 'kalala' (though this appears to be a marginal note related to a different rule); third, Quran 4:176, which again applies the two-thirds rule and the male-to-female ratio. The Urdu commentary summarizes: after daughters take two-thirds, granddaughters get nothing unless accompanied by a grandson who becomes an agnate.

Key Terms
عَصَبَة (asabah): Agnatic heir who inherits the residue after fixed shares are distributed; includes male descendants through males.
فَرَائِض (fara'id): The fixed shares allocated to specific heirs in the Quran and Sunnah.
بَنَاتُ الابْن (banat al-ibn): Daughters of a son; granddaughters through a male line.
سَقَطَت (saqatat): Falls; a technical term meaning the heir is excluded from inheritance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) They inherit only when the daughters are deceased.

Key Takeaway
Granddaughters are excluded by daughters' two-thirds unless a grandson includes them as agnates.
