Exclusion of Half-Sisters by Full Sisters' Two-Thirds
Ruling with proof on half-sister exclusion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the exclusion of half-sisters, identify the condition of a half-brother, and cite the Quranic and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Half-sisters are excluded when full sisters take two-thirds, unless a half-brother includes them.

In Hanafi inheritance law, full sisters have priority over half-sisters. This lesson examines the rule that when two or more full sisters exhaust the two-thirds share, half-sisters from the father are excluded from inheritance unless a half-brother is present, who as an agnate includes them. The ruling is supported by Quran 4:176, a companion's saying, and a prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs present
Determine which categories of sisters exist: full sisters (same parents), half-sisters (same father), and whether a half-brother is present.
Full sisters are primary; half-sisters are secondary.
2
Apply the exclusion rule
If there are two or more full sisters, they receive the fixed two-thirds share. This exhausts the estate's sister-share, excluding half-sisters from inheritance.
Exclusion is total unless a half-brother exists.
3
Check the exception: half-brother presence
If a half-brother (male agnate from father) accompanies the half-sisters, he turns them into agnates, and they inherit together with the full sisters according to male-female ratio.
The half-brother must be present; otherwise half-sisters are blocked.
4
Trace the proofs
Analyze the three proofs: Quran 4:176 (two-thirds assigned, brothers ratio), the saying of Ibn Abbas (explicit exclusion unless male), and the hadith (fixed shares first, residue to nearest male agnate).
The hadith and verse together support the Hanafi ruling.
5
Understand cross-madhhab difference
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that half-sisters are not entirely excluded; they inherit as residuaries if there are no full sisters, but with full sisters present, they are excluded only if the full sisters are asabah. Hanafis exclude absolutely when two-thirds completed.
The practical effect: Hanafis give nothing to half-sisters without a half-brother; Shafi'is sometimes include them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اسْتَكْمَلَ الْأَخَوَاتُ لِلْأَبِ وَالأُمِّ الثُّلُقَيْنِ سَقَطَ الأَخَوَاتُ لِلْأَبِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهُنَّ أَخٌ فَيَعْصِبُهُنَّ
وَجْهٌ (١) الْآيَةُ: {فَإِن كَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُمَا الظُّلُتَانِ مِمَّا تَرَكَ وَإِن كَانُوا إِخْوَةً رِجَالًا وَنِسَاءً فَلِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ يُبَيِّنُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ أَن تَضِلُّوا وَاللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيم} (سورة النساء، 4 أيت غير 176)
وَجْهٌ (٢) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ: فَإِنْ كَانَ بَنُو الأُمِّ وَالْآبِ امْرَأَتَيْنِ فَأَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْإِنَاثِ فَيُفْرَضُ فَنَّ القُلُتَانِ وَلَا مِيرَاثَ مَعَهُنَّ لِبَنَاتِ الْأَبِ، إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهُنَّ ذَكَرٌ مِنْ أَبِ، فَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَهُنَّ ذَكَرٌ بُدِئَ بِفَرَائِضِ مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ فَرِيضَةٌ فَأَعْطُوهَا، فَإِنْ فَضَلَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فَضْلٌ كَانَ بَيْنَ بَنِي الْأَبِ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْضُلْ شَيْءٍ فَلَا شَيْءَ لَهُمْ (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالأَخَوَاتِ لِأَبِ وَأُمِّ أَوْ لأَب، نمبر 12326)
وَجْهٌ (٣) الْحَدِيثُ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «أَلْحِقُوا الْفَرَائِضَ بِأَهْلِهَا فَمَا تَرَكَتِ الْفَرَائِضُ فَلِأَوْلَى رَجُلٍ ذَكَرٍ» (صحيح البخاري، بَابُ ابْنَيْ عَمٍّ أَحَدُهُمَا أَخٌ لِلْأُمِّ وَالْآخَرُ زَوْجٌ، نمبر 6746؛ سنن ابوداود، باب في مِيرَاتِ الْعَصَبَةِ، 2898)
اصول: جب کبھی بھائی اور بہن دونوں حصہ لینے والے ہوں تو قاعدہ لذکر مثل حظ الأثمین جاری ہو گا، یعنی بھائی کو دو گنا اور بہن کو ایک گنا ملے گا، خواہ وہ دونوں میت کے لئے بیٹا یا بیٹی ہو یا پوتا، پوتی ہو یا بھائی، بہن ہو، البتہ یہ دونوں بھائی، بہن ہی ہونگے۔
And when the sisters for father and mother complete the two-thirds, the sisters for father fall, unless there is with them a brother, so he makes them agnates. Proof 1: The verse: 'But if there are two, for them two-thirds of what he leaves; and if they are brothers, men and women, then for the male like the share of two females. Allah makes clear to you, lest you go astray. And Allah is Knowing of all things' [4:176]. Proof 2: The saying of the Companion: 'If the children of the mother and father are two or more women, then they are prescribed the two-thirds, and there is no inheritance with them for the daughters of the father, unless there is a male from the father with them. If there is a male with them, then begin with the fixed shares of those who have a fixed share and give them; then if there is a surplus after that, it is among the children of the father, for the male like the share of two females; if nothing remains, nothing for them.' Proof 3: The hadith: from Ibn Abbas, from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Give the fixed shares to their people, and what is left over goes to the nearest male relative.' Principle: Whenever a brother and sister are both taking shares, the rule of the male like the share of two females applies, meaning the brother gets two portions and the sister one, whether they are son/daughter, grandson/granddaughter, or brother/sister, as long as they are indeed brother and sister.
Source pages p. 442

Commentary
This is a parallel ruling to the previous one, now concerning full sisters (from the same mother and father) and half-sisters (from the father only). The ruling: When full sisters complete the two-thirds share, half-sisters are excluded from inheritance. However, if there is a half-brother (a male from the father) present, he acts as an agnate and includes the half-sisters, and they all inherit according to the principle of 'the male gets twice the share of the female.' This is confirmed by three proofs: first, Quran 4:176, which establishes the two-thirds for two sisters and the male-female ratio; second, a saying of Ibn Abbas reported in Al-Bayhaqi's Sunan al-Kubra, explicitly stating that when children of the mother and father (i.e., full siblings) reach two-thirds, daughters of the father (half-sisters) get nothing unless there is a male from the father; third, a hadith from the Prophet instructing to allocate fixed shares first and the remainder to the nearest male relative. The Urdu commentary explains that whenever a brother and sister together inherit, the Quranic ratio applies to them, regardless of their specific relation (children, grandchildren, siblings), provided they are indeed brother and sister (i.e., same generation).

Key Terms
الْأَخَوَاتُ لِلْأَبِ وَالأُمِّ (al-akhawat li'l-ab wa'l-umm): Full sisters (same mother and father).
الْأَخَوَاتُ لِلْأَبِ (al-akhawat li'l-ab): Half-sisters (same father, different mother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition under which half-sisters (from the father) inherit alongside full sisters who have already taken two-thirds of the estate?
A) They never inherit with full sisters.
B) They inherit only if there is a half-brother (from the father) present to make them agnates.
C) They inherit equally with full sisters regardless of any male agnate.
D) They inherit only if the full sisters renounce their share.

Key Takeaway
Full sisters' two-thirds share blocks half-sisters from inheritance unless a half-brother includes them as residuaries.

Order of Agnates (Aqrab al-Asabat)
Listing nearest agnates in order of priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the order of priority of agnates (asabat) in Hanafi inheritance and identify the three types of asaba.

Core Idea
Residue after fixed shares goes to the nearest agnate; full siblings outweigh half-siblings.

In this lesson, we cover the foundational Hanafi list of residuary heirs (asabat) in order of priority. This is a key memorization anchor for faraid. The passage also introduces the three types of asaba: by self, by another, and with another, which explain how females can become residuary heirs.

Guided Path
1
Recite the order from the matn
Read the list: sons, their sons, father, grandfather, brothers, sons of brothers (nephews), paternal uncles, sons of paternal grandfather. Identify the first five categories.
This order is absolute in Hanafi law.
2
Apply the principle of degree
When two heirs are in the same degree (e.g., two brothers), the full brother (same mother and father) takes precedence over the half-brother (same father only). This is based on the hadith from Ali.
Degree means relation to deceased; full sibling has stronger connection.
3
Identify the proofs cited
Three proofs: Quran 4:176 (kalalah), hadith 'Give fixed shares...' for residue to nearest male, and hadith from Ali on full brother preference. Note that these are naqli (textual) evidences.
The second hadith is a key principle for all asaba.
4
Classify each agnate into the three types
From the Urdu commentary: asaba bi-nafsihi (son, grandson, father, etc.), asaba bi-ghayrihi (daughter with son), asaba ma'a ghayrihi (sister with daughter). Identify which category each heir from the list belongs to.
Only males are asaba bi-nafsihi; females enter via bi-ghayrihi or ma'a ghayrihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ أَقْرَبِ الْعَصَبَاتِ قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: وَأَقْرَبُ الْعَصَبَاتِ الْبَنُونَ، ثُمَّ بَنُوهُمْ، ثُمَّ الْأَبُ، ثُمَّ الْجَدُّ، ثُمَّ الْإِخْوَةُ، ثُمَّ بَنُو الْإِخْوَةِ وَهُمُ الْأَعْمَامُ، ثُمَّ بَنُو أَبِي الْجَدِّ. وَإِذَا اسْتَوَى وَارِثَانِ فِي دَرَجَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ فَأَوْلَاهُمْ مَنْ كَانَ لِلْأَبِ وَالْأُمِّ. وَجْهٌ: (١) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ: يَسْتَفْتُونَكَ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِي الْكَلَالَةِ (سورة النساء، 4، آية 176). وَجْهٌ: (٢) الْحَدِيثُ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «أَلْحِقُوا الْفَرَائِضَ بِأَهْلِهَا فَمَا تَرَكَتِ الْفَرَائِضُ فَلِأَوْلَى رَجُلٍ ذَكَرٍ» (صحيح البخاري، رقم 6746، سنن أبي داود، رقم 2898). وَجْهٌ: (٣) الْحَدِيثُ: عَنْ عَلِيٍّ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: وَإِنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَضَى بِالدَّيْنِ قَبْلَ الْوَصِيَّةِ، وَإِنَّ أَعْيَانَ بَنِي الْأُمِّ يَتَوَارَثُونَ دُونَ بَنِي الْعَلَّاتِ، الرَّجُلُ يَرِثُ أَخَاهُ لِأَبِيهِ وَأُمِّهِ دُونَ أَخِيهِ لِأَبِيهِ (سنن الترمذي، رقم 2094). أصول: عصبات یعنی باپ کے رشتہ دار، چونکہ یہ حصہ لینے والے سب باپ کے رشتہ دار ہوتے ہیں اسلئے عصبات کہتے ہیں۔ اصول: عصبات کی چار قسمیں ہیں: 1) عصبہ بنفسہ: جو خود بخود عصبہ بنے، جیسے بیٹا، پوتا وغیرہ، 2) عصبہ بغیرہ: جو غیر کے واسطہ سے عصبہ بنے، جیسے بیٹی، بیٹے کیساتھ، پوتی، پوتے کیساتھ وغیرہ، 3) عصبہ مع غیرہ: جو عورت عصبہ نہ بنے، اور نہ کسی نے عصبہ بنایا، البتہ بیٹی، پوتی کے بعد کوئی عصبہ مرد نہ ہو تو حقیقی یاعلاتی بہن کیساتھ عصبہ بنیں گی۔
CHAPTER OF THE NEAREST AGNATES. The author, may Allah have mercy on him, said: And the nearest of the agnates are the sons, then their sons (grandsons), then the father, then the grandfather, then the brothers, then the sons of brothers (nephews), and they are the paternal uncles, then the sons of the paternal grandfather. And when two heirs are equal in the same degree, then the closer of them is the one who is from the father and mother. Face (1): The verse for proof: 'They ask you for a ruling. Say, Allah gives you a ruling concerning the one who dies without a child...' (Surah An-Nisa, 4:176). Face (2): The hadith: Ibn Abbas, from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Give the fixed shares to their entitled ones, and whatever remains after the fixed shares goes to the nearest male relative' (Sahih al-Bukhari, no. 6746; Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 2898). Face (3): The hadith: From Ali that he said: 'Indeed, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) judged that the debt is before the will, and that the full brothers inherit from each other to the exclusion of half-brothers; a man inherits from his full brother, not from his half-brother' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 2094). Principles: Asaba means the father's relatives; because all these shares are taken by father's relatives, they are called asaba. Principles: Asaba are of four types: 1) Asaba bi-nafsihi: one who is an agnate by himself, like son, grandson, etc. 2) Asaba bi-ghayrihi: one who becomes agnate through someone else, like daughter with son, granddaughter with grandson. 3) Asaba ma'a ghayrihi: a female who does not become agnate by herself and no one makes her agnate, but when there is no male agnate after a daughter or granddaughter, she becomes agnate with a full or half-sister.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage from the chapter 'Aqrab al-Asabat' lists the order of residuary heirs (asabat) in Hanafi law. The matn begins by stating the closest agnate: the sons of the deceased, then grandsons (sons' sons), then the father, then the grandfather (father's father), then brothers (full or half? The text says 'ikhwa' but later specifies full vs half), then nephews (sons of brothers), then paternal uncles, then sons of paternal grandfather (i.e., cousins). The principle is that the nearer in degree excludes the more distant. When two heirs are in the same degree (e.g., two brothers), the one who is full (same mother and father) takes precedence over the half-brother (same father only). The proofs cited: 1) Quran 4:176, which deals with kalalah and mentions siblings, establishing that siblings inherit as residuary after fixed shares? Actually the verse is cited generally as authority for the system. 2) The hadith 'Give the fixed shares...' establishes the principle of asaba. 3) A hadith from Ali stating that full brothers inherit to the exclusion of half-brothers (from father only). The Urdu commentary adds the classification of asaba into three types: asaba bi-nafsihi (inherently residuary, e.g., son), asaba bi-ghayrihi (made residuary by a male counterpart, e.g., daughter with son), and asaba ma'a ghayrihi (female residuary in the company of another female, e.g., sisters with daughters). This classification is key to understanding how females can become residuary heirs in certain circumstances.

Key Terms
العصبات (al-ʿaṣabāt): Agnates; male relatives on the father's side who inherit the residue after fixed shares.
عصبہ بنفسہ (ʿaṣabah bi-nafsihī): An agnate who inherits by virtue of his own relationship to the deceased, without needing another person.
عصبہ بغیرہ (ʿaṣabah bi-ghayrihī): A female who becomes an agnate because she is accompanied by a male of the same degree (e.g., daughter with son).
عصبہ مع غیرہ (ʿaṣabah maʿa ghayrihī): A female who becomes an agnate in the company of another female (e.g., full or half-sister with a daughter).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased man leaves a full brother and a half-brother (from father only). Who inherits the residue after fixed shares?
A) The full brother only
B) The half-brother only
C) Both equally
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
The order of agnates in Hanafi faraid prioritizes sons, then their male descendants, then father, then grandfather, then brothers, then nephews, then uncles, etc., with full siblings taking precedence over half-siblings.

Order of the Nearest Asabah in Hanafi Inheritance
Explains the order of residuary heirs by closeness and their inheritance rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of asabah and apply the rules of precedence (full vs half, sharing with sisters, wala) when distributing inheritance.

Core Idea
In Hanafi faraid, the closest male blood relative inherits the residual; grandfather precedes brother, full siblings outrank half, and wala applies when no blood asabah exist.

This lesson presents the foundational Hanafi order of residuary heirs (asabah), backed by Quranic verse, Prophetic hadith, and the practice of the Companions. You will learn the precise sequence of male relatives who inherit after the fixed shares, the special 2:1 sharing rule for sons and brothers with their sisters, and the rule for wala (clientage) when no blood asabah survive. Understanding this order is essential for correctly calculating inheritance in any given case.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the order of asabah from the matn
List the categories in sequence: sons, then their sons, then father, then grandfather, then brothers, then sons of brothers, then paternal uncles, then sons of paternal uncles, then higher grandfathers. Commit this order to memory.
The order is based on closeness of relationship: descending progeny, then ascending ancestors, then collateral descendants.
2
Understand the rule for males inheriting with females
For sons, sons' sons, and brothers: when they inherit with sisters of the same class, the male takes twice the female's share (2:1). For all other asabah (uncles, cousins, etc.), males take the entire inheritance and females are excluded.
This distinction is a key Hanafi rule; other schools may have different rules.
3
Apply precedence among equal degrees
When two asabah are equally distant in relationship (e.g., two paternal uncles), the one who is related through both father and mother (full) takes precedence over the one related only through the father (consanguine).
Full siblings always outrank half-siblings when they are in the same category.
4
Know the wala rule when no blood asabah exist
If the deceased has no asabah by blood, the manumitter (master who freed the slave) becomes the asabah, and then the manumitter's own asabah, in order of closeness. Women inherit from wala only if they personally freed the slave.
Wala is a legal relationship created by manumission, not blood.
5
Connect the proofs to the rules
The Quran (4:11) establishes the 2:1 ratio for children. The hadith 'Give the fixed shares to those entitled to them, and whatever remains is for the nearest male' (Bukhari) establishes the principle of residual inheritance. The hadith about full brothers outranking half (Tirmidhi) supports the precedence rule. The hadith of Barirah shows wala belongs to the one who frees.
These proofs are directly cited in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ أَقْرَبِ الْعَصَبَاتِ
قَالَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: وَأَقْرَبُ الْعَصَبَاتِ الْبَنُونَ ثُمَّ بَنُوهُمْ ثُمَّ الْأَبُ ثُمَّ الْجَدُّ ثُمَّ الْإِخْوَةُ ثُمَّ بَنُو الْإِخْوَةِ ثُمَّ الْأَعْمَامُ ثُمَّ بَنُو الْأَبِ ثُمَّ الْجَدِّ. وَإِذَا اسْتَوَى وَارِثَانِ فِي دَرَجَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ فَأَوْلَاهُمْ مَنْ كَانَ لِلْأَبِ وَالْأُمِّ. وَالِابْنُ وَابْنُ الابْنِ وَالْإِخْوَةُ يُقَاسِمُونَ أَخَوَاتِهِمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ، وَمَنْ عَدَاهُمْ مِنْ الْعَصَبَاتِ يَنْفَرِدُ ذُكُورُهُمْ بِالْمِيرَاثِ دُونَ إِنَاثِهِمْ. وَإِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ لِلْمَيِّتِ عَصَبَةٌ مِنْ النَّسَبِ فَالْعَصَبَةُ هُوَ الْمَوْلَى الْمُعْتِقُ ثُمَّ الْأَقْرَبُ فَالْأَقْرَبُ مِنْ عَصَبَةِ الْمَوْلَى.
وَجْهُ الْآيَةِ: ﴿يُوصِيكُمُ اللَّهُ فِي أَوْلَادِكُمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ﴾ (النساء: 11)
وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «أَلْحِقُوا الْفَرَائِضَ بِأَهْلِهَا فَمَا تَرَكَتِ الْفَرَائِضُ فَلِأَوْلَى رَجُلٍ ذَكَرٍ» (صحيح البخاري رقم 6746)
وَالْحَدِيثُ الْآخَرُ: عَنْ عَلِيٍّ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَضَى بِالدَّيْنِ قَبْلَ الْوَصِيَّةِ، وَأَنَّ أَعْيَانَ بَنِي الْأُمِّ يَتَوَارَثُونَ دُونَ بَنِي الْعَلَّاتِ، الرَّجُلُ يَرِثُ أَخَاهُ لِأَبِيهِ وَأُمِّهِ دُونَ أَخِيهِ لِأَبِيهِ» (سنن الترمذي رقم 2094)
وَفِي الْحَدِيثِ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ: «اشْتَرَيْتُ بَرِيرَةَ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ: اشْتَرِيهَا فَإِنَّ الْوَلَاءَ لِمَنْ أَعْتَقَ» (صحيح البخاري رقم 6751)
وَعَنْ عَلِيٍّ وَعَبْدِ اللَّهِ وَزَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ: أَنَّهُمْ كَانُوا يَجْعَلُونَ الْوَلَاءَ لِلْكُبْرِ مِنَ الْعَصَبَةِ، وَلَا يُوَرِّثُونَ النِّسَاءَ إِلَّا مَا أَعْتَقْنَ.
وَعَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ: كَانَ عُمَرُ وَعَلِيٌّ وَزَيْدُ بْنُ ثَابِتٍ لَا يُوَرِّثُونَ النِّسَاءَ مِنَ الْوَلَاءِ إِلَّا مَا أَعْتَقْنَ.
Chapter of the Nearest Asabah. He (the author) said, may Allah have mercy on him: The nearest of the asabah are the sons, then their sons, then the father, then the grandfather, then the brothers, then the sons of brothers, then the paternal uncles, then the sons of the paternal uncle, then the grandfather. And when two heirs are equal in degree, the one who is from both father and mother is nearest. And the son, and the son's son, and the brothers share with their sisters: for the male the share of two females. And whoever besides them from the asabah, their males take the inheritance exclusively, not their females. And if the deceased has no asabah from lineage, then the asabah is the manumitter (the master who freed him), then the nearest then the nearest from the asabah of the manumitter. The evidence of the verse: 'Allah instructs you concerning your children: for the male the share of two females' (An-Nisa 4:11). The evidence of the hadith: from Ibn Abbas from the Prophet (SAW) said: 'Give the fixed shares to those entitled to them, and whatever remains after the fixed shares is for the nearest male relative' (Bukhari no. 6746). And another hadith: from Ali that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) decreed that debt is prior to bequest, and that full brothers inherit from each other to the exclusion of half-brothers, a man inherits from his full brother, not his half-brother' (Tirmidhi no. 2094). And in the hadith: from Aisha: 'I bought Barirah, the Prophet said: Buy her, for the wala (right of inheritance through clientage) belongs to the one who frees' (Bukhari no. 6751). And from Ali, Abdullah, and Zaid bin Thabit: that they would give the wala to the eldest among the asabah, and would not let women inherit from wala except what they themselves freed. And from Ibrahim: Umar, Ali, and Zaid bin Thabit would not let women inherit from wala except what they themselves freed.
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is the matn of Al-Quduri on the chapter of the nearest asabah, followed by proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and sayings of the Companions, and explanatory usul. The matn establishes the order of residuary heirs (asabah) based on closeness of relationship: first sons, then their sons (i.e., grandsons), then father, then grandfather, then brothers (full and consanguine), then sons of brothers, then paternal uncles, then sons of paternal uncles, then the grandfather (i.e., higher grandfathers). When two residuary heirs are of the same degree (e.g., two paternal uncles), the one who is related through both father and mother (full) takes precedence over one related only through the father (consanguine).

The matn then gives the rule for males who inherit alongside their sisters: sons, sons' sons, and brothers (full and consanguine) share with their sisters in a 2:1 ratio (male takes twice the female's share). This is based on the Quranic verse (4:11) and the general principle of the asabah. However, other asabah (like uncles, cousins, etc.) do not share with their sisters; instead, the males take all inheritance and females get nothing. This is a key distinction: the sharing rule applies only to those who are in direct paternal lineage (sons and brothers) or their descendants.

If there is no asabah by blood relation, then the 'wala' (clientage) from freeing a slave creates an asabah relationship. The manumitter (master) becomes the asabah, and if he is deceased, then his asabah (by lineage) inherit in order of closeness. This is proven by the hadith of Barirah and the practice of the Companions (Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, Zaid ibn Thabit) that women do not inherit through wala except the one who herself freed a slave. The wala follows the rule that only males inherit through wala as asabah, unless a woman personally freed a slave, then she inherits as asabah.

The hadith about giving fixed shares first and then the remainder to the nearest male establishes the priority: Quranic sharers (ashab al-furud) take first, then asabah take what remains. This is a foundational principle in Hanafi inheritance law.

The usul explanations at the end clarify that asabah are relatives through the father, and they are of four types: asabah bi-nafsihi (by themselves, like sons), asabah bi-ghayrihi (by others, like daughters with sons), asabah ma'a ghayrihi (with others, like full sisters with daughters), and the rule of sharing applies only to certain categories.

Key Terms
عصبة (asabah): Residuary heirs who inherit after the Quranic sharers; they are male relatives through the father (or through wala).
ولاء (wala): The bond of clientage created by manumission; the freed slave's inheritance goes to the manumitter's asabah.
أقرب العصبات (aqrab al-asabat): The closest residuary heirs in order of precedence as listed: sons, grandsons, father, grandfather, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi order of asabah, which of the following is correct?
A) Grandfather takes precedence over full brother.
B) Full brother takes precedence over grandfather.
C) Full brother and grandfather share equally.
D) Neither; the uncle takes precedence.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi order of asabah is fixed: sons, then their sons, then father, then grandfather, then brothers; full siblings outrank half; sharing with sisters applies only to sons, grandsons, and brothers; wala fills in when no blood asabah exist.

The Mother's Exclusion: From One-Third to One-Sixth
Explains the mother's exclusion from 1/3 to 1/6 with Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of hajb nuqsan to reduce the mother's inheritance share from one-third to one-sixth in the presence of a child, grandchild, or two brothers, and cite the Quranic proof.

Core Idea
The mother's share drops to one-sixth if the deceased leaves a child, grandchild, or two brothers.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the mother's prescribed share is normally one-third. However, when certain close heirs exist, her share is reduced to one-sixth. This lesson unpacks the conditions for this reduction, the legal reasoning behind it, and the Quranic basis. Understanding this exclusion (hajb nuqsan) is essential for correctly distributing an estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs that cause exclusion
From the text, the mother's share is reduced by the presence of a child (son or daughter), a grandchild (son's child), or two brothers. Note: Brothers include both paternal and consanguine brothers in the Hanafi school.
If only one brother exists, the mother retains her one-third share.
2
Apply the rule of hajb nuqsan
When any of these heirs is present, the mother's share changes from 1/3 to 1/6. This is a partial reduction (nuqsan), not total exclusion (hirman). The mother still inherits.
Hajb nuqsan reduces the share, while hajb hirman bars the heir entirely.
3
Cite the Quranic proof
The ruling is derived from Surah an-Nisa 4:11: 'If he has brothers, then his mother has one-sixth.' The term 'brothers' is understood by the Hanafis to include two brothers (or one brother and one sister? Actually the text says two brothers).
The verse explicitly provides the condition for the reduction.
4
Differentiate between hajb types
The mother is not excluded completely; she still receives one-sixth. This contrasts with heirs like a uterine sibling who is totally excluded by a child. Understanding the distinction between hirman and nuqsan is key.
Some mistakenly think the mother is totally excluded; the text clarifies partial reduction.

Source Text

بَابُ الْحَجْبِ

قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - 1 وَتُخْجَبُ الأُمُّ مِنْ الثَّلُثِ إِلَى السُّدُسِ بِالْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ أَوْ بِأَخَوَيْنِ

ل وَ الْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ الْبَنَاتِ لِبَنِي الِابْنِ وَأَخَوَاتِهِمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ ل وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَتُحْجَبُ الْأُمُّ مِنْ الثَّلُثِ إِلَى السُّدُسِ وَلِأَبَوَيْهِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ مِمَّا تَرَكَ إِن كَانَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُ وَلَدٌ وَوَرِثَهُ أَبَوَاهُ فَلِأُمِّهِ الثُّلُثُ فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ مِنْ بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِي بِهَا أَوْدَيْنِ (سورة النساء، 4 أيت نمبر 11) وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ الْبَنَاتِ لِبَني الابْنِ \ عَنْ خَارِجَةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنِ الْوَلَدُ ذَكَرًا وَكَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَأَكْثَرَ مِنَ الْبَنَاتِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا ميراث لِبَنَاتِ الابْنِ مَعَهُنَّ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ بَنَاتِ الابْنِ ذَكَرْ هُوَ مِنَ الْمُتَوَفَّى مَنْزِلَتِهِنَّ، أَوْ هُوَ أَطْرَفُ مِنْهُنَّ، فَيَرُدُّ عَلَى مَنْ بِمَنْزِلَتِهِ وَمَنْ فَوْقَهُ مِنْ بَنَاتِ الْأَبْنَاءِ فَضْلًا إِنْ فَضَلَ، فَيُقَسِمُونَهُ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ} [النساء: 11] ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْضُلْ شَيْءٌ فَلَا شَيْءٍ لَهُمْ،(السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ أَوْلَادِ الِابْنِ، نمبر 12313)

..... وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَأَخَوَاتِهِمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الأُنْثَيَيْنِ فَتَفْسِيرُ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَلَى مَعَانِي زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ ...... فَإِنْ كَانَ بَنُو الْأُمَ وَالْآبِ امْرَأَتَيْنِ فَأَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْإِنَاثِ فَيُفْرَضُ هُنَّ الثَّلُثَانِ وَلَا مِيرَاثَ مَعَهُنَّ لِبَنَاتِ الْأَبِ، إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهُنَّ ذَكَرٌ مِنْ أَبِ، فَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَهُنَّ ذَكَرْ بُدِئَ بِفَرَائِضِ مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ فَرِيضَةٌ فَأَعْطُوهَا، فَإِنْ فَضَلَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فَضْلٌ كَانَ بَيْنَ بَنِي الْأَبِ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْضُلْ شَيْءٍ فَلَا شَيْءَ لَهُمْ "" (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مِيرَاتِ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ لِأَبِ وَأُمّ أَوْ لِأَبِ، نمبر 12326)

ج وجه:(۲) الآية لثبوت وَأَخَوَاتِهِمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ فَإِن كَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُمَا الثُّلُثَانِ مِمَّا تَرَكَ وَإِن كَانُوا إِخْوَةَ رِجَالًا وَنِسَاءَ فَلِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ يُبَيِّنُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ أَن تَضِلُّوا وَاللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ) (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 176)

اصول: اگر ماں کیسا تھ بیٹا، پوتا، دو بھائی نہ ہو تو ماں کو تہائی ملتا ہے ، اور ان کے موجودگی میں ماں مجوب ہو گی اور تہائی کے بجائے سدس یعنی چھٹا حصہ ملے گا۔
Chapter of Exclusion. He said - may Allah have mercy on him: The mother is excluded from one-third to one-sixth by a child, a child's child, or two brothers. And the residue after the prescribed share of daughters is for the sons of the son and their sisters: for the male a share like two females. Proof (1): the verse for establishing the mother's exclusion from one-third to one-sixth: 'And for his parents, each of them one-sixth of what he left if he has a child... if he has no child and his parents inherit him, then his mother has one-third. If he has brothers, then his mother has one-sixth...' (Quran 4:11). Proof (1): saying of the Companion for establishing that the residue after daughters' shares goes to sons of the son: from Kharija ibn Zaid from his father Zaid ibn Thabit: 'If there is no male child and there are two or more daughters, then the sons' daughters have no inheritance with them unless there is a male with them... then they divide the residue for the male a share like two females.' (Bayhaqi). Proof (1): saying of the Companion for establishing the ruling for brothers and sisters: from Abu al-Zinad's interpretation of Zaid ibn Thabit's rulings: 'If there are two or more females from the same mother and father, they get two-thirds, and the daughters of the father have no inheritance with them unless there is a male with them from the father... then the residue is divided among the children of the father for the male a share like two females.' (Bayhaqi). Proof (2): the verse for brothers and sisters: 'If they are two females, they have two-thirds... if they are brothers and sisters, for the male a share like two females' (Quran 4:176). Principle: If the mother has no son, grandson, or two brothers, she gets one-third. With their presence, the mother is excluded (from one-third) and gets one-sixth instead.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on exclusion (hajb) in inheritance. The author states two rulings: first, the mother's share is reduced from one-third to one-sixth when the deceased has a child, grandchild, or two brothers (paternal or maternal? In Hanafi law, two brothers mean two paternal or consanguine brothers, but the text says 'brothers' generally). Second, after the daughters take their prescribed share (one-half for one daughter, two-thirds for two or more), the residue goes to the sons of the son and their sisters, with the male taking double the female. The text provides Quranic proof from 4:11 for the mother's exclusion, and from 4:176 for the sibling ratio. Additionally, statements of Zaid ibn Thabit (recorded by Bayhaqi) clarify that when there are daughters, the sons' daughters only inherit if a male descendant (like a grandson) is present to make them agnates; otherwise they are excluded. Similarly, for siblings, if there are multiple sisters from the same parents, they get two-thirds, and half-sisters (from father) only inherit if a male half-brother is present. The Urdu principle summarizes: the mother gets one-third only in the absence of a son, grandson, or two brothers; with their presence, she is excluded from one-third and gets one-sixth.

Key Terms
حَجْب (hajb): Exclusion or reduction of an heir's share due to the presence of a closer or more entitled heir.
نُقْصَان (nuqsan): Partial reduction of an heir's share (not total exclusion).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
The mother inherits one-sixth instead of one-third in the presence of which of the following?
A) A husband and a daughter.
B) A son, a grandson, or two brothers.
C) A father and a mother.
D) Only a daughter.

Key Takeaway
The mother's share is never less than one-sixth; it is reduced from one-third to one-sixth only by a child, grandchild, or two brothers.

8 min
Residue After Daughters Goes to Sons of the Son
Explains the allocation of residue after daughters to sons of the son with proof from Zaid ibn Thabit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule that the residue after the daughters' prescribed shares goes to the sons of the son (and their sisters) with the male taking twice the female, and identify when sons' daughters are excluded.

Core Idea
The residue after daughters' shares belongs to the sons of the son, not to the daughters themselves.

When a deceased person leaves daughters, they receive their fixed shares, but the remaining estate does not automatically go to them. Instead, Hanafi law directs the residue to the sons of the son (and their sisters) as residuary heirs. This lesson explains the rule, its proof from the practice of Zaid ibn Thabit, and key conditions such as the presence of a male descendant for the sons' daughters to inherit.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario: daughters present
When the deceased leaves one or more daughters (but no sons), the daughters receive their prescribed shares: 1/2 for one daughter, 2/3 for two or more daughters. The remaining estate is called 'al-fadil 'an fard al-banat'.
If there are both sons and daughters, the sons are residuary heirs, so the residue goes to them, not to grandsons.
2
Calculate the residue after daughters' shares
Take the total estate, subtract the daughters' fixed shares. The remainder is the residue. For example, with one daughter, residue = 1/2; with two daughters, residue = 1/3.
If the residue is zero, there is nothing for grandsons.
3
Allocate residue to sons of the son
The residue goes to the sons of the son (i.e., grandchildren through the son) and, if present, their sisters. The sons of the son take a share double that of their sisters, just like regular ta'sib rules.
Sons of the son are asabah (residuary heirs) when there are daughters but no sons.
4
Recognize the condition for sons' daughters
If only daughters of the son (granddaughters through the son) exist without a male descendant of similar degree, they are excluded (hajb hirman) by the daughters of the deceased. Only if a male grandson (son of the son) is present do they become residuary heirs along with him.
This is derived from the saying of Zaid ibn Thabit in the text.
5
Cite the proof from the Companion's practice
The text quotes Zaid ibn Thabit: 'If there is no male child and there are two or more daughters, then the sons' daughters have no inheritance with them unless there is a male with them... then they divide the residue for the male a share like two females.' (Bayhaqi).
This establishes the ruling through the practice of a Companion, accepted as proof (qawl sahabi) in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْحَجْبِ

قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - 1 وَتُخْجَبُ الأُمُّ مِنْ الثَّلُثِ إِلَى السُّدُسِ بِالْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ أَوْ بِأَخَوَيْنِ

ل وَ الْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ الْبَنَاتِ لِبَنِي الِابْنِ وَأَخَوَاتِهِمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ ل وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَتُحْجَبُ الْأُمُّ مِنْ الثَّلُثِ إِلَى السُّدُسِ وَلِأَبَوَيْهِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ مِمَّا تَرَكَ إِن كَانَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُ وَلَدٌ وَوَرِثَهُ أَبَوَاهُ فَلِأُمِّهِ الثُّلُثُ فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ مِنْ بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِي بِهَا أَوْدَيْنِ (سورة النساء، 4 أيت نمبر 11) وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ الْبَنَاتِ لِبَني الابْنِ \ عَنْ خَارِجَةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنِ الْوَلَدُ ذَكَرًا وَكَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَأَكْثَرَ مِنَ الْبَنَاتِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا ميراث لِبَنَاتِ الابْنِ مَعَهُنَّ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ بَنَاتِ الابْنِ ذَكَرْ هُوَ مِنَ الْمُتَوَفَّى مَنْزِلَتِهِنَّ، أَوْ هُوَ أَطْرَفُ مِنْهُنَّ، فَيَرُدُّ عَلَى مَنْ بِمَنْزِلَتِهِ وَمَنْ فَوْقَهُ مِنْ بَنَاتِ الْأَبْنَاءِ فَضْلًا إِنْ فَضَلَ، فَيُقَسِمُونَهُ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ} [النساء: 11] ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْضُلْ شَيْءٌ فَلَا شَيْءٍ لَهُمْ،(السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ أَوْلَادِ الِابْنِ، نمبر 12313)

..... وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَأَخَوَاتِهِمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الأُنْثَيَيْنِ فَتَفْسِيرُ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَلَى مَعَانِي زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ ...... فَإِنْ كَانَ بَنُو الْأُمَ وَالْآبِ امْرَأَتَيْنِ فَأَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ مِنَ الْإِنَاثِ فَيُفْرَضُ هُنَّ الثَّلُثَانِ وَلَا مِيرَاثَ مَعَهُنَّ لِبَنَاتِ الْأَبِ، إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَهُنَّ ذَكَرٌ مِنْ أَبِ، فَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَهُنَّ ذَكَرْ بُدِئَ بِفَرَائِضِ مَنْ كَانَتْ لَهُ فَرِيضَةٌ فَأَعْطُوهَا، فَإِنْ فَضَلَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فَضْلٌ كَانَ بَيْنَ بَنِي الْأَبِ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْضُلْ شَيْءٍ فَلَا شَيْءَ لَهُمْ "" (السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ مِيرَاتِ الْإِخْوَةِ وَالْأَخَوَاتِ لِأَبِ وَأُمّ أَوْ لِأَبِ، نمبر 12326)

ج وجه:(۲) الآية لثبوت وَأَخَوَاتِهِمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ فَإِن كَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُمَا الثُّلُثَانِ مِمَّا تَرَكَ وَإِن كَانُوا إِخْوَةَ رِجَالًا وَنِسَاءَ فَلِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ يُبَيِّنُ اللَّهُ لَكُمْ أَن تَضِلُّوا وَاللَّهُ بِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ عَلِيمٌ) (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 176)

اصول: اگر ماں کیسا تھ بیٹا، پوتا، دو بھائی نہ ہو تو ماں کو تہائی ملتا ہے ، اور ان کے موجودگی میں ماں مجوب ہو گی اور تہائی کے بجائے سدس یعنی چھٹا حصہ ملے گا۔
Chapter of Exclusion. He said - may Allah have mercy on him: The mother is excluded from one-third to one-sixth by a child, a child's child, or two brothers. And the residue after the prescribed share of daughters is for the sons of the son and their sisters: for the male a share like two females. Proof (1): the verse for establishing the mother's exclusion from one-third to one-sixth: 'And for his parents, each of them one-sixth of what he left if he has a child... if he has no child and his parents inherit him, then his mother has one-third. If he has brothers, then his mother has one-sixth...' (Quran 4:11). Proof (1): saying of the Companion for establishing that the residue after daughters' shares goes to sons of the son: from Kharija ibn Zaid from his father Zaid ibn Thabit: 'If there is no male child and there are two or more daughters, then the sons' daughters have no inheritance with them unless there is a male with them... then they divide the residue for the male a share like two females.' (Bayhaqi). Proof (1): saying of the Companion for establishing the ruling for brothers and sisters: from Abu al-Zinad's interpretation of Zaid ibn Thabit's rulings: 'If there are two or more females from the same mother and father, they get two-thirds, and the daughters of the father have no inheritance with them unless there is a male with them from the father... then the residue is divided among the children of the father for the male a share like two females.' (Bayhaqi). Proof (2): the verse for brothers and sisters: 'If they are two females, they have two-thirds... if they are brothers and sisters, for the male a share like two females' (Quran 4:176). Principle: If the mother has no son, grandson, or two brothers, she gets one-third. With their presence, the mother is excluded (from one-third) and gets one-sixth instead.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on exclusion (hajb) in inheritance. The author states two rulings: first, the mother's share is reduced from one-third to one-sixth when the deceased has a child, grandchild, or two brothers (paternal or maternal? In Hanafi law, two brothers mean two paternal or consanguine brothers, but the text says 'brothers' generally). Second, after the daughters take their prescribed share (one-half for one daughter, two-thirds for two or more), the residue goes to the sons of the son and their sisters, with the male taking double the female. The text provides Quranic proof from 4:11 for the mother's exclusion, and from 4:176 for the sibling ratio. Additionally, statements of Zaid ibn Thabit (recorded by Bayhaqi) clarify that when there are daughters, the sons' daughters only inherit if a male descendant (like a grandson) is present to make them agnates; otherwise they are excluded. Similarly, for siblings, if there are multiple sisters from the same parents, they get two-thirds, and half-sisters (from father) only inherit if a male half-brother is present. The Urdu principle summarizes: the mother gets one-third only in the absence of a son, grandson, or two brothers; with their presence, she is excluded from one-third and gets one-sixth.

Key Terms
الْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ الْبَنَاتِ (al-fadil 'an fard al-banat): The residue of the estate after the daughters have taken their prescribed share (one-half or two-thirds).
تَعْصِيب (ta'sib): The principle of residuary inheritance where male agnates take the remaining estate after prescribed shares are given.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A deceased woman leaves two daughters and a son's son (grandson). How is the estate divided?
A) Two daughters get everything; grandson excluded.
B) Two daughters get 2/3, grandson gets 1/3.
C) Two daughters get 2/3, and the residue returns to them (radd), so they get all.
D) Two daughters get 1/2 each, grandson gets nothing.

Key Takeaway
The residue after daughters' shares always goes to the nearest male agnates, beginning with the sons of the son, even if daughters are present.

Hajb of the Mother and Inheritance of Grandchildren
States two inheritance rules with Quranic and companion proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two rulings on mother's hajb and surplus distribution to grandchildren, and apply them to inheritance scenarios.

Core Idea
Mother gets 1/6 if child, grandchild, or two brothers exist; surplus after daughters goes to grandchildren as asabah (2:1 male:female).

This passage from al-Quduri's matn presents two key inheritance rules in the chapter of hajb. First, conditions that reduce the mother's share from one-third to one-sixth. Second, what happens to the residue after daughters take their fixed shares—it goes to grandchildren in a specific ratio. Both rules are supported by the Quran and the companion Zayd ibn Thabit. We will examine these rules and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and locate the two separate rulings: (A) hajb of the mother and (B) surplus for grandchildren.
The ruling on the mother is based on Quran 4:11; the ruling on grandchildren is based on the saying of Zayd ibn Thabit.
2
Analyze the condition for mother's hajb
List the heirs that cause the mother's share to drop from 1/3 to 1/6: a child (son or daughter), a son's child (grandchild), or two brothers. Note that the brothers must be full or consanguine in the Hanafi school.
The text simply says 'أخوين' (two brothers); the Hanafi interpretation restricts to full/consanguine.
3
Understand the surplus rule
After daughters receive their prescribed shares (1/2 or 2/3), the remaining surplus goes to the children of the son (grandchildren) as asabah, with the male taking twice the female's share.
This applies only if there are no direct sons of the deceased.
4
Examine the proofs
The Quranic verse (4:11) provides the basis for the mother's hajb by 'إخوة' (brothers). The saying of Zayd ibn Thabit (via his son Kharijah) establishes the surplus rule for grandchildren.
The companion saying is in Sunan al-Bayhaqi, considered a reliable source in Hanafi fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْحَجْبِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - وَتُحْجَبُ الأُمُّ مِنْ الثَّلُثِ إِلَى السُّدُسِ بِالْوَلَدِ أَوْ وَلَدِ الِابْنِ أَوْ بِأَخَوَيْنِ
وَالْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ الْبَنَاتِ لِبَنِي الِابْنِ وَأَخَوَاتِهِمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ
وَجْهٌ: (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَتُحْجَبُ الْأُمُّ مِنْ الثَّلُثِ إِلَى السُّدُسِ ﴿وَلِأَبَوَيْهِ لِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ مِمَّا تَرَكَ إِن كَانَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُ وَلَدٌ وَوَرِثَهُ أَبَوَاهُ فَلِأُمِّهِ الثُّلُثُ فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ مِن بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِي بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 آيت نمبر 11). وَجْهٌ: (2) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَالْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ الْبَنَاتِ لِبَنِي الِابْنِ، عَنْ خَارِجَةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ: وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنِ الْوَلَدُ ذَكَرًا وَكَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَأَكْثَرَ مِنَ الْبَنَاتِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا مِيرَاثَ لِبَنَاتِ الِابْنِ مَعَهُنَّ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ مَعَ بَنَاتِ الِابْنِ ذَكَرٌ هُوَ مِمَّنْ لَوْ كَانَ مَعَ الْمُتَوَفَّى مَنْزِلَتِهِنَّ، أَوْ هُوَ أَطْرَفُ مِنْهُنَّ، فَيَرُدُّ عَلَى مَنْ بِمَنْزِلَتِهِ وَمَنْ فَوْقَهُ مِنْ بَنَاتِ الْأَبْنَاءِ فَضْلًا إِنْ فَضَلَ، فَيُقَسِّمُونَهُ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْضُلْ شَيْءٌ فَلَا شَيْءَ لَهُمْ. (السَّنَنُ الْكُبْرَى لِلْبَيْهَقِيِّ، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ أَوْلَادِ الِابْنِ، رقم 12313)
أُصُولٌ: اگر ماں کے تین بیٹا، پوتا، دو بھائی نہ ہو تو ماں کو تہائی ملتا ہے، اور ان کے موجودگی میں ماں محجوب ہو گی اور تہائی کے بجائے سدس یعنی چھٹا حصہ ملے گا۔
Chapter of Exclusion. He said - may Allah have mercy on him - the mother is excluded from the third to the sixth by a child, a son's child, or two brothers. And the surplus from the prescribed share of the daughters goes to the sons' sons and their sisters: for the male the share of two females. Proof: (1) The verse for establishing that the mother is excluded from the third to the sixth: 'And for his parents, for each one of them a sixth of what he left, if he has a child; if he does not have a child and his parents inherit him, then for his mother a third; if he has brothers, then for his mother a sixth after any bequest he bequeaths or debt.' (Surah An-Nisa, verse 11). Proof: (2) The saying of the Companion for establishing the surplus: from Kharijah ibn Zayd, from his father Zayd ibn Thabit: 'If the child is not male and there are two or more daughters, then the granddaughters (daughters of the son) have no inheritance with them unless there is with the granddaughters a male who is at their station or closer in relation to the deceased, then he returns upon those at his station and those above them from the granddaughters a surplus if there is surplus, and they divide it for the male the share of two females. If nothing remains, then nothing for them.' (Sunan al-Kubra lil-Bayhaqi, Chapter on Inheritance of Children of the Son, no. 12313). Principle: If the mother does not have a son, grandson, or two brothers, she receives one-third. In their presence, the mother is excluded (to one-sixth) and instead of one-third gets one-sixth.
Source pages p. 445

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from the chapter on exclusion (hajb) in inheritance. First, the mother's share is reduced from one-third (her default share when no children) to one-sixth when certain heirs exist: a child (son or daughter), a son's child (grandchild), or two brothers of the deceased. This is based on Quran 4:11 which explicitly states that if the deceased has brothers, the mother gets one-sixth. Second, when there are daughters who receive their prescribed shares (half for one, two-thirds for two or more), any surplus residue goes to the children of the son (grandchildren) as asabah (residuary heirs). The distribution follows the rule 'for the male the share of two females,' meaning a son's son takes twice the share of a son's daughter. This ruling is supported by the practice of Zayd ibn Thabit, as narrated by his son Kharijah. The Urdu summary at the end reiterates the first ruling: if the mother has no son, grandson, or two brothers, she takes one-third; otherwise, she is reduced to one-sixth.

Key Terms
حَجْب (hajb): Exclusion from inheritance or reduction of share due to the presence of a closer heir.
الْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ الْبَنَاتِ (al-faadil 'an fard al-banat): The surplus remaining after the daughters have taken their prescribed shares (1/2 or 2/3).
أَخَوَيْنِ (akhawain): Two brothers of the deceased (presumably full or consanguine in standard Hanafi fiqh).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following heirs reduces the mother's share from 1/3 to 1/6?
A) Three maternal sisters
B) Two brothers of the deceased
C) One son and one daughter
D) A grandson (son's son)

Key Takeaway
The mother's default 1/3 is reduced to 1/6 by a child, grandchild, or two full/consanguine brothers; after daughters, the residue goes to grandchildren as asabah with a 2:1 ratio.

Two Inheritance Cases: Daughter with Grandchildren, and Two Cousins with a Maternal Brother
Two inheritance distributions with Quranic and companion proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares for two Hanafi faraid scenarios: a daughter with grandchildren from a predeceased son, and two male cousins where one is a maternal brother, applying Quranic prescribed shares and asabah distribution.

Core Idea
In Hanafi faraid, a person may inherit through multiple relationships, receiving separate shares for each.

This passage from al-Quduri presents two specific inheritance cases that illustrate key principles of Hanafi faraid: the distribution of residue to grandchildren as asabah when a daughter is present, and the dual inheritance of a maternal brother who is also a cousin. By studying these cases, you will learn how to allocate prescribed shares and then divide the residue according to the rules of asabah, including the 2:1 male-to-female ratio.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs in each case
For the first case, the deceased leaves a daughter, granddaughters (daughters of a predeceased son), and grandsons (sons of the predeceased son). For the second case, the deceased leaves two male cousins, one of whom is also a maternal brother.
2
Apply the Quranic prescribed shares
From Quran 4:11, the sole daughter receives 1/2. From Quran 4:12, a maternal sibling receives 1/6 if alone.
In the first case, granddaughters do not get a prescribed share when there is a male among them.
3
Distribute the residue (asabah)
After the prescribed shares are taken, the remainder goes to the nearest male agnatic relatives. In case 1, it goes to the sons of the son and their sisters in a 2:1 ratio. In case 2, the residue after the maternal brother's 1/6 is divided equally between the two cousins as asabah.
In case 2, the maternal brother also participates in the residue because he is also a cousin.
4
Calculate the final shares
Compute the fractions: Case 1: Daughter 1/2, grandchildren (as asabah) the other half divided 2:1. Case 2: Maternal brother gets 1/6, then the remaining 5/6 is split equally between the two cousins, so each gets 5/12. The maternal brother total = 1/6 + 5/12 = 7/12; the other cousin gets 5/12.
Verify the total sums to 1.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا تَرَكَ بِنْتًا وَبَنَاتِ ابْنٍ وَبَنِي ابْنٍ فَلِلْبِنْتِ النِّصْفُ وَالْبَاقِي لِبَنِي الِابْنِ وَأَخَوَاتِهِمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ. وَمَنْ تَرَكَ ابْنَيْ عَمٍّ أَحَدُهُمَا أَخٌ لِأُمٍّ فَلِلْأَخِ مِنَ الْأُمِّ السُّدُسُ وَالْبَاقِي بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَانِ.
وَجْهٌ: (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا تَرَكَ بِنْتًا وَبَنَاتِ ابْنٍ وَبَنِي ابْنٍ ﴿فَإِن كُنَّ نِسَاءً فَوْقَ اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُنَّ ثُلُثَا مَا تَرَكَ وَإِن كَانَتْ وَاحِدَةً فَلَهَا النِّصْفُ﴾ [سورة النساء، 4:11]. وَجْهٌ: (2) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا تَرَكَ بِنْتًا وَبَنَاتِ ابْنٍ وَبَنِي ابْنٍ فَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَ بَنَاتِ الِابْنِ ذَكَرٌ هُوَ بِمَنْزِلَتِهِنَّ فَلَا سُدُسَ لَهُنَّ وَلَا فَرِيضَةَ، وَلَكِنْ إِنْ فَضَلَ فَضْلٌ بَعْدَ فَرِيضَةِ أَهْلِ الْفَرَائِضِ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الْفَضْلُ لِذَلِكَ الذَّكَرِ وَلِمَنْ بِمَنْزِلَتِهِ مِنَ الْإِنَاثِ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ، وَلَيْسَ لِمَنْ هُوَ أَطْرَفُ مِنْهُنَّ شَيْءٌ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْضُلْ شَيْءٌ فَلَا شَيْءَ لَهُنَّ. (السَّنَنُ الْكُبْرَى لِلْبَيْهَقِيِّ، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ أَوْلَادِ الِابْنِ، رقم 12313)
وَجْهٌ: (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ تَرَكَ ابْنَيْ عَمٍّ أَحَدُهُمَا أَخٌ لِأُمٍّ ﴿وَإِن كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلَالَةً أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ وَلَهُ أَخٌ أَوْ أُخْتٌ فَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ فَإِن كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلُثِ﴾ [سورة النساء، 4:12].
أُصُولٌ: کسی شخص کی دو قرابتیں مجتمع ہوں تو دو الگ الگ حصے ملیں گے۔
If he leaves a daughter, daughters of a son, and sons of a son, then for the daughter is half, and the remainder is for the sons of the son and their sisters: for the male the share of two females. And whoever leaves two male cousins, one of whom is a maternal brother, then for the maternal brother is one-sixth, and the remainder is shared equally between them. Proof: (1) The verse for establishing: 'If they are women above two, then for them two-thirds of what he left, and if there is one, then for her half.' (An-Nisa 4:11). Proof: (2) The saying of the Companion: from Zayd ibn Thabit: 'If there is with the granddaughters a male who is at their station, then they have no sixth and no prescribed share; but if there is a surplus after the prescribed shares of the heirs, that surplus goes to that male and to those females at his station, for the male the share of two females; and nothing for those below them. If nothing remains, then nothing for them.' (Sunan al-Kubra, no. 12313). Proof: (1) The verse for establishing: 'And if a man who is inherited (i.e., dies) as kalala or a woman, and he has a brother or a sister, then for each one of them a sixth; if they are more than that, then they are partners in a third.' (An-Nisa 4:12). Principle: If a person has two relationships (with the deceased), he will receive two separate shares.
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage covers two inheritance scenarios. First, if the deceased leaves one daughter and grandchildren from a son: the daughter receives her prescribed half (1/2). The residue (the other half) goes to the sons of the son and their sisters (granddaughters) as asabah, with the male taking twice the female's share. This is supported by Quran 4:11, which gives the daughter half, and the practice of Zayd ibn Thabit, who ruled that grandchildren take the residue only if there is a male among them. If only granddaughters exist, they get nothing if there are two or more daughters. Second, if the deceased leaves two male cousins, one of whom is also a maternal brother (i.e., the mother's son from a different father), then the maternal brother takes his prescribed share of one-sixth from the Quran (4:12), and the remainder (five-sixths) is divided equally between the two cousins as asabah (since they are equally distant in relation). The Urdu principle states that if a person has two relationships to the deceased, he may receive shares from both capacities. Here, the maternal brother inherits both as a maternal sibling (1/6) and as a cousin (asabah).

Key Terms
ابْنَا عَمٍّ (ibna 'amm): Two male cousins (sons of the deceased's paternal uncle).
أَخٌ لِأُمٍّ (akhun li-umm): A maternal brother (shares the same mother but different father).
الْفَاضِلُ (al-faadil): The residue after prescribed shares are given.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where a person leaves two male cousins, one of whom is also a maternal brother, what does the maternal brother receive?
A) Only one-sixth as a maternal brother
B) One-sixth as a maternal brother plus half of the residue as a cousin
C) Nothing because he is a maternal relative
D) The entire estate because he is both

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, a person may inherit through multiple relationships, receiving separate shares for each, as demonstrated by the maternal brother who inherits both as a sharer and as an asabah cousin.

Inheritance of Daughter and Grandchildren through Son
Ruling on daughter's half and grandsons' residue

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the shares of a daughter and grandchildren (from a son) in a Hanafi faraid case, applying the rules of asabah and the male-double-female principle.

Core Idea
The daughter takes her fixed half; the residual goes to the son's children with male taking double female.

This lesson examines a classic inheritance scenario from al-Quduri: a deceased leaving a daughter and grandchildren from a son. The passage provides the ruling and proofs. You'll learn how to allocate the shares step by step, understanding the interplay between Quranic fixed shares and residuary inheritance.

Guided Path
1
List all surviving heirs
Identify the daughter, son's daughters, and son's sons. Note that the son's children are considered descendants (asabah) when no direct male descendant exists.
2
Assign the Quranic share to the daughter
Apply the ruling from Surah An-Nisa 4:11: if only one daughter, she receives half (1/2). This is fard (fixed share).
3
Determine the residue and asabah
After the daughter's half, the remaining half is the residue. According to the Hanafi school, the son's children inherit this residue as asabah (residuary heirs).
4
Divide the residue among grandchildren
The residue is distributed among the son's sons and daughters with the male taking twice the share of the female (like the rule for siblings in Surah An-Nisa 4:176). This is valid when a male of equal rank is present.
5
Verify with the proofs
The passage cites the Quranic verses and the saying of Ibn Mas'ud. Confirm that the daughter's half is based on 4:11 and the grandchildren's residuary status is supported by analogy with 4:176 and the Companion's statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْحَجْبِ
وَإِذَا تَرَكَ بِنْتًا وَبَنَاتِ ابْنٍ وَبَنِي ابْنٍ فَلِلْبِنْتِ النِّصْفُ وَالْبَاقِي لِبَنِي الِابْنِ وَأَخَوَاتِهِمْ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ
وَجْهٌ (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: ﴿فَإِن كُنَّ نِسَاءً فَوْقَ اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُنَّ ثُلُثَا مَا تَرَكَ وَإِن كَانَتْ وَاحِدَةً فَلَهَا النِّصْفُ﴾ [سورة النساء، 4:11]
وَجْهٌ (2) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ: عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: «فَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَ بَنَاتِ الِابْنِ ذَكَرٌ هُوَ بِمَنْزِلَتِهِنَّ فَلَا سُدُسَ لَهُنَّ وَلَا فَرِيضَةَ، وَلَكِنْ إِنْ فَضَلَ فَضْلٌ بَعْدَ فَرِيضَةِ أَهْلِ الْفَرَائِضِ كَانَ ذَلِكَ الْفَضْلُ لِذَلِكَ الذَّكَرِ وَلِمَنْ بِمَنْزِلَتِهِ مِنَ الْإِنَاثِ لِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنْثَيَيْنِ، وَلَيْسَ لِمَنْ هُوَ أَطْرَفُ مِنْهُنَّ شَيْءٌ، فَإِنْ لَمْ يَفْضُلْ شَيْءٌ فَلَا شَيْءَ لَهُنَّ» [رَوَاهُ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ فِي السُّنَنِ الْكُبْرَى، بَابُ مِيرَاثِ أَوْلَادِ الِابْنِ، رَقْم 12313]
وَجْهٌ (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ تَوْرِيثِ بَنِي الِابْنِ وَأَخَوَاتِهِمْ: ﴿يَسْتَفْتُونَكَ قُلِ اللَّهُ يُفْتِيكُمْ فِي الْكَلَالَةِ إِنِ امْرُؤٌ هَلَكَ لَيْسَ لَهُ وَلَدٌ وَلَهُ أُخْتٌ فَلَهَا نِصْفُ مَا تَرَكَ وَهُوَ يَرِثُهَا إِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهَا وَلَدٌ فَإِن كَانَتَا اثْنَتَيْنِ فَلَهُمَا الثُّلُثَانِ مِمَّا تَرَكَ وَإِن كَانُوا إِخْوَةً رِجَالًا وَنِسَاءً فَلِلذَّكَرِ مِثْلُ حَظِّ الْأُنثَيَيْنِ﴾ [سورة النساء، 4:176]
وَجْهٌ (2) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ: عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ نَحْوُهُ [الْبَيْهَقِيُّ]
Chapter of Exclusion. And if one leaves a daughter and granddaughters (son's daughters) and grandsons (son's sons), then the daughter gets half, and the remainder goes to the sons of the son and their sisters, for the male the like of the portion of two females. Proof (1) the verse for establishing that: 'If they are women above two, then for them two-thirds of what he left, and if one, then for her half' [4:11]. Proof (2) the saying of the Companion: from Ibn Mas'ud who said: 'If there is with the daughters of the son a male who is of their rank, then there is no sixth for them nor a prescribed share, but if there remains a surplus after the prescribed shares of the heirs, then that surplus is for that male and for those females of his rank, for the male the like of the portion of two females, and there is nothing for those who are more distant than them; if nothing remains, then nothing for them' [al-Bayhaqi]. Proof (1) the verse for establishing the inheritance of the sons of the son and their sisters: 'They ask you for a ruling; say: God gives you a ruling concerning the kalalah. If a man dies having no child and he has a sister, then for her half of what he left, and he inherits from her if she has no child; if there are two, then for them two-thirds of what he left; if they are brothers and sisters, men and women, then for the male the like of the portion of two females' [4:176]. Proof (2) the saying of the Companion: from Ibn Mas'ud similar [al-Bayhaqi].
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of al-Quduri on inheritance in the chapter of hajb (exclusion). The scenario: a deceased leaves a daughter, along with granddaughters and grandsons from a son. The daughter receives her Quranic half (1/2). The residue is given to the son's children, with the male taking twice the female's share, treating them as asabah (residuary heirs). The author then provides proofs: first, the Quranic verse (4:11) establishing the half for the single daughter; second, the saying of Ibn Mas'ud (a Companion) clarifying that the son's children are not entitled to a fixed share but take what remains after other fixed shares; third, the kalalah verse (4:176) analogically supporting the principle of male receiving double the female; and fourth, another similar report from Ibn Mas'ud. This ruling follows the Hanafi position: the daughter's half is fard, and the residue to the son's children is asabah, which is obligatory to distribute. The authority weight is from the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
حَجْب (hajb): Exclusion of certain heirs from inheritance due to the presence of others closer in relation or of higher priority.
بَنُو الِابْن (banu al-ibn): Sons of the deceased's son, i.e., grandsons through the male line. They inherit as asabah when there is no direct male descendant.
عَصَبَة (asabah): Residuary heirs who take the surplus after Quranic shares are distributed; they inherit by virtue of male agnatic relation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the share of the daughter when she is the only daughter and there are grandchildren through a son?
A) Two-thirds
B) Half
C) One-sixth
D) The residue

Key Takeaway
When a daughter and grandchildren (via son) survive, the daughter takes her fixed half, and the residue goes to the grandchildren as asabah with male taking double the female's share.

The Dual Capacity Heir: Uterine Brother and Paternal Cousin
Ruling on dual capacity in inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the inheritance shares when a uterine brother is also a paternal cousin, applying the Hanafi rule of multiple capacities.

Core Idea
A dual-relation heir inherits through each capacity separately: first as a Quranic heir, then as an agnate.

Who inherits when a person leaves two paternal cousins, but one of them is also a uterine brother? The Hanafi school recognizes that the same person can inherit through two different relations, receiving a Quranic share as a sibling and then sharing the residue as an agnate. This lesson walks through the ruling, its proofs from the Quran and Companion practice, and the disagreement with an earlier view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Heirs and Their Relations
In this case, the deceased leaves two paternal cousins (ibnay 'amm). One of them is also a uterine brother (akh li-umm). No other heirs exist. Write down both relations for the dual cousin.
The dual cousin is both a Quranic heir (uterine brother) and an agnate (paternal cousin).
2
Apply the Quranic Share for Uterine Sibling
According to Quran 4:12, a single uterine brother inherits one-sixth (1/6). This is a fixed share. Allocate 1/6 to the uterine brother from the total estate.
The verse applies to siblings from the mother's side, male or female, each gets 1/6 if alone.
3
Determine the Residue and Asabah Distribution
After the Quranic share, the remaining estate (5/6) is divided equally between the two paternal cousins, as they are equal asabah. The dual cousin takes his share of the residue in addition to his 1/6.
Hanafi law treats paternal cousins as agnates; when equal in degree, they inherit equally per capita.
4
Calculate the Final Shares
Let total estate be 12 units for easy math. Uterine brother gets 1/6 = 2 units. Residue = 10 units, divided equally: each cousin gets 5 units. The dual cousin totals 2+5=7 units; the other cousin gets 5 units.
Thus, dual cousin receives 7/12, other cousin receives 5/12 of the estate.
5
Recognize the Dispute and the Hanafi Tarjih
Ibn Mas'ud gave the entire estate to the uterine brother, ignoring the paternal cousin. The Hanafi school follows 'Ali and Zaid, giving the uterine brother only his Quranic share and then sharing residue. This is the mufta bihi.
The key principle: a person inherits through multiple capacities, and each relation gives a separate entitlement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ تَرَكَ ابْنَيْ عَمٍّ أَحَدُهُمَا أَخٌ لِأُمٍّ فَلِلْأَخِ مِنَ الْأُمِّ السُّدُسُ وَالْبَاقِي بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَانِ
وَجْهٌ (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: ﴿وَإِن كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلَالَةً أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ وَلَهُ أَخٌ أَوْ أُخْتٌ فَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ فَإِن كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلُثِ﴾ [سورة النساء، 4:12]
وَجْهٌ (2) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ قَالَ: كَانَ عَلِيٌّ وَزَيْدٌ يَقُولَانِ فِي بَنِي عَمٍّ أَحَدُهُمْ أَخٌ لِأُمٍّ: «يُعْطِيَانِهِ السُّدُسَ، وَمَا بَقِيَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ بَنِي عَمِّهِ»، وَكَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ «يُعْطِيهِ الْمَالَ كُلَّهُ» [مُصَنَّفُ ابْنِ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ، فِي بَنِي عَمٍّ أَحَدُهُمْ أَخٌ لِأُمٍّ، رَقْم 31086]
And who leaves two paternal cousins, one of them being a uterine brother, then for the uterine brother is one-sixth, and the remainder between them is half and half. Proof (1) the verse for establishing that: 'If a man is inherited kalalah or a woman, and he has a brother or a sister, then for each one of them is one-sixth; if they are more than that, then they are partners in one-third' [4:12]. Proof (2) the saying of the Tabi'i: from al-Sha'bi who said: 'Ali and Zaid used to say concerning paternal cousins one of whom is a uterine brother: they give him one-sixth, and what remains is between him and his paternal cousin; and Abdullah used to give him the entire wealth' [Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah].
Source pages p. 446

Commentary
This lesson presents a second ruling in the chapter of hajb. The case: two paternal cousins (ibnay 'amm) survive, but one of them is also a uterine brother (akh li-umm) of the deceased. The ruling: the cousin who is also a uterine brother receives one-sixth as his uterine brother share, and the remainder is divided equally between the two cousins (since as paternal cousins they are equal in degree and asabah). The proof is from the kalalah verse (4:12) which gives siblings through the mother one-sixth each or one-third collectively. The second proof is the practice of 'Ali and Zaid (Companions) who gave the uterine brother his share and then divided the residue equally with the other cousin, while Ibn Mas'ud gave the whole to the uterine brother (as the nearest relative). The Hanafi position follows 'Ali and Zaid: the person inherits through his dual capacity, taking the uterine share first and then sharing as a paternal cousin in the residue. This illustrates the principle that when two relations combine, two separate shares are given.

Key Terms
ابْنَا عَم (ibnay 'amm): Two paternal cousins (sons of the paternal uncle). They are asabah and inherit equally when no closer heirs exist.
أَخ لِأُم (akh li-umm): A uterine brother (brother through the mother only). He is a Quranic heir entitled to 1/6 if alone, up to 1/3 if multiple.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case described in the lesson, what is the total share of the dual cousin (uterine brother and paternal cousin)?
A) 1/6
B) 5/12
C) 7/12
D) 1/2

Key Takeaway
A heir with multiple relations inherits through each capacity: first the Quranic share, then the agnatic share, combining them.

The Mushtarika Case: Husband, Mother, Uterine and Full Siblings
Ruling on the controversial mushtarika case with husband, mother, and siblings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the shares of each heir in the mushtarika case and explain why full siblings are excluded according to the Hanafi school, citing the Quranic verses used as proof.

Core Idea
Full siblings are excluded because fixed shares exhaust the estate; one-third is for uterine siblings only.

This lesson examines a famous inheritance scenario known as the mushtarika case, where a woman dies leaving her husband, mother, uterine siblings, and full siblings. The Hanafi rule is clear: full siblings receive nothing. But why? The answer lies in a combination of three Quranic verses and a preference among Companions. We will walk through the proofs and the dispute to understand the school's position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the heirs and their Quranic shares
List the four types of heirs: husband, mother, uterine siblings, full siblings. Recall the fixed shares: husband gets half (if no child), mother gets one-sixth (if siblings exist), uterine siblings get one-third collectively. Full siblings are not mentioned in these verses for this scenario.
The husband's share is from 4:12, mother's from 4:11, uterine siblings from 4:12 (kalalah verse).
2
Sum the fixed shares
Add the shares: 1/2 (husband) + 1/6 (mother) + 1/3 (uterine siblings) = 1 (the whole estate). Thus full siblings have no residue left.
This arithmetical fact is key; the full siblings are asabah but the estate is exhausted.
3
Analyze the dispute among the Sahaba
Some Companions (Umar, Ibn Mas'ud) included full siblings in the one-third, making them 'partners' (mushtarika). Others (Ali) excluded them. The Hanafi school follows Ali's view.
The name 'mushtarika' derives from the opposing view, but Hanafis use it as a technical term for this exact heir configuration.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi position relies on the literal application of the kalalah verse (4:12), which specifies 'siblings through the mother' for the one-third. Full siblings are not uterine, so they are not included. Additionally, full siblings are asabah and do not receive fixed shares; when there is no residue, they get nothing.
The narration from Ibrahim confirms that Ali did not include them, adding weight to the Hanafi position.

وَالْمُشَرِّكَةُ أَنْ تَتْرُكَ الْمَرْأَةُ زَوْجًا وَأُمًّا وَإِخْوَةً مِنْ أُمٍّ وَإِخْوَةً مِنْ أَبٍ وَأُمٍّ فَلِلزَّوْجِ النِّصْفُ وَلِلْأُمِّ السُّدُسُ وَلِأَوْلَادِ الْأُمِّ الثُّلُثُ وَلَا شَيْءَ لِلْإِخْوَةِ لِلْأَبِ وَالْأُمِّ
وَجْهٌ (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: ﴿وَلَكُمْ نِصْفُ مَا تَرَكَ أَزْوَاجُكُمْ إِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُنَّ وَلَدٌ﴾ [سورة النساء، 4:12]
وَجْهٌ (2) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: ﴿فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُ وَلَدٌ وَوَرِثَهُ أَبَوَاهُ فَلِأُمِّهِ الثُّلُثُ فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ﴾ [سورة النساء، 4:11]
وَجْهٌ (3) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: ﴿وَإِن كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلَالَةً أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ وَلَهُ أَخٌ أَوْ أُخْتٌ فَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ فَإِن كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِن ذَلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلُثِ﴾ [سورة النساء، 4:12]
وَجْهٌ (4) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: كَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ وَعُمَرُ «يُشْرِكَانِ»، قَالَ: وَكَانَ عَلِيٌّ لَا يُشْرِكُ»، قَالَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ: «وَهَذِهِ مِنْ سِتَّةِ أَسْهُمٍ: لِلزَّوْجِ النِّصْفُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَسْهُمٍ، وَلِلْأُمِّ السُّدُسُ سَهْمٌ، وَلِلْإِخْوَةِ مِنَ الْأُمِّ الثُّلُثُ سَهْمَانِ» [مُصَنَّفُ ابْنِ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ، فِي زَوْجٍ وَأُمٍّ وَإِخْوَةٍ وَأَخَوَاتٍ لِأَبٍ وَأُمٍّ وَإِخْوَةٍ لِأُمّ، رَقْم 31105]
And the 'Mushtarika' is that a woman leaves a husband, a mother, uterine brothers, and full brothers and sisters. Then for the husband is half, for the mother is one-sixth, for the children of the mother (i.e., uterine siblings) is one-third, and there is nothing for the full brothers and sisters. Proof (1) the verse for establishing that: 'And for you is half of what your wives leave if they have no child' [4:12]. Proof (2) the verse: 'If he has no child and his parents inherit him, then for his mother is one-third; if he has siblings, then for his mother is one-sixth' [4:11]. Proof (3) the verse: 'If a man is inherited kalalah or a woman, and he has a brother or a sister, then for each one of them is one-sixth; if they are more than that, then they are partners in one-third' [4:12]. Proof (4) the saying of the Tabi'i: from Ibrahim who said: 'Abdullah and Umar used to include them (i.e., make them partners), and 'Ali did not include them.' Abu Bakr said: 'This is from six shares: for the husband half (three shares), for the mother one-sixth (one share), for the uterine siblings one-third (two shares)' [Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah].
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This lesson presents the mushtarika (or 'mushtaraka') case, a well-known inheritance scenario. The deceased is a woman survived by her husband, her mother, uterine siblings (half-brothers/sisters through mother), and full siblings (through both parents). The ruling: the husband takes half (1/2), the mother takes one-sixth (1/6), the uterine siblings collectively take one-third (1/3), and the full siblings receive nothing. The key point is that the full siblings are excluded because the one-third is given to the uterine siblings, and the residue after the half and sixth is exactly one-third, so full siblings get nothing. However, there is a dispute: some early authorities (Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and Umar) included the full siblings in the one-third, making them 'partners' (mushtarika) with the uterine siblings. This is why the case is called mushtarika. The Hanafi position, following Ali, is to exclude the full siblings from the one-third, as they are not heirs in the presence of uterine siblings. The proofs are three Quranic verses: one for the husband's half (4:12), one for the mother's reduction to one-sixth in the presence of siblings (4:11), and one for the uterine siblings' one-third (4:12). The fourth proof is the narration from Ibrahim indicating the practice of two caliphs. The Hanafi school adopts the position of Ali, which is the majority view.

Key Terms
مُشَرِّكَة (mushtarika): A specific inheritance case where a deceased woman leaves husband, mother, uterine siblings, and full siblings. Full siblings are excluded (or included by some).
إِخْوَة لِأَب وَأُم (ikhwa li-ab wa-umm): Full siblings (brothers and sisters from both parents). They are asabah, not Quranic sharers except in certain cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the mushtarika case, what do the full siblings (through both parents) receive?
A) One-sixth
B) One-third
C) Nothing
D) The residue

Key Takeaway
In the mushtarika case, full siblings are excluded because the Quranic fixed shares of husband, mother, and uterine siblings exactly total the entire estate.

The Musharrakah Case: Exclusion of Full Siblings
Defining the Musharrakah case with proofs and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling in the Musharrakah case, identify the Quranic and Sahaba proofs, and explain the difference with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
In Musharrakah, Hanafis exclude full siblings; Shafi'is include them in the uterine siblings' third.

The Musharrakah case is a classic inheritance dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. A woman dies leaving a husband, mother, uterine siblings, and full siblings. The question: do the full siblings share in the one-third allocated to the uterine siblings? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position based on the Quranic kalalah verse and the practice of Ali, contrasting it with the Shafi'i view that includes full siblings following Uthman and other Companions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Musharrakah scenario
Identify the heirs: husband, mother, uterine siblings (from mother only), and full siblings (same mother and father).
The term 'Musharrakah' refers to the partnership discussion between sibling types.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
In the Hanafi school, full siblings receive nothing; only uterine siblings take the one-third share. The husband gets half, the mother one-sixth.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa, following Ali and Ibn Mas'ud.
3
Identify the Quranic proof
The kalalah verse (4:12) specifies that siblings through the mother share the third. The Hanafis interpret this as exclusive to uterine siblings.
Full siblings are asabah, but here no residue remains, so they are excluded.
4
Present the Shafi'i counter-evidence
The Shafi'i school cites the practice of Uthman, Shurayh, and Masruq who made full siblings partners with uterine siblings.
Also a report that Umar initially excluded but later included them.
5
Contrast the positions and note the thamarah
The practical difference: in Hanafi fiqh, full siblings get nothing; in Shafi'i fiqh, they share equally in the one-third with uterine siblings.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi due to stronger Quranic basis and the authority of Ali.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
