وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت: ﴿وَلَكُمْ نِصْفُ مَا تَرَكَ أَزْوَاجُكُمْ إِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُنَّ وَلَدٌ فَإِن كَانَ لَهُنَّ وَلَدٌ فَلَكُمُ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْنَ مِن بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِينَ بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ وَلَهُنَّ الرُّبُعُ مِمَّا تَرَكْتُمْ إِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّكُمْ وَلَدٌ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 آیت نمبر 12)
وجه : (۲) الآية لثبوت: ﴿فَإِن لَّمْ يَكُن لَّهُ وَلَدٌ وَوَرِثَهُ أَبَوَاهُ فَلِأُمِّهِ الثُّلُثُ فَإِن كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ مِن بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصِي بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 آیت نمبر 11)
وجه : (۳) الآية لثبوت: ﴿وَإِن كَانَ رَجُلٌ يُورَثُ كَلَالَةً أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ وَلَهُ أَخٌ أَوْ أُخْتٌ فَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِّنْهُمَا السُّدُسُ فَإِن كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِن ذَٰلِكَ فَهُمْ شُرَكَاءُ فِي الثُّلُثِ مِن بَعْدِ وَصِيَّةٍ يُوصَى بِهَا أَوْ دَيْنٍ غَيْرَ مُضَارٍّ وَصِيَّةً مِّنَ اللَّهِ﴾ (سورة النساء، 4 آیت نمبر 12)
وجه : (۴) قول التابعي لثبوت: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: كَانَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ، وَعُمَرُ «يُشْرِكَانِ»، قَالَ: وَكَانَ عَلِيٌّ لَا يُشْرِكُ»، قَالَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ: «وَهَذِهِ مِنْ سِتَّةِ أَسْهُمٍ لِلزَّوْجِ النِّصْفُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَسْهُمٍ، وَلِلْأُمِّ السُّدُسُ، وَلِلْإِخْوَةِ مِنَ الْأُمِّ الثُّلُثُ، وَهُوَ سَهْمَانِ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، في زوج وأم وإخوة وأخوات لأب وأم وإخوة لأم، مَنْ شَرَّكَ بَيْنَهُمْ، رقم 31105)

Chapter of Hajb. And the Musharrakah is that a woman leaves a husband, a mother, uterine siblings, and full siblings: for the husband half, for the mother one-sixth, for the uterine siblings one-third, and nothing for the full siblings. Evidence (1): the verse [...] Evidence (2): the verse [...] Evidence (3): the verse [...] Evidence (4): the saying of the tabi'i: from Ibrahim, he said: Abdullah and Umar 'make them partners (yushrikān)', he said: and Ali did not make them partners. Abu Bakr said: 'This is from six shares: for the husband half (three shares), for the mother one-sixth, and for the uterine siblings one-third (two shares).' Evidence (1) for al-Shafi'i: the saying of the tabi'i: from Shurayh and Masruq that they made the full siblings partners with the uterine siblings. Evidence (2): the saying of the Companion: from Abu 'Ajlan that Uthman made them partners. Principles: The reason for calling it the Musharrakah problem: because it involves several types of brothers, and the mother, and the grandmother's problem is called Musharrakah. Sometimes the full siblings are excluded and sometimes they are included.
Source pages p. 447

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the Musharrakah case in inheritance. The text first states the Hanafi ruling: when a woman dies leaving a husband, mother, uterine siblings, and full siblings (from the same father and mother), the husband takes half (1/2), the mother takes one-sixth (1/6), the uterine siblings share one-third (1/3), and the full siblings receive nothing. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and is based on the Quranic verses that allocate shares to spouses, mothers, and uterine siblings. The full siblings are excluded because their shares would overlap; the uterine siblings take priority as specified in the verse on kalalah. The text then provides proofs: the three relevant verses (4:12, 4:11, 4:12) and the practice of Sahaba like Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and Umar who made the full siblings partners (i.e., included them with the uterine siblings in the third), while Ali excluded them. The Hanafi position follows Ali and the Quranic allocation. Then the text presents the evidence for the Shafi'i position, which includes the full siblings with the uterine siblings in the third, based on the practice of Shurayh, Masruq, and Caliph Uthman. The Urdu commentary adds that the name 'Musharrakah' refers to the sharing between different types of siblings, and explains that sometimes full siblings are excluded and sometimes included (in the Shafi'i view). The Hanafi position is that full siblings are excluded when uterine siblings are present, based on the principle that they are not from the same category as the heirs mentioned in the kalalah verse.

Key Terms
الْمُشَرِكَةُ (al-musharrakah): A specific inheritance case where a woman dies leaving a husband, mother, uterine siblings, and full siblings; named for the partnership (mushārakah) between siblings.
حَجْب (hajb): Exclusion from inheritance; here referring to the exclusion of full siblings from the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) They receive nothing.
C) They take the residue after all shares.
D) They receive one-sixth each.

Key Takeaway
In the Musharrakah case, the Hanafi school excludes full siblings because the Quranic one-third share is exclusive to uterine siblings and the estate is fully consumed by fard shares.

Two Types of Hajb in Inheritance Law
Classifying Hajb into two main types with lists of heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two types of Hajb (hirman) and list the heirs in each category.

Core Idea
Hajb is not only about excluding others; some heirs are themselves permanently excluded.

Inheritance law requires precise rules about who inherits and who is blocked. This passage from Hanafi faraid clarifies two categories of exclusion: those who block others but still inherit, and those who are permanently excluded. Mastering this classification is a fundamental step in solving inheritance distributions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of hajb
Read the passage and note that the first type is 'those who themselves are not excluded but exclude others', and the second is 'those who are permanently excluded'.
2
List the six heirs of Type 1
From the text, write down the six heirs: son, father, husband, daughter, mother, wife. These exclude more distant relatives but themselves inherit as asabah or fixed shares.
These are sometimes called 'primary heirs'.
3
List the five permanently excluded heirs of Type 2
Note the five disqualifying attributes: disbelief (kufr), killing (qatl), apostasy (riddah), slavery (riqq), and difference of abode (ikhtilaf al-dar). These individuals never inherit.
Some schools differ on slavery, but Hanafis consider it a permanent bar.
4
Apply to a scenario
Take a scenario: deceased leaves a son and a brother. According to Type 1, the son excludes the brother. But if the son is a killer, he falls into Type 2 and does not inherit; the brother then inherits as asabah.
Type 2 overrides Type 1 if the heir is disqualified.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أصول: حجب حرمان کی دو قسمیں ہیں: نمبر ا وہ جو خود محروم نہیں ہوتے بلکہ دوسروں کو وراثت سے محروم کرتے ہیں، اور یہ چھ قسم کے لوگ ہیں: ۱ بیٹا، ۲ باپ، ۳ شوہر، ۴ بیٹی، ۵ ماں، ۶ بیوی، یہ دوسروں کو محروم کرتے ہیں لیکن خود عصبہ یا حصہ کے طور پر وراثت لے لیتے ہیں۔ حجب کی دوسری قسم: نمبر ۲ وہ ہمیشہ کے لئے وراثت سے محروم ہو جاتے ہیں، اور وہ پانچ ہیں: ۱ کافر، ۲ قاتل، ۳ مرتد، ۴ غلام، ۵ اختلاف دارین، یہ لوگ میت کے مال وارث نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔
Principles: The exclusion (hajb hirman) has two types: number one, those who themselves are not excluded but exclude others from inheritance, and they are six types of people: 1 son, 2 father, 3 husband, 4 daughter, 5 mother, 6 wife. These exclude others but themselves take inheritance as asabah or as a share. The second type of hajb: number two, those who are permanently excluded from inheritance, and they are five: 1 disbeliever, 2 killer, 3 apostate, 4 slave, 5 difference of religion (dār). These people do not inherit from the deceased's property.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of the two types of Hajb (exclusion) in inheritance law. The first type is Hajb Hirman watan (exclusion of others while oneself inherits). The heirs mentioned—son, father, husband, daughter, mother, wife—are 'stronger' heirs who block more distant heirs but themselves receive a share. For example, a son excludes grandchildren and siblings, but he himself inherits as asabah. The second type is Hajb Hirman where the heir is permanently excluded due to an inherent disqualification: kufr (disbelief), qatl (homicide), riddah (apostasy), riqq (slavery), or ikhtilāf al-dār (difference of abode, i.e., living in non-Muslim territory with no treaty). These individuals never inherit from the deceased. This classification is a fundamental principle in Hanafi faraid.

Key Terms
حجب (hajb): Exclusion from inheritance; here defined as two types: one where the heir excludes others but still inherits, and the other where the heir is permanently excluded due to a disqualifying attribute.
اختلاف دارین (ikhtilāf al-dārain): Difference of abode: a Muslim in a non-Muslim territory not under Islamic government does not inherit from a relative in Muslim territory and vice versa, under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of the first type of Hajb (where the heir excludes others but himself inherits)?
A) A slave.
B) A killer.
C) A son.
D) An apostate.

Key Takeaway
The classification of Hajb into two types—those who exclude others while inheriting, and those permanently excluded—is essential for correctly determining inheritance shares.

The Musharrakah Case: Hanafi Position and Proofs
Presents proofs for the Hanafi ruling on the Musharrakah inheritance case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on the Musharrakah case and evaluate the proofs from the Sahaba and tabi'un that support it.

Core Idea
In Musharrakah, consanguine siblings inherit with full siblings because 'Uthman's practice overrides general analogy.

This lesson delves into the famous Musharrakah inheritance case, a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The passage presents two key proofs that the Hanafi school uses to support its ruling that consanguine siblings are included with full siblings in the residue. By examining these proofs, you will understand how the Hanafi school prioritizes specific precedents from the Sahaba and tabi'un over general principles.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Musharrakah scenario
Identify the heirs: husband, mother, full siblings, and consanguine siblings. The dispute is about whether consanguine siblings inherit.
This case is also called al-ḥimāriyyah (the donkey case) in some traditions.
2
Identify the Hanafi position
State that the Hanafi school includes consanguine siblings in the residue (asabah) after giving fard shares to husband and mother.
Contrast with the Shafi'i position of exclusion.
3
Examine the first proof
Read the narration from Shuraih and Masruq (tabi'un) that they included the siblings. Understand its source and weight in Hanafi usul.
This is considered a Qawl Tabi'i, which is a weaker proof.
4
Examine the second proof
Read the narration from Abu 'Ijl that Caliph 'Uthman included them. This is a Qawl Sahabi, a stronger proof for the Hanafis.
No known opposition from other Sahaba gives it more weight.
5
Contrast with the opposing view
The Shafi'i school relies on general analogy: full siblings block consanguine siblings. The Hanafi response is that the specific precedent overrides the general rule.
Thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi, consanguine siblings get a share; in Shafi'i, they are excluded.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْحَجْبِ
وجه:(ا) دليل الشافعى قول التابعى لثبوت وَالْمُشَرِكَةُ أَنْ تَتْرُكَ الْمَرْأَةُ زَوْجًا \ عَنْ شُرَيْحٍ، وَمَسْرُوقِ، «أَنَّهُمَا شَرَّكَا الْإِخْوَةَ مِنَ الْأَبِ وَالْأُمّ مَعَ الْإِخْوَةِ مِنَ الْأُمّ»»"(مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي زَوْجِ وَأُمَ وَإِخْوَةٍ وَأَخَوَاتٍ لِأَبِ وَأُمَ وَإِخْوَةٍ لِأُمَ، مَنْ شَرَّكَ بَيْنَهُمْ، فَبر 31101) وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالْمُشَركَةُ أَنْ تَتْرُكَ الْمَرْأَةُ زَوْجًا \ عَنْ أَبِي عِجْلَرٍ، أَنَّ عُثْمَانَ، شَرَّكَ بَيْنَهُمْ» (مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي زَوْجِ وَأَمَ وَإِخْوَةٍ وَأَخَوَاتٍ لِأَبِ وَأُمَ وَإِخْوَةِ لِأُمّ، مَنْ شَرَّكَ بَيْنَهُمْ، غبر 31100)
اصول: مشتر کہ مسئلہ کہنے کی وجہ : ا اس میں کئی قسم کے بھائی، اور ماں، دادی کا مسئلہ اسلئے مشتر کہ کہا، ۲ کبھی حقیقی بھائی انکار کر دیئے جاتے ہیں اور کبھی شریک کئے جاتے ہیں۔
Chapter of Exclusion. First aspect: The proof of al-Shafi'i is the saying of the tabi'i for establishing the Musharrakah: that the woman leaves a husband... from Shuraih and Masruq that they included the siblings from the father and mother with the siblings from the mother. (Mushaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 31101). Second aspect: The saying of the Sahabi for establishing the Musharrakah: from Abu 'Ijl, that 'Uthman included between them. (Mushaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 31100). Principle: The reason for calling it the Musharrakah problem: because it involves several types of brothers, and the mother and grandmother, therefore called Musharrakah. Sometimes full brothers are excluded, sometimes they are included.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage opens the Chapter of Exclusion (Hajb) with a discussion of the famous Musharrakah case. The author first presents two proofs for the Hanafi position that in this specific scenario, consanguine siblings are included with full siblings in the inheritance. The first proof (aspect one) is attributed to al-Shafi'i, but is actually a saying of the tabi'un Shuraih and Masruq, who included the siblings from the father and mother (full siblings) with siblings from the mother (consanguine). The second proof is the action of Caliph 'Uthman, who also included them. The Hanafi school gives greater weight to the practice of the Sahabi 'Uthman. The Urdu note explains why this case is called "Musharrakah" (shared): because it involves multiple types of siblings, and the ruling varies—sometimes full siblings are excluded, sometimes they are included, depending on the presence of other heirs.

Key Terms
المشركة (al-musharrakah): An inheritance case where the deceased leaves a husband, mother, full siblings, and consanguine siblings; the consanguine siblings are included with the full siblings in the residue.
حجب (hajb): The legal concept of excluding an heir from inheritance, either completely (hirman) or partially (nuqsan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Consensus of the Sahaba
C) The practice of 'Uthman and the tabi'un
D) The opinion of Imam Abu Hanifa alone

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi inclusion of consanguine siblings in Musharrakah is based on specific historical precedents, not general analogy.

Two Types of Exclusion (Hajb Hirman)
Classification of hajb hirman categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the two categories of hajb hirman and identify the six heirs who exclude others but themselves inherit, as well as the five types who are permanently excluded.

Core Idea
Inheritance exclusion is either by powerful heirs who inherit and exclude others, or by permanent disqualification.

Hajb hirman (total exclusion) is a key principle in Islamic inheritance that determines who is excluded from inheriting. The Hanafi school classifies this exclusion into two clear categories. Understanding these categories is essential for correctly calculating shares and avoiding common mistakes when applying the rules of inheritance.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the two categories
Internalize that hajb hirman has two types: (1) heirs who exclude others but themselves inherit, and (2) individuals who are permanently excluded regardless of their relation.
2
List the six excluding heirs
Recall the six heirs: son, father, husband, daughter, mother, wife. These are the main heirs who, when present, block more distant relatives from inheriting.
They inherit either as asabah (e.g., son, father) or as fixed sharers (e.g., husband, wife).
3
List the five permanently excluded
Memorize the five types: disbeliever, killer, apostate, slave, and difference of religion. These individuals never inherit, regardless of their proximity.
The underlying cause for each is that they are legally disqualified from owning property or benefiting from the deceased.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول: حجب حرمان کی دو قسمیں ہیں: نمبر ا وہ جو خود محروم نہیں ہوتے بلکہ دوسروں کو وراثت سے محروم کرتے ہیں، اور یہ چھ قسم کے لوگ ہیں ابیٹا، ۲ باپ، ۳ شوہر ، ۴ بیٹی، ۵ ماں ، بیوی، یہ دوسروں کو محروم کرتے ہیں لیکن خود عصبہ یا حصہ کے طور پر وراثت لے لیتے ہیں۔ حجب کی دوسری قسیم : نمبر ۲ وہ ہمیشہ کے لئے وراثت سے محروم ہو جاتے ہیں، اور وہ پانچ ہیں ،ا کافر، ۲ قاتل ۳۰ مرتد ، ۴ غلام، ۵ اختلاف دارین، یہ لوگ میت کے مال وارث نہیں ہوتے ہیں۔
Principle: There are two types of exclusion (hajb hirman): Number one: those who themselves are not excluded but exclude others from inheritance, and these are six types: (1) son, (2) father, (3) husband, (4) daughter, (5) mother, (6) wife. These exclude others but themselves inherit as asabah or by share. The second type: those who are permanently excluded from inheritance, and there are five: (1) disbeliever, (2) killer, (3) apostate, (4) slave, (5) difference of religion. These people do not inherit from the deceased's property.
Source pages p. 448

Commentary
This passage is a concise classification from the Urdu commentary on the rules of hajb (exclusion) in inheritance. It divides hajb hirman into two categories. The first category consists of heirs who themselves inherit (either as residuary heirs or as Quranic sharers) but have the power to exclude other, more distant heirs. Six heirs are mentioned: son, father, husband, daughter, mother, and wife. For example, the son excludes all other male agnates except the father. The second category lists five types of individuals who are permanently disqualified from inheriting: the disbeliever (non-Muslim), the killer (who caused the death of the deceased), the apostate (who leaves Islam), the slave (who cannot own property), and the difference of religion (between Muslim and non-Muslim). These individuals never inherit, regardless of their relationship.

Key Terms
حجب حرمان (hajb hirman): Legal exclusion from inheritance, either total (hirman) or partial (nuqsan). Here specifically refers to total exclusion.
عصبة (asabah): Residuary heir who inherits the remaining estate after Quranic sharers have taken their shares.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Hajb hirman divides into two: heirs who exclude but inherit, and permanently disqualified persons.

Faraid — Inheritance

The Law of Radd and Exclusion of the Killer
States three Hanafi faraid rulings with supporting proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on radd (return of surplus to blood sharers excluding spouses), apply the exclusion of the killer from inheritance, and explain why all non-Muslims inherit from each other as one millah.

Core Idea
Radd returns surplus to blood sharers except spouses; the killer never inherits; all non-Muslims inherit from each other as one millah.

Faraid (inheritance) is a precise science in Islamic law. After each Quranic sharer receives their prescribed share, there may be a surplus when there is no residuary heir (asabah). How should this surplus be distributed? The Hanafi school has a clear rule: it is returned (radd) to the blood-related sharers in proportion to their shares, but never to the spouse. Additionally, a person who causes the death of the deceased is barred from inheritance, and all non-Muslims are treated as one religious community for inheritance purposes. This lesson unpacks these three rulings and their proofs from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the passage and list the three separate fiqh rulings: (1) radd of surplus to blood sharers except spouses, (2) the killer does not inherit, (3) all non-Muslims inherit from each other.
These rulings are presented together because they are essential principles in Hanafi faraid.
2
Analyze the proof for radd
The passage cites two proofs: (a) the practice of 'Ali (radi Allahu 'anhu) who returned surplus to all sharers except spouses, and (b) the statement that none of the Companions returned anything to the spouse. Understand that these constitute a qawl al-sahabi (statement of a Companion) which is considered a proof (dalil) in Hanafi usul.
Note also the alternative view of Zaid ibn Thabit who placed the surplus in the public treasury.
3
Examine the proof for excluding the killer
The hadith from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi explicitly states: 'The killer has nothing.' This is an ahad hadith but is accepted in Hanafi fiqh. The ruling excludes any killer, intentional or accidental, as long as the killing is punishable by diyah or qisas.
Other schools may differentiate between intentional and accidental killing, but the Hanafi position is absolute.
4
Understand the millah concept for non-Muslims
The passage states 'all disbelief is one religion' meaning that all non-Muslims (Jews, Christians, etc.) inherit from each other as if they are of one faith. This is supported by the hadith 'People of two religions do not inherit from each other' and the statement of Sufyan that 'Islam is one millah, shirk is one millah.'
This ensures that non-Muslims of different sects can inherit from each other, contrary to some later opinions that differentiate.
5
Connect the rulings to practical application
Apply these rules to a sample inheritance scenario: a deceased leaves a husband, a daughter, and no asabah. The husband gets 1/4, the daughter gets 1/2, leaving a surplus of 1/4. According to radd, the surplus goes to the daughter (blood sharer) in proportion to her share, not to the husband. If the daughter had killed the deceased, she would be excluded and the surplus would go to the husband? Actually, if she is excluded, the husband might get the entire estate? Careful: the killer is excluded, so the daughter would not inherit at all, and the husband would take his share and the remainder goes to... but there is no asabah, so radd would apply to other blood sharers if any. This shows the complexity.
This step integrates all three rulings in one scenario.

Source Text

وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يَرِثُ الْقَاتِلُ مِنْ الْمَقْتُولِ \ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِهِ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُقَوّمُ دِيَةَ الْخَطَ عَلَى أَهْلِ الْقُرَى أَرْبَعَ مِائَةِ دِينَارٍ ..... وَقَضَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّ عَقْلَ الْمَرْأَةِ بَيْنَ عَصَبَتِهَا مَنْ كَانُوا لَا يَرِثُونَ مِنْهَا شَيْئًا إِلَّا مَا فَضَلَ عَنْ وَرَثَتِهَا، وَإِنْ قُتِلَتْ فَعَقْلُهَا بَيْنَ وَرَثَتِهَا، وَهُمْ يَقْتُلُونَ قَاتِلَهُمْ، وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَيْسَ لِلْقَاتِلِ شَيْءٌ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ وَارِثٌ فَوَارِثُهُ أَقْرَبُ النَّاسِ إِلَيْهِ، وَلا يَرِثُ الْقَاتِلُ شَيْئًا»» (سنن ابوداود، بَابُ دِيَاتِ الْأَعْضَاءِ، نمبر 4564/سنن الترمذي، بَابُ بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي إِبْطَالِ مِيرَاثِ القَاتِلِ،نمبر2109)

وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَالْكُفْرُ كُلُّهُ مِلَّةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ يَتَوَارَتْ بِهِ أَهْلُهُ \ عَنْ ابْنِ أَبِي لَيْلَى، عَنْ أَبِي الزُّبَيْرِ، عَنْ جَابِرٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لا يَتَوَارَثُ أَهْلُ مِلَّتَيْنِ» ( سنن الترمذي، بَابُ لَا يَتَوَارَتُ أَهْلُ مِلَّتَيْنِ، نمبر 2108)
اصول : نسبی اور خاندانی رشتہ داروں کو ان کے حصے کے مطابق دوبارہ تقسیم کر نارد کہلاتا ہے، اور چونکہ میاں اور بیوی نسبی رشتہ میں داخل نہیں ہیں اسلئے ان کو دوبارہ حصہ نہیں ملے گا، انہیں سہام پر اکتفا کر نا پڑے گا۔ اصول: تمام کا فرخواہ یہودی ہو یا نصرانی ایک دوسرے کے وارث بنیں گے گویاوہ ایک ہی مذہب ہو۔
Chapter of Radd. The author (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The surplus from the shares of the people of fixed shares, if there is no residuary heir, is returned to them according to their shares, except to the two spouses. And the killer does not inherit from the killed. And all disbelief is one religion; its people inherit from each other. First aspect: saying of the tabi'i to establish that the surplus from the shares of the people of shares is returned... from Ibrahim that 'Ali used to return to every holder of a share except the husband and wife. (Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 31168). Second aspect: the hadith to establish the surplus... Ibrahim said: None of the Companions of the Prophet used to return anything to the wife and husband. He said: Zaid would give every holder of his share, and whatever remained he placed in the public treasury. (Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 31176). First aspect: the hadith to establish that the killer does not inherit from the killed... from 'Amr ibn Shu'aib from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet fixed the blood money for accidental killing... and he ruled that the killer has nothing, and he does not inherit anything. (Abu Dawud, no. 4564; Tirmidhi, no. 2109). First aspect: saying of the tabi'i to establish that all disbelief is one religion... Sufyan said: Islam is one religion, shirk is one religion. (Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 31453). Second aspect: the hadith to establish that all disbelief is one religion... from Jabir that the Prophet said: The people of two religions do not inherit from each other. (Tirmidhi, no. 2108). Principle: The redistribution of blood relatives according to their shares is called radd, and since the husband and wife are not relatives by blood, they do not get a share in the return; they must be content with their shares. Principle: All disbelievers, whether Jew or Christian, will inherit from each other, as if they are of one religion.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is from the Chapter of Radd (Return). It contains the core Hanafi ruling on three matters: First, the law of radd: If there is no residuary heir (asabah) after the Quranic sharers have taken their shares, the surplus is returned to the sharers in proportion to their shares, except for the spouse (husband or wife). This means the spouse does not benefit from radd; they only get their prescribed share, and any surplus goes to the other blood-related sharers. This is supported by the practice of 'Ali (as transmitted by Ibrahim) and the statement that no Companion returned anything to the spouse. Second, the killer does not inherit from the deceased, regardless of whether the killing was intentional or accidental. This is proven by the hadith from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi. Third, all non-Muslims, regardless of their specific religion (Jew, Christian, etc.), are considered one religion (millah) for the purpose of inheritance, meaning they inherit from each other. This is supported by the statement of Sufyan and the hadith that people of two religions do not inherit from each other. The Urdu notes clarify the definition of radd and the reasoning behind excluding spouses.

Key Terms
الرد (ar-radd): The return of the surplus of the estate to the Quranic sharers (except spouses) in proportion to their shares when there is no residuary heir.
قاتل (qatil): A person who causes the death of the deceased, whether intentionally or accidentally, and is thereby excluded from inheritance.
ملة (millah): A religious community or creed. Here it means that all non-Muslims are considered one religion for inheritance purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following heirs does NOT benefit from the radd (return) of surplus when there is no residuary heir?
A) The daughter
B) The mother
C) The husband
D) The full sister

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, the surplus after Quranic shares is returned to blood-related sharers (except spouses), the killer is entirely excluded, and all non-Muslims inherit from each other as one millah.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
8 min
Chapter of Radd: Surplus Distribution and Related Inheritance Rules
Presents matn and proofs for multiple inheritance rules: radd, killer, kufr, apostate, simultaneous death, Magians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rules on radd (surplus distribution), killer's inheritance, kufr as one millah, Muslim/non-Muslim inheritance, apostate property, simultaneous death, and Magian inheritance, and identify the proof for each ruling.

Core Idea
In Hanafi faraid, radd returns surplus to blood heirs excluding spouses; all kufr is one millah; killer cannot inherit; apostate's wealth for Muslim heirs; simultaneous death no mutual inheritance; Magians inherit only through lawful relationships.

This passage from al-Quduri presents the core rulings on surplus distribution (radd) and several other inheritance principles: the exclusion of spouses from radd, the prohibition of a killer inheriting, the treatment of all disbelievers as one community for inheritance, the bar between Muslim and non-Muslim inheritance, the treatment of an apostate's property, rules for simultaneous death, and the special case of Magians. Each ruling is supported by proofs from the practice of the Companions and prophetic hadith. Let's work through these rulings systematically.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the ruling on radd and its proof
Identify the ruling: surplus is returned to fixed-share heirs proportionally except spouses. Then examine the proof: practice of 'Ali and Zayd.
2
Examine the killer's inheritance ruling
Note that a killer does not inherit. Identify the hadith from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb that the killer has nothing.
3
Understand 'kufr is one millah' and Muslim/non-Muslim bar
Interpret the proof: all disbelievers inherit from each other; Muslims and non-Muslims do not inherit from each other. Note the hadith: 'People of two different millahs do not inherit from each other.'
4
Analyze apostate property and simultaneous death rules
Distinguish between apostate's pre- and post-apostasy wealth; recognize that in simultaneous death, each deceased's estate goes to their own living heirs.
5
Apply the Magian inheritance rule
Understand that Magians inherit through the closest lawful relationship, not through invalid marriages.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الرَّد
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ الله : وَالْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ ذَوِي السَّهَامِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ عَصَبَةٌ مَرْدُودٌ عَلَيْهِمْ بِقَدْرِ سِهَامِهِمْ إِلَّا عَلَى الزَّوْجَيْنِ ، وَلَا يَرِثُ الْقَاتِلُ مِنْ الْمَقْتُولِ وَالْكُفْرُ كُلُّهُ مِلَّةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ يَتَوَارَثُ بِهِ أَهْلُهُ وَلَا يَرِثُ الْمُسْلِمُ الْكَافِرَ وَلَا الْكَافِرُ الْمُسْلِمَ وَمَالُ الْمُرْتَدِّ لِوَرَثَتِهِ مِنْ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَمَا اكْتَسَبَهُ فِي حَالِ رِدَّتِهِ فَيْءٌ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ وَإِذَا غَرِقَ جَمَاعَةٌ أَوْ سَقَطَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَائِطٌ وَلَمْ يُعْلَمْ مَنْ مَاتَ مِنْهُمْ أَوَّلًا فَمَالُ كُلِّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ لِلْأَحْيَاءِ مِنْ وَرَثَتِهِ وَإِذَا اجْتَمَعَ فِي الْمَجُوسِيِّ قَرَابَتَانِ لَوْ تَفَرَّقَتَا فِي شَخْصَيْنِ وَرِثَ بِكُلِّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْهُمَا وَلَا يَرِثُ الْمَجُوسِيُّ بِالْأَنْكِحَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ الَّتِي يَسْتَحِلُّونَهَا فِي دِينِهِمْ
وَجْهٌ : (۱) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ ذَوِي السَّهَامِ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، أَنَّ عَلِيًّا، كَانَ يَرُدُّ عَلَى كُلِّ ذِي سَهْمٍ، إِلَّا الزَّوْجَ وَالْمَرْأَةَ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، في الرد واختلافهم فيه، رقم 31168)
وَجْهٌ : (۲) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالْفَاضِلُ عَنْ فَرْضِ ذَوِي السَّهَامِ قَالَ إِبْرَاهِيمُ: لَمْ يَكُنْ أَحَدٌ مِنْ أَصْحَابِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم يَرُدُّ عَلَى الْمَرْأَةِ وَالزَّوْجِ شَيْئًا، قَالَ: وَكَانَ زَيْدٌ يُعْطِي كُلَّ ذِي فَرْضٍ فَرِيضَتَهُ، وَمَا بَقِيَ جَعَلَهُ فِي بَيْتِ الْمَالِ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، في الرد واختلافهم فيه، رقم 31176)
وَجْهٌ : (۱) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يَرِثُ الْقَاتِلُ مِنْ الْمَقْتُولِ عَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ جَدِّهِ، قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم يُقَوِّمُ دِيَةَ الْخَطَأِ عَلَى أَهْلِ الْقُرَى أَرْبَعَ مِائَةِ دِينَارٍ ..... وَقَضَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّ عَقْلَ الْمَرْأَةِ بَيْنَ عَصَبَتِهَا مَنْ كَانُوا لَا يَرِثُونَ مِنْهَا شَيْئًا إِلَّا مَا فَضَلَ عَنْ وَرَثَتِهَا، وَإِنْ قُتِلَتْ فَعَقْلُهَا بَيْنَ وَرَثَتِهَا، وَهُمْ يَقْتُلُونَ قَاتِلَهُمْ، وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لَيْسَ لِلْقَاتِلِ شَيْءٌ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ لَهُ وَارِثٌ فَوَارِثُهُ أَقْرَبُ النَّاسِ إِلَيْهِ، وَلَا يَرِثُ الْقَاتِلُ شَيْئًا» (سنن أبي داود، باب ديات الأعضاء، رقم 4564/سنن الترمذي، باب ما جاء في إبطال ميراث القاتل، رقم 2109)
وَجْهٌ : (۱) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَالْكُفْرُ كُلُّهُ مِلَّةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ يَتَوَارَثُ حَدَّثَنَا سُفْيَانُ: «الْإِسْلَامُ مِلَّةٌ، وَالشِّرْكُ مِلَّةٌ» (مصنف ابن شيبه في النصراني يرث اليهودي واليهودي يرث النصراني، رقم 31453)
وَجْهٌ : (۲) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَالْكُفْرُ كُلُّهُ مِلَّةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ يَتَوَارَثُ بِهِ أَهْلُهُ عَنْ ابْنِ أَبِي لَيْلَى، عَنْ أَبِي الزُّبَيْرِ، عَنْ جَابِرٍ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا يَتَوَارَثُ أَهْلُ مِلَّتَيْنِ» (سنن الترمذي، باب لا يتوارث أهل ملتين، رقم 2108)
وَجْهٌ : (۱) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يَرِثُ الْمُسْلِمُ الْكَافِرَ وَلَا الْكَافِرُ الْمُسْلِمَ عَنْ أُسَامَةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ رضي الله عنهما : أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا يَرِثُ الْمُسْلِمُ الْكَافِرَ وَلَا الْكَافِرُ الْمُسْلِمَ» (صحيح البخاري، باب: لا يرث المسلم الكافر ولا الكافر المسلم، رقم 6764)
وَجْهٌ : (۱) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَالُ الْمُرْتَدِّ لِوَرَثَتِهِ مِنْ الْمُسْلِمِينَ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ، أَنَّهُ أُتِيَ بِمُسْتَوْرِدِ الْعِجْلِيِّ وَقَدِ ارْتَدَّ، فَعَرَضَ عَلَيْهِ الْإِسْلَامَ، فَأَبَى فَقَتَلَهُ وَجَعَلَ مِيرَاثَهُ بَيْنَ وَرَثَتِهِ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ (مصنف ابن شيبه، في المرتد عن الإسلام، رقم 13384/مصنف عبد الرزاق، رقم 19296)
وَجْهٌ : (۱) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا غَرِقَ جَمَاعَةٌ أَوْ سَقَطَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَائِطٌ عَنْ عُمَرَ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يُوَرِّثُ الْأَحْيَاءَ مِنَ الْأَمْوَاتِ، وَلَا يُوَرِّثُ الْغَرْقَى بَعْضَهُمْ مِنْ بَعْضٍ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من قال: يرث كل واحد منهم وارثه من الناس ولا يورث بعضهم من بعض، رقم 31349)
وَجْهٌ : (۱) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا اجْتَمَعَ فِي الْمَجُوسِيِّ قَرَابَتَانِ سَأَلْتُ حَمَّادًا، عَنْ مِيرَاثِ الْمَجُوسِيِّ، قَالَ: «يَرِثُونَ مِنَ الْوَجْهِ الَّذِي يَحِلُّ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، من قال: يرث كل واحد منهم وارثه من الناس ولا يورث بعضهم من بعض، رقم 31425)
وَجْهٌ : (۲) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا اجْتَمَعَ فِي الْمَجُوسِيِّ قَرَابَتَانِ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، قَالَ: «لَا يَرِثُ الْمَجُوسِيُّ إِلَّا بِوَجْهٍ وَاحِدٍ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبه، من قال: يرث كل واحد منهم وارثه، رقم 31423)
وَجْهٌ : (۱) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يَرِثُ الْمَجُوسِيُّ بِالْأَنْكِحَةِ الْفَاسِدَةِ سَأَلْتُ حَمَّادًا، عَنْ مِيرَاثِ الْمَجُوسِيِّ، قَالَ: «يَرِثُونَ مِنَ الْوَجْهِ الَّذِي يَحِلُّ» (مصنف ابن شيبه، من قال: يرث كل واحد منهم وارثه، رقم 31425)
أصول: نسبی اور خاندانی رشتہ داروں کو ان کے حصے کے مطابق دوبارہ تقسیم کرنا رد کہلاتا ہے، اور چونکہ میاں اور بیوی نسبی رشتہ میں داخل نہیں ہیں اسلئے ان کو دوبارہ حصہ نہیں ملے گا، انہیں سہام پر اکتفا کرنا پڑے گا۔
أصول: تمام کافر خواہ یہودی ہو یا نصرانی ایک دوسرے کے وارث بنیں گے گویا وہ ایک ہی مذہب ہو۔
أصول: دو قرابتوں میں سے جو قریب تر ہو اس قرابت سے وارث بنے گا۔
أصول: جو قرابت حلال طریقے پر ہو اس قرابت کی وجہ سے وارث بنے گا۔
Chapter of Return: He (the author, may Allah have mercy on him) said: The surplus over the fixed shares of the possessors of shares, when there is no residuary heir, is returned to them in proportion to their shares, except to the two spouses. And the killer does not inherit from the killed. And all disbelief is one millah; its people inherit through it. And a Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever, nor does a disbeliever from a Muslim. And the property of an apostate is for his Muslim heirs, and what he acquired during his apostasy is a fay for the Muslims. And when a group drowns or a wall falls upon them and it is not known who died first, then the property of each one of them is for the living among his heirs. And when in a Magian there combine two relationships which if separated would be in two persons, he inherits through each one of them. And a Magian does not inherit through the invalid marriages that they deem lawful in their religion.
Proof (1): The hadith to establish the surplus over the fixed shares: from Ibrahim that 'Ali used to return to every possessor of a share except the husband and wife (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, in al-Radd wa Ikhtilafihim fih, no. 31168).
Proof (2): The hadith to establish the surplus over the fixed shares: Ibrahim said: None of the Companions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to return anything to the wife and husband. He said: Zayd used to give every possessor of a fixed share his share, and whatever remained he placed in the treasury (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, in al-Radd wa Ikhtilafihim fih, no. 31176).
Proof (1): The hadith to establish that the killer does not inherit from the killed: from 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb, from his father, from his grandfather, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to assess the blood money for accidental killing on the townspeople as four hundred dinars... And the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ruled that the blood money of a woman is among her 'asaba (residuary heirs) whoever they are, they do not inherit from her anything except what remains over her heirs; and if she is killed, her blood money is among her heirs, and they kill her killer; and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'There is nothing for the killer, and if he has no heir, then his heir is the nearest person to him, and the killer does not inherit anything' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Diyat al-A'da', no. 4564 / Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Ibtal Mirath al-Qatil, no. 2109).
Proof (1): The saying of the Tabi'i to establish that all disbelief is one millah: Sufyan narrated: 'Islam is a millah, and shirk is a millah' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, in al-Nasrani yarith al-Yahudi wa al-Yahudi yarith al-Nasrani, no. 31453).
Proof (2): The hadith to establish that all disbelief is one millah: from Ibn Abi Layla, from Abu al-Zubayr, from Jabir, from the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'People of two different millahs do not inherit from each other' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, La Yatawarath Ahl Millatayn, no. 2108).
Proof (1): The hadith to establish that a Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever nor a disbeliever from a Muslim: from Usama ibn Zayd (may Allah be pleased with them both): The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'A Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever, nor a disbeliever from a Muslim' (Sahih al-Bukhari, La yarith al-Muslim al-Kafir wa la al-Kafir al-Muslim, no. 6764).
Proof (1): The saying of the Companion to establish that the property of an apostate is for his Muslim heirs: from 'Ali: Mustawrid al-'Ijli was brought to him while he had apostatized; he presented Islam to him, but he refused, so he killed him and made his inheritance among his Muslim heirs (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, in al-Murtadd 'an al-Islam, no. 13384 / Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, no. 19296).
Proof (1): The saying of the Tabi'i to establish that when a group drowns or a wall falls upon them: from 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz that he used to give inheritance to the living from the dead, and did not give inheritance among the drowned to each other (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Man qala: yarith kullu wahidin minhum warithuhu min al-nas wa la yuwarrath ba'dahum min ba'd, no. 31349).
Proof (1): The hadith to establish that when in a Magian there combine two relationships: I asked Hammad about the inheritance of the Magian; he said: 'They inherit from the aspect that is lawful' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Man qala: yarith kullu wahidin minhum warithuhu min al-nas wa la yuwarrath ba'dahum min ba'd, no. 31425).
Proof (2): The saying of the Tabi'i to establish that when in a Magian there combine two relationships: from al-Zuhri, he said: 'A Magian does not inherit except through one aspect' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Man qala: yarith kullu wahidin minhum warithuhu, no. 31423).
Proof (1): The saying of the Tabi'i to establish that a Magian does not inherit through invalid marriages: I asked Hammad about the inheritance of the Magian; he said: 'They inherit from the aspect that is lawful' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, no. 31425).
Principles: Returning (radd) refers to redistributing the surplus to blood and family relatives according to their shares; and since the husband and wife are not included in the blood relationship, they will not receive a share again; they will have to be content with their fixed shares.
Principles: All disbelievers, whether Jewish or Christian, will inherit from each other as if they are of the same religion.
Principles: Of the two relationships, the one that is closer will inherit through that relationship.
Principles: He will inherit through the relationship that is lawful.
Source pages p. 449

Commentary
This passage is the text of the matn from al-Quduri covering the chapter on al-Radd (Return of Surplus in Inheritance) along with its proofs from hadith and athar. The author first states the ruling on the return of surplus: when there are fixed-share heirs but no residuary heir ('asaba), the surplus is returned to them proportionally. However, the spouses (husband and wife) are excluded from this return because they are not blood relatives; their shares are fixed and they do not receive additional inheritance from the surplus. The proof cited is the practice of 'Ali (radiya Allahu 'anhu) and the statement of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i that none of the Companions returned anything to the spouses, and Zayd ibn Thabit would place the surplus in the public treasury. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools have differences.

Next, the text states that a killer does not inherit from the person he killed. This is established by the hadith of 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb wherein the Prophet (sallallahu 'alayhi wa sallam) ruled that the killer has nothing, and if he has no heir, the nearest relative inherits instead. This is a general prohibition to prevent the killer from benefiting from his crime.

The third ruling is that all forms of disbelief (kufr) are considered one millah (religious community) for purposes of inheritance. Thus a Jew can inherit from a Christian and vice versa, because they share the common bond of disbelief. This is supported by the saying of Sufyan al-Thawri that 'Islam is a millah, and shirk is a millah,' and the hadith 'People of two different millahs do not inherit from each other,' implying that within the same millah of disbelief, inheritance is possible.

Then the text states the well-established rule that a Muslim does not inherit from a disbeliever, nor a disbeliever from a Muslim, based on the authentic hadith in Bukhari.

The property of an apostate goes to his Muslim heirs at the time of his death, but any wealth he acquired during his apostasy becomes fay' (war booty for the Muslim state). This is based on the practice of 'Ali (radiya Allahu 'anhu) with Mustawrid al-'Ijli.

When a group dies simultaneously in a drowning or building collapse without knowing who died first, they do not inherit from each other; each deceased's property goes to his own living heirs. This is based on the practice of 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz.

Finally, for Magians (Zoroastrians), their inheritance is based on the nearest lawful relationship. If two relationships coincide, they inherit through the closer one. They do not inherit through marriages that are considered invalid in Islam, even if those marriages are considered lawful in their own religion. This principle is derived from the statements of Hammad and al-Zuhri.

The Urdu commentary (usul) at the end summarizes: radd is returning surplus to blood relatives proportionally, excluding spouses; all disbelievers inherit from each other as one faith; among two relationships, the closer takes priority; inheritance is only through lawful relationships.

Key Terms
الرَّد (al-radd): The return of surplus from an estate to the fixed-share heirs proportionally after their prescribed shares have been given, when there is no residuary heir.
عَصَبَة ('asabah): Residuary heirs who inherit the remaining estate after fixed shares are distributed, typically male agnates.
مِلَّة (millah): A religious community or creed; used here to denote that all disbelievers (Jews, Christians, etc.) are considered one community for inheritance purposes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to the surplus of an estate when there are fixed-share heirs but no residuary heir, and the deceased left a wife and a daughter?
A) The surplus goes to the public treasury.
B) The surplus is returned to the wife proportionally.
C) The surplus is returned to the daughter proportionally, but not to the wife.
D) The surplus is divided equally between the wife and daughter.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi faraid, radd returns surplus to blood fixed-share heirs except spouses; all kufr is one millah; a killer cannot inherit; apostate's wealth goes to Muslim heirs; simultaneous death prevents mutual inheritance; Magians inherit only through lawful relationships.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
8 min
The 'Asabah of a Child of Zina or Li'an
Ruling on inheritance of child of zina/li'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the inheritance of a child of zina or li'an and identify the proofs from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
A child of zina or li'an inherits from the mother and her relatives, not from the biological father.

In Hanafi inheritance law, the legal parentage of a child determines the line of heirs. For a child born from zina (adultery) or li'an (mutual imprecation), paternity is legally severed. This lesson examines the ruling on who serves as the child's 'asabah (agnatic heirs) and the proofs from the Prophet's ﷺ teachings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Subject
Recognize that the ruling concerns children born from zina (illicit relations) or li'an (a formal denial of paternity in court).
2
State the Hanafi Ruling
The child's inheritance goes to the mother and her heirs (maternal relatives), not to the biological father, nor does the father inherit from the child.
3
Examine the First Hadith
The hadith from Makhul (Sunan Abi Dawud 2907) explicitly gives the inheritance of the child of li'an to his mother and her heirs.
This is the primary proof for the li'an case.
4
Examine the Second and Third Hadiths
The hadith of Ibn Umar (Bukhari 6748) confirms the child is attached to the mother after li'an. The hadith of Amr ibn Shu'ayb (Abu Dawud 2113) denies inheritance for the child of zina entirely.
Together, these establish the rule for both zina and li'an.
5
Conclude with the Hanafi Position
The school holds that no inheritance exists between the biological father and the child; the child's 'asabah are from the mother's side.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الرَّدِّ وَعَصَبَةُ وَلَدِ الزَّنَا وَوَلَدِ الْمُلَاعَنَةِ مِنَ الْأُمَّهَاتِ. حَدَّثَنَا مَكْحُولٌ قَالَ: جَعَلَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم مِيرَاثَ ابْنِ الْمُلَاعَنَةِ لِأُمِّهِ وَلِوَرَثَتِهَا مِنْ بَعْدِهَا (سنن أبو داود، باب ميراث ابن الملاعنة، رقم 2907). وَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما أَنَّ رَجُلًا لَاعَنَ امْرَأَتَهُ فِي زَمَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَانْتَفَى مِنْ وَلَدِهَا، فَفَرَّقَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم بَيْنَهُمَا وَأَلْحَقَ الْوَلَدَ بِالْمَرْأَةِ (صحيح البخاري، باب ميراث الملاعنة، رقم 6748). وَعَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «أَيُّمَا رَجُلٍ عَاهَرَ بِحُرَّةٍ أَوْ أَمَةٍ فَالْوَلَدُ وَلَدُ زِنًا لَا يَرِثُ وَلَا يُورَثُ» (سنن أبو داود، باب ما جاء في إبطال ميراث ولد الزنا، رقم 2113). وَالْعَمَلُ عَلَى هَذَا عِنْدَ أَهْلِ الْعِلْمِ أَنَّ وَلَدَ الزَّنَا لَا يَرِثُ مِنْ أَبِيهِ. اصول: جس عورت سے لعان كيا اس عورت كا وه بچه باپ كا وارث نهيں هو گا، اور نه باپ اس كا وارث هو گا.
Chapter of Return. The agnatic heirs of a child of zina and a child of li'an are from the mothers. Narrated to us Makhul: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) gave the inheritance of the child of li'an to his mother and to her heirs after her. And from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them): A man performed li'an with his wife during the Prophet's time and denied her child, so the Prophet separated them and attached the child to the woman. And from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Any man who commits zina with a free woman or slave, the child is a child of zina, he does not inherit nor is he inherited from.' And the practice among the people of knowledge is that the child of zina does not inherit from his father. Principle: For a woman with whom li'an was performed, that child will not inherit from the father, nor will the father inherit from him.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on the inheritance of a child born from zina (adultery) or li'an (mutual imprecation). The text clarifies that such a child's 'asabah (agnatic heirs) are from the mother's side, meaning the child inherits from the mother and her relatives, but not from the biological father. The ruling is supported by three hadiths: the first (from Makhul) specifically states that the child of li'an inherits from the mother and her heirs; the second (Ibn Umar) confirms that the child is attributed to the mother; the third (Amr ibn Shu'ayb) explicitly denies inheritance between the father and child of zina. The Urdu principle reiterates the same for li'an. Note: The Hanafi school maintains that a child of zina or li'an has no paternal lineage and thus no inheritance rights from the father or to the father.

Key Terms
عصبة (asabah): Agnatic heirs – those entitled to the residue of the estate after fixed shares.
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): Child born from illicit sexual relations (zina).
الملاعنة (al-mula'anah): Li'an – mutual imprecation between spouses leading to separation and denial of paternity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) From the biological father
B) From the mother and her heirs
C) From both parents equally
D) From no one

Key Takeaway
A child of zina or li'an inherits only from the mother and her relatives; the biological father has no inheritance rights.

Suspending Inheritance for a Pregnant Widow
Ruling on postponing estate distribution for pregnant widow

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on suspending the estate when a deceased leaves a pregnant wife, explain the evidence from the hadith, and apply the condition of live birth.

Core Idea
The estate must be suspended until birth to protect the unborn child's potential inheritance right.

When a man dies and his wife is pregnant, the unborn child may be an heir. Islamic law safeguards this potential right by postponing distribution until after delivery. This lesson covers the ruling and its proof from the Prophet's hadith: 'When the newborn cries out, he inherits.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Act and Ruling
The act is the suspension (waqf) of the deceased's estate. The ruling is that it is obligatory (wajib) to postpone distribution until the wife gives birth.
This protects the potential heir's share.
2
Locate the Dalil (Evidence)
The evidence is the hadith from Abu Hurayrah: 'When the newborn cries out (at birth), he inherits.' This is a Sunnah ahad, transmitted zanni al-thubut but qati al-dalala in meaning.
The hadith establishes the condition for inheritance.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (Legal Indication)
The conditional clause 'idha istahalla' (when he cries) makes inheritance contingent on a live birth. Since the status of the fetus is unknown, distribution must wait until birth confirms life.
Istihlal (crying) is the minimal sign of life.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf (Disagreement)
There is no significant intra-Hanafi or inter-madhhab dispute on this principle; it is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon). All schools require live birth for inheritance.
Minor differences exist on the waiting period, but the suspension itself is unanimous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ مَاتَ وَتَرَكَ حَمَلًا وُقِفَ مَالُهُ حَتَّى تَضَعَ امْرَأَتُهُ. عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ قَالَ: «إِذَا اسْتَهَلَّ الْمَوْلُودُ وَرِثَ» (سنن أبو داود، باب في المولود يستهل ثم يموت، رقم 2920).
And whoever dies and leaves a pregnancy (fetus), his wealth is suspended until his wife gives birth. From Abu Hurayrah from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'When the newborn cries out (at birth), he inherits.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on newborn who cries then dies, no. 2920)
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that if a man dies and leaves his wife pregnant, the distribution of his estate is postponed until the child is born. This is because the fetus has a potential inheritance share as a legal heir (e.g., if it is a son, it may take a share or become residuary). The hadith of Abu Hurayrah provides the proof: a newborn inherits if it shows signs of life (by crying). Thus, the estate must be held until the child is born alive to determine its share. If the child is stillborn (no cry), the inheritance is distributed as if the child never existed.

Key Terms
حمل (haml): Fetus or pregnancy – an unborn child whose inheritance rights are potential.
استهل (istahalla): To cry out at birth – sign of life that confirms live birth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To wait for the wife to remarry
B) To determine if the child is born alive and thus entitled to inheritance
C) Because pregnancy invalidates all inheritance rights
D) To give time for debts to be paid

Key Takeaway
The inheritance of a fetus is contingent on live birth; distribution must wait until that is determined.

Grandfather's Inheritance with Siblings: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether grandfather excludes siblings or shares with them

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on grandfather's inheritance with siblings and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between them.

Core Idea
The grandfather excludes siblings per Abu Hanifa, but shares (minimum 1/3) per the Sahibayn — the latter is the mufta bihi.

In this lesson, we examine an important intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the inheritance of the paternal grandfather when siblings of the deceased are present. The difference of opinion between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, has practical consequences in estate distribution. Understanding this dispute will help you recognize how the Hanafi school resolved it and which position is relied upon today.

Guided Path
1
State the two positions
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa (grandfather excludes siblings) and the ruling of the Sahibayn (muqasamah with minimum one-third).
2
Identify the evidence
For Abu Hanifa: hadith of Imran ibn Husayn, qawl of Abu Bakr; for Sahibayn: practice of Umar and Uthman, hadith of Zuhri.
Note the different interpretations of the same sources.
3
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, siblings get nothing; under Sahibayn, they share with the grandfather.
This is the practical consequence in estate distribution.
4
Determine the tarjih
Later Hanafi scholars favoured the Sahibayn's view, making it the mufta bihi.
The reliance on caliphal practice and ease for heirs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْجَدُّ أَوْلَى بِالْمَالِ مِنَ الْإِخْوَةِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ. وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يُقَاسِمُهُمْ إِلَّا أَنْ تُنْقِصَهُ الْمُقَاسَمَةُ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ. وَقَالَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ وَابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ وَابْنُ الزُّبَيْرِ: الْجَدُّ أَبٌ. وَقَرَأَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ {يَا بَنِي آدَمَ} {وَاتَّبَعْتُ مِلَّةَ آبَائِي إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَإِسْحَاقَ وَيَعْقُوبَ} وَلَمْ يُذْكَرْ أَنَّ أَحَدًا خَالَفَ أَبَا بَكْرٍ فِي زَمَانِهِ وَأَصْحَابُ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مُتَوَافِرُونَ. وَقَالَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ: يَرِثُنِي ابْنُ ابْنِي دُونَ إِخْوَتِي وَلَا أَرِثُ أَنَا ابْنَ ابْنِي. وَيُذْكَرُ عَنْ عُمَرَ وَعَلِيٍّ وَابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ وَزَيْدٍ أَقَاوِيلُ مُخْتَلِفَةٌ. وَعَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ أَنَّ رَجُلًا أَتَى النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَقَالَ: إِنَّ ابْنَ ابْنِي مَاتَ فَمَا لِي مِنْ مِيرَاثِهِ؟ فَقَالَ: «لَكَ السُّدُسُ» فَلَمَّا أَدْبَرَ دَعَاهُ فَقَالَ: «لَكَ سُدُسٌ آخَرُ» فَلَمَّا أَدْبَرَ دَعَاهُ فَقَالَ: «إِنَّ السُّدُسَ الْآخَرَ طُعْمَةٌ» قَالَ قَتَادَةُ: فَلَا يَدْرُونَ مَعَ أَيِّ شَيْءٍ وَرَّثَهُ. قَالَ قَتَادَةُ: أَقَلُّ شَيْءٍ وَرِثَ الْجَدُّ السُّدُسُ. وَعَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ قَالَ: كَانَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ يُشْرِكُ بَيْنَ الْجَدِّ وَالْأَخِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ غَيْرُهُمَا وَيَجْعَلُ لَهُ الثُّلُثَ مَعَ الْأَخَوَيْنِ، وَمَا كَانَتِ الْمُقَاسَمَةُ خَيْرًا لَهُ قَاسَمَ وَلَا يُنْقِصُ مِنَ السُّدُسِ فِي جَمِيعِ الْمَالِ. ثُمَّ أَثَارَهَا زَيْدٌ بَعْدَهُ وَفَشَتْ عَنْهُ. وَحَضَرْتُ الْخَلِيفَتَيْنِ قَبْلَكَ — يُرِيدُ عُمَرَ وَعُثْمَانَ — يَقْضِيَانِ لِلْجَدِّ مَعَ الْأَخِ الْوَاحِدِ النِّصْفَ، وَمَعَ الِاثْنَيْنِ الثُّلُثَ، فَإِذَا كَانُوا أَكْثَرَ مِنْ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يُنْقِصْ مِنَ الثُّلُثِ شَيْئًا.
And the grandfather has precedence over siblings in the estate according to Abu Hanifa. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He shares with them (muqasamah) unless the sharing (muqasamah) reduces him below one-third. And Abu Bakr, Ibn Abbas, and Ibn al-Zubayr said: The grandfather is a father. And Ibn Abbas recited {O children of Adam} and {I followed the religion of my fathers Ibrahim, Ishaq, and Ya'qub} and it is not mentioned that anyone opposed Abu Bakr in his time while the Companions of the Prophet were abundant. And Ibn Abbas said: My grandson (son's son) inherits from me over my brothers, and I do not inherit from my grandson. And differing sayings are mentioned from Umar, Ali, Ibn Mas'ud, and Zayd. And from Imran ibn Husayn that a man came to the Prophet and said: My grandson died, what do I get from his inheritance? He said: 'You have one-sixth.' When he turned away, he called him and said: 'You have another sixth.' When he turned away, he called him and said: 'That other sixth is a gift (tu'mah).' Qatadah said: So they do not know with what he (the Prophet) caused him to inherit. Qatadah said: The least thing the grandfather inherited was one-sixth. And from al-Zuhri: Umar ibn al-Khattab used to share between the grandfather and the brother when there was no one else, and he gave him one-third with two brothers, and whenever sharing was better for him, he shared, and he did not reduce below one-sixth in the entire estate. Then Zayd (ibn Thabit) took it up after him and it spread from him. And I attended the two caliphs before you — meaning Umar and Uthman — they used to decree for the grandfather with one brother one-half, and with two brothers one-third, and if there were more than that, he was not reduced below one-third.
Source pages p. 451

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the inheritance of the grandfather (i.e., the father's father) when he is present with siblings of the deceased. Abu Hanifa's position is that the grandfather excludes the siblings entirely and takes the whole estate (as if he were the father). The Sahibayn hold that the grandfather shares (yuqasim) with the siblings, but his share is not allowed to fall below one-third. The text then provides evidence from the practices of the Companions and hadith. The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn shows the grandfather receiving one-sixth in that case, but the Sahibayn interpret this as minimal. The practice of Umar and Uthman (as narrated by Zuhri and others) supports the sharing approach with a minimum of one-third. This difference is practical: under Abu Hanifa's view, siblings get nothing if the grandfather is present; under the Sahibayn's view, they share. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is the view of the Sahibayn (muqasamah with minimum one-third), as it is easier and based on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs.

Key Terms
الجد (al-jadd): Paternal grandfather (father's father).
المقاسمة (al-muqasamah): Sharing proportionally among heirs; in this context, the grandfather and siblings divide the estate as if the grandfather were a brother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, what is the minimum share a grandfather receives when inheriting with siblings?
A) One-half
B) One-third
C) One-sixth
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position on grandfather's inheritance with siblings is muqasamah (sharing) with a minimum of one-third, based on the practice of the caliphs.

Inheritance of Grandmothers: Nearness and Blocking
Rules on which grandmothers inherit and how they block each other

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules for grandmother inheritance in the Hanafi school and apply the blocking (hajb) rules among grandmothers.

Core Idea
A grandmother inherits one-sixth only if no mother exists; the nearest grandmother blocks the distant.

In Hanafi faraid, grandmothers are eligible for a fixed one-sixth share, but their entitlement is highly dependent on the presence of other heirs, especially the mother. This lesson unpacks the key principles from the classical source, including how nearness determines the recipient of the sixth and how blocking works between grandmothers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
When multiple grandmothers are alive (e.g., paternal and maternal), who inherits the one-sixth share?
The scenario assumes no mother is present; otherwise all grandmothers are blocked.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The nearest grandmother in degree to the deceased takes the entire sixth. If two are equally near, they share it equally. Additionally, a grandfather blocks his own mother, and each grandmother blocks her own mother (great-grandmother).
3
Examine the dalil
The hadith from Ibn Buraydah (Sunan Abi Dawud 2895) establishes the grandmother's sixth conditional on the absence of a mother. The story of Umar (Sunan Abi Dawud 2894) shows the rule when two grandmothers are present.
The dalil uses the condition 'if there is no mother below her', indicating that mother blocks grandmother completely.
4
Apply the blocking rules
The mother of the deceased blocks all grandmothers (paternal and maternal). Among grandmothers, nearer blocks more distant. For example, paternal grandmother blocks her own mother (great-grandmother).
5
Resolve equal closeness
If two grandmothers are equally close (e.g., paternal and maternal grandmother of the same generation), they share the one-sixth equally. This is from the practice of Umar.
If only one grandmother is present, she takes the entire sixth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اجْتَمَعَ الْجَدَّاتُ فَالسُّدُسُ لِأَقْرَبِهِنَّ. وَيَحْجُبُ الْجَدُّ أُمَّهُ. وَلَا تَرِثُ أُمُّ أَبِي الْأُمِّ. وَكُلُّ جَدَّةٍ تَحْجُبُ أُمَّهَا. عَنِ الْحَسَنِ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يُوَرِّثُ ثَلَاثَ جَدَّاتٍ وَيَقُولُ: أَيَّتُهُنَّ كَانَتْ أَقْرَبَ فَهُوَ لَهَا دُونَ الْأُخْرَى، فَإِذَا اسْتَوَتَا فَهُوَ بَيْنَهُمَا. وَعَنِ ابْنِ بُرَيْدَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم جَعَلَ لِلْجَدَّةِ السُّدُسَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ دُونَهَا أُمٌّ (سنن أبو داود، باب في الجدة، رقم 2895). وَعَنِ الْجَدَّةِ الْأُخْرَى إِلَى عُمَرَ بْنِ الْخَطَّابِ تَسْأَلُهُ مِيرَاثَهَا فَقَالَ: مَا لَكِ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى شَيْءٌ، وَمَا كَانَ الْقَضَاءُ الَّذِي قُضِيَ بِهِ إِلَّا لِغَيْرِكِ، وَمَا أَنَا بِزَائِدٍ فِي الْفَرَائِضِ، وَلَكِنْ هُوَ ذَلِكَ السُّدُسُ، فَإِنِ اجْتَمَعْتُمَا فِيهِ فَهُوَ بَيْنَكُمَا، وَأَيَّتُكُمَا خَلَتْ بِهِ فَهُوَ لَهَا (سنن أبو داود، باب في الجدة، رقم 2894). اصُول: تمام جدات یعنی دادیوں اور نانیوں کا چھٹا حصہ ہی ہے۔ اصول: ماں ہو تو دادی اور نانی کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا، کیونکہ ماں دادی اور نانی کو محجوب کر دیتی ہے۔
And when grandmothers gather (are many), the sixth is for the nearest among them. And the grandfather blocks his mother. And the mother of the maternal grandmother does not inherit. And every grandmother blocks her mother. From al-Hasan that he used to make three grandmothers inherit and said: whichever of them is nearer, it (the sixth) is for her to the exclusion of the other, and if they are equal, then it is between them. And from Ibn Buraydah from his father that the Prophet (peace be upon him) allocated the sixth to the grandmother when there is no mother below her (Sunan Abi Dawud, chapter on the grandmother, no. 2895). And regarding the other grandmother (who came) to Umar ibn al-Khattab asking him about her inheritance, he said: You have nothing in the Book of Allah, and the judgment that was given was only for someone else, and I am not one to add to the prescribed shares, but it is that same sixth: if you both gather in it, it is between you two, and whichever of you is alone with it, it is for her (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 2894). Principle: All grandmothers, meaning paternal and maternal grandmothers, only have the sixth. Principle: If the mother is present, the grandmother (both sides) gets nothing, because the mother blocks the grandmother.
Source pages p. 452

Commentary
This passage outlines the rules for grandmothers' inheritance. The primary rule: when multiple grandmothers exist (e.g., paternal grandmother, maternal grandmother, etc.), the fixed share of one-sixth (suduk) goes to the one who is nearest in degree to the deceased. For example, the mother's mother (grandmother) is closer than the mother's mother's mother. The grandfather (paternal grandfather) blocks his own mother (i.e., the great-grandmother on the paternal side) from inheriting. Also, the mother of the maternal grandmother (i.e., the great-grandmother) does not inherit at all. Furthermore, every grandmother blocks her own mother (meaning the more distant grandmother is excluded by the nearer one). The hadith of Ibn Buraydah confirms the basic rule that a grandmother gets the sixth only if there is no mother intervening (i.e., no living mother). The story of Umar shows that when two grandmothers (different sides) both claim, Umar gives the sixth to be divided between them if equal in nearness. The Urdu principles summarize: all grandmothers only get the sixth, and if the mother is alive, the grandmother is totally blocked from inheritance.

Key Terms
جدات (jaddat): Grandmothers (paternal and maternal) as legal heirs.
حجب (hajb): Blocking – preventing a more distant heir from inheriting due to presence of a nearer heir.
سدس (suds): One-sixth share, the fixed portion for grandmothers (and other heirs).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a grandmother inherit a sixth according to the Hanafi school?
A) Always, regardless of other heirs
B) Only when there is no mother alive
C) Only when the grandfather is also present
D) Only if she is the paternal grandmother

Key Takeaway
A grandmother's right to the sixth is conditional on the absence of a mother, and among multiple grandmothers, the nearest takes priority.

Inheritance of Mawla al-Muwala: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Presenting Hanafi proofs and Shafi'i evidence for client by agreement inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that mawla al-muwala inherits and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A client by agreement (mawla al-muwala) inherits in the Hanafi school but not in the Shafi'i school.

This lesson examines the inter-madhhab dispute over the inheritance of mawla al-muwala (client by agreement). The Hanafi school relies on two Quranic verses, a hadith, and the practice of Umar to establish inheritance. The Shafi'i school, however, interprets the same verse as limiting inheritance to blood relatives. Understanding each school's proof structure is essential for grasping the legal reasoning behind differing rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: mawla al-muwala inherits from his patron. Recognize that this is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school.
The Hanafi school considers this a wajib right once the agreement is valid.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school holds that mawla al-muwala does not inherit; instead the estate goes to the Bayt al-Mal (public treasury).
This disagreement is based on different interpretations of the same Quranic texts.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school cites the same verse (al-Anfal 75) but restricts 'أولوا الأرحام' to blood relatives. They also cite al-Hasan al-Basri's opinion that the estate is for the Muslims.
Note that the Shafi'i use a saying of a Tabi'i (successor), not a Companion or hadith.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school counters with stronger evidence: an explicit hadith from Tamim ad-Dari where the Prophet (ﷺ) says the client is 'most entitled of people to his life and his death', and the practice of Umar. These indicate that the client inherits.
The Hanafi school argues that the verse's generality includes the client by agreement, and the hadith and Companion practice confirm this.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi law, the client inherits; under Shafi'i law, he does not, and the estate goes to the public treasury.
This difference affects estate planning and the validity of such agreements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ ذَوِي الْأَرْحَامِ وَمَوْلَى الْمُوَالَاةِ يَرِثُ
وَجْهٌ (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَوْلَى الْمُوَالَاةِ يَرِثُ ﴿وَأُولُوا الْأَرْحَامِ بَعْضُهُمْ أَوْلَى بِبَعْضٍ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ﴾ [الأنفال: 75]
وَجْهٌ (2) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَوْلَى الْمُوَالَاةِ يَرِثُ ﴿وَلِكُلٍّ جَعَلْنَا مَوَالِيَ مِمَّا تَرَكَ الْوَالِدَانِ وَالْأَقْرَبُونَ وَالَّذِينَ عَقَدَتْ أَيْمَانُكُمْ فَآتُوهُمْ نَصِيبَهُمْ﴾ [النساء: 33]
وَجْهٌ (3) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَوْلَى الْمُوَالَاةِ يَرِثُ عَنْ تَمِيمٍ الدَّارِيِّ، أَنَّهُ قَالَ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، مَا السُّنَّةُ فِي الرَّجُلِ يُسْلِمُ عَلَى يَدَيِ الرَّجُلِ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، قَالَ: «هُوَ أَوْلَى النَّاسِ بِمَحْيَاهُ وَمَمَاتِهِ» (سنن أبي داود، باب في الرجل يسلم على يدي الرجل، رقم 2918)
وَجْهٌ (4) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَوْلَى الْمُوَالَاةِ يَرِثُ أَنَّ عُمَرَ بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ، قَالَ: «إِذَا وَالَى رَجُلٌ رَجُلًا، فَلَهُ مِيرَاثُهُ، وَعَلَيْهِ عَقْلُهُ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، رقم 31578)
ثُمَّ ذَكَرَ دَلِيلَ الشَّافِعِيِّ: وَجْهٌ (1) دَلِيلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَوْلَى الْمُوَالَاةِ يَرِثُ ﴿وَأُولُوا الْأَرْحَامِ بَعْضُهُمْ أَوْلَى بِبَعْضٍ﴾
وَجْهٌ (2) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَوْلَى الْمُوَالَاةِ يَرِثُ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، قَالَا: «مِيرَاثُهُ لِلْمُسْلِمِينَ، وَعَقْلُهُ عَلَيْهِمْ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، رقم 31585)
Chapter of Dhawil Arham. And the client by agreement inherits. Proof (1) The verse to establish that the client by agreement inherits: 'And those of kinship are more entitled to one another in the decree of Allah.' [Surah al-Anfal 75] Proof (2) The verse to establish that the client by agreement inherits: 'And for all We have made inheritors of what parents and relatives leave; and those with whom you have made a covenant, give them their share.' [Surah an-Nisa 33] Proof (3) The hadith to establish that the client by agreement inherits from Tamim ad-Dari that he said: O Messenger of Allah, what is the sunnah regarding a man who accepts Islam at the hands of another man? He said: 'He is the most entitled of people to his life and his death.' Proof (4) The saying of the Companion to establish that the client by agreement inherits: 'Umar ibn al-Khattab said: When a man makes a clientage agreement with another man, his inheritance belongs to him, and his blood money is upon him.' Then he mentioned the proof of al-Shafi'i: Proof (1) The proof of al-Shafi'i is the verse to establish that the client by agreement inherits: 'And those of kinship are more entitled.' Proof (2) The saying of the Tabi'i to establish that the client by agreement inherits from al-Hasan: 'His inheritance is for the Muslims, and his blood money is upon them.'

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the inheritance of mawla al-muwala (client by agreement). The Hanafi school holds that such a client inherits, supported by four proofs: two Quranic verses (al-Anfal 75 and an-Nisa 33), a hadith from Tamim ad-Dari, and the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab. The Shafi'i school uses the same verse from al-Anfal to argue that inheritance is limited to blood relatives, and also cites al-Hasan al-Basri's opinion that the estate goes to the public treasury. The Hanafi response is implicit in the strength of their proofs, especially the explicit hadith. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
مَوْلَى الْمُوَالَاةِ (mawla al-muwalāh): A person who enters into a clientage agreement (walā') with another, agreeing to inherit from each other and pay blood money, without actual slavery or emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Quranic verse from Surah an-Nisa (4:33)

D) Saying of al-Hasan al-Basri

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes mawla al-muwala's inheritance through multiple strong proofs, while the Shafi'i school restricts inheritance to blood relatives.

Inheritance When Freed Slave Leaves Father and Son of Mawla
Ruling on distribution when freed slave leaves father and son of mawla

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the son of the mawla takes precedence over the father in inheriting from the freed slave, and identify the proof from the Companion Zaid ibn Thabit.

Core Idea
In wala inheritance, the son of the mawla excludes the father completely.

When a freed slave (mu'taq) dies, his patron (mawla) and the mawla's relatives inherit through wala. But who among the mawla's relatives gets priority? This passage from Al-Quduri resolves a specific conflict: the mawla's father versus the mawla's son. The ruling is clear and supported by a Companion's verdict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conflicting heirs
The freed slave leaves the father of his mawla and the son of his mawla. These are two potential heirs through wala.
Both are relatives of the mawla, not of the deceased directly.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The property goes entirely to the son of the mawla; the father gets nothing.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Locate the proof
The proof is the saying of Zaid ibn Thabit: "The property is for the son, and the father has nothing."
This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Analyse the proof's authority
The statement of a Companion (qawl sahabi) is accepted in Hanafi fiqh as a proof when it does not contradict Qiyas and is on a matter that cannot be based on personal opinion. Here, inheritance rules are tawqifi (based on revelation), so the Companion's word is decisive.
The thubut and dalala are both zanni but accepted as binding in practice.
5
Derive the underlying principle
The son is a stronger 'asabah than the father in the context of wala. The principle is that the closer relative by lineage to the mawla takes precedence.
This aligns with general inheritance rules where a son excludes a father in 'asabah.

Source Text

وَجْهٌ (1) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: وَقَالَ زَيْدُ بْنُ ثَابِتٍ: «الْمَالُ لِلِابْنِ، وَلَيْسَ لِلْأَبِ شَيْءٌ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، رقم 31520)
أُصُولٌ: مَيِّتٍ [؟] أَصْلٌ: وَلَدُ الْمَوْلَى مُقَدَّمٌ عَلَى أَبِيهِ فِي الْإِرْثِ.
And if the freed slave leaves behind the father of his mawla and the son of his mawla, then his property is for the son. Proof (1) The saying of the Companion to establish that: Zaid ibn Thabit said: 'The property is for the son, and the father has nothing.' Principles: ... Principle: The son of the mawla is preferred over the father in inheritance.

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: when a freed slave (mu'taq) dies leaving his mawla's father and son, the entire estate goes to the son. The father gets nothing. This is supported by the saying of Zaid ibn Thabit, a Companion. The underlying principle is that the son, being a closer relative by lineage, takes precedence over the father in the context of wala inheritance. This follows the general rule that a son is a stronger 'asabah than the father.

Key Terms
الْمُعْتَقُ (al-mu'taq): The freed slave who was emancipated and whose wala belongs to his mawla.
الْمَوْلَى (al-mawla): The patron who emancipated the slave and retains wala inheritance rights.

Key Takeaway
In wala inheritance, the son of the mawla takes precedence over the father, based on the Companion's ruling of Zaid ibn Thabit.

Inheritance of Wala: Grandfather vs Brother of Mawla
Ruling on wala inheritance with intra-Hanafi dispute and prohibition on sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the distribution of wala when a freed slave leaves both the grandfather and brother of the mawla, and explain why the grandfather's right is preferred (mufta bihi).

Core Idea
Wala follows lineage: the grandfather takes all because the patron is attributed to him, not to the brother.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on inheritance of wala (clientage rights). While the prohibition on selling or gifting wala is unanimous among the Hanafi imams, the division among heirs when the freed slave leaves both the grandfather and the brother of the mawla is contested. Understanding the basis of these rulings refines your grasp of how lineage determines legal relationships in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two separate rulings
The passage contains two distinct rulings: one on the distribution of wala inheritance (disputed) and one on the prohibition of selling or gifting wala (agreed). Separate them clearly.
The first ruling is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the second is based on a hadith.
2
Trace each imam's position on the disputed ruling
For the distribution of wala, note that Abu Hanifa gives the entire wala to the grandfather, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) say it is divided equally between the grandfather and the brother. Identify the evidence each side uses: al-Zuhri for the grandfather, and Ata' for equal division.
The text cites tabi'i opinions as evidence.
3
Analyse the basis of tarjih
Understand why Abu Hanifa's view is preferred (mufta bihi). The reasoning is that wala attaches to the lineage (nasab), and the grandfather is the source of lineage, while the brother is not. Al-Zuhri's fatwa supports this principle.
The tarjih authority is the text's presentation, implying al-Zuhri's view is stronger.
4
Confirm the agreed ruling and its dalil
For the prohibition of selling or gifting wala, cite the hadith from Ibn 'Umar. In Hanafi usul, the imperative 'nahy' indicates tahrim (prohibition). This ruling is unanimous.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear.

وَجْهٌ (1) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِنْ تَرَكَ جَدَّ مَوْلَاهُ وَأَخَ مَوْلَاهُ فَالْمَالُ لِلْجَدِّ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، فِي رَجُلٍ تَرَكَ جَدَّهُ وَأَخَاهُ قَالَ: «الْوَلَاءُ لِلْجَدِّ لِأَنَّهُ يُنْسَبُ إِلَى الْجَدِّ، وَلَا يُنْسَبُ إِلَى الْأَخِ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، رقم 31534)

وَجْهٌ (أ) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَا يُبَاعُ الْوَلَاءُ وَلَا يُوهَبُ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَنْ بَيْعِ الْوَلَاءِ، وَعَنْ هِبَتِهِ» (سنن أبي داود، باب في بيع الولاء، رقم 2919)
