And wala may not be sold nor gifted. Proof (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to establish that if he leaves the grandfather of his mawla and the brother of his mawla, the property is for the grandfather: from al-Zuhri regarding a man who left his grandfather and his brother, he said: 'The wala is for the grandfather because one is attributed to the grandfather, and not to the brother.' Proof (2) The saying of the Tabi'i to establish that from Ata' regarding a man who died leaving a mawla of his and his grandfather and his brother, to whom does the wala belong? Ata' said: 'The wala is between them in halves.' Proof (S) The hadith to establish that wala may not be sold nor gifted: from Ibn 'Umar, he said: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of wala and its gift.'

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings within an intra-Hanafi dispute. First, regarding the distribution of the wala inheritance when the freed slave leaves the grandfather of his mawla and the brother of his mawla: Abu Hanifa gives the entire wala to the grandfather, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is divided between them equally. The text provides supporting views from tabi'un: al-Zuhri supports the grandfather, while Ata' supports equal division. The second ruling is that wala (the right of inheritance arising from clientage) cannot be sold or gifted, based on a hadith from Ibn Umar. This ruling is agreed upon. The mufta bihi regarding the first dispute is the view of Abu Hanifa, as the grandfather is more closely related to the patron's lineage.

Key Terms
الْوَلَاءُ (al-walā'): The right of inheritance and responsibility for blood money arising from clientage (emancipation or agreement).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, wala is a non-transferable right that follows lineage; when a freed slave dies leaving both grandfather and brother of the mawla, the mufta bihi is that the grandfather inherits the entire wala.

Dispute on Wala Inheritance: Grandfather vs Brother
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wala inheritance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on wala inheritance when a freed slave leaves his grandfather and brother, and explain the proofs from tabi'i statements and the hadith on prohibition of selling wala.

Core Idea
Wala inheritance follows asabah hierarchy: grandfather takes all under Abu Hanifa, but Sahibayn split equally.

The wala (clientship) from freeing a slave is a special form of inheritance, akin to asabah. This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding who inherits the wala when a freed slave dies leaving his grandfather and his brother. The text from Al-Quduri presents the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the counter-opinion of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, along with proofs from the Salaf. Understanding this dispute clarifies the rules of asabah hierarchy and the unique nature of wala.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the three imams' positions
Read the passage and note the case: a freed slave dies leaving his grandfather and his brother. According to Abu Hanifa, the entire wala goes to the grandfather. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is divided equally. Tag these positions clearly.
Remember that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad are the Sahibayn, companions of Abu Hanifa.
2
Examine the proof for each position from tabi'i statements
The text cites al-Zuhri supporting Abu Hanifa (wala to grandfather because he is attributed to him) and Ata' supporting the Sahibayn (equal division). Also, opinions from Shuraih and Zayd ibn Thabit on a related case of son and father clarify the asabah hierarchy.
These are statements of the Salaf, used as supporting evidence, not primary revealed sources.
3
Understand the hadith prohibiting sale/gift of wala
The text includes a hadith from Ibn Umar: the Prophet forbade selling or gifting wala. This establishes that wala is a right that cannot be transferred by contract, only by inheritance as asabah.
The prohibition is taken as evidence of the sanctity of wala as a kinship-based right.
4
Apply the asabah hierarchy to determine the mufta bihi
The principles extracted state: the son is first asabah, then the father, then the nearest paternal relative. Since the grandfather is closer than the brother in the asabah line (grandfather being father's father, brother being sibling), Abu Hanifa's view that grandfather takes all is preferred. The Sahibayn's view may be based on considering both as equally distant? The text does not resolve, but later Hanafi practice favors Abu Hanifa.
The mufta bihi is the grandfather taking all, as per the majority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ ذَوِي الْأَرْحَامِ ك فَإِنْ تَرَكَ جَدَّ مَوْلاهُ وَأَخَ مَوْلاهُ فَالْمَالُ لِلْجَدِ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ وَهُوَ بَيْنَهُمَا وَلَا يُبَاعِ الْوَلاءُ وَلَا يُوهَبُ
وجه:(۲)الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا تَرَكَ الْمُعْتَقُ أَبَا مَوْلَاهُ \ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، قَالَ: «هُوَ لِلِابْنِ»( مصنف
ابن ابي شيبه رَجُلٌ مَاتَ وَتَرَكَ ابْنَهُ وَأَبَاهُ وَمَوْلَاهُ ، ثُمَّ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى وَتَرَكَ مَالًا ، غبر 31522) وجه:(۱)دليل ابي يوسف قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِذَا تَرَكَ الْمُعْتَقُ أَبَا مَوْلَاهُ عَنْ قَتَادَةَ، عَنْ شُرَيْحٍ،
وزَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ فِي رَجُلٍ مَاتَ وَتَرَكَ ابْنَهُ وَأَبَاهُ وَمَوْلَاهُ ، ثُمَّ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى وَتَرَكَ مَالًا، فَقَالَ شُرَيْح: «لِأَبِيهِ السُّدُسُ، وَمَا بَقِيَ فَلِلِابْنِ» وَقَالَ زَيْدُ بْنُ ثَابِتٍ: «الْمَالُ لِابْنِ، وَلَيْسَ لِلْأَبِ شَيْءٌ»( مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، رَجُلٌ مَاتَ وَتَرَكَ ابْنَهُ وَأَبَاهُ وَمَوْلَاهُ، ثُمَّ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى وَتَرَكَ مالا ، نمبر 31520)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ تَرَكَ جَدَّ مَوْلَاهُ وَأَخَ مَوْلاهُ فَالْمَالُ لِلْجَدِ \ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، فِي رَجُلٍ تَرَكَ جَدَّهُ وَأَخَاهُ قَالَ: «الْوَلَاءُ لِلْجَدِ لِأَنَّهُ يُنْسَبُ إِلَى الْجَدِ، وَلَا يُنْسَبُ إِلَى الْأَحْ» »( مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، رَجُلٌ مَاتَ وَتَرَكَ ابْنَهُ وَأَبَاهُ وَمَوْلَاهُ، ثُمَّ مَاتَ الْمَوْلَى وَتَرَكَ مالًا ، نمبر 31534)
وجه : (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِنْ تَرَكَ جَدَّ مَوْلَاهُ وَأَخَ مَوْلاهُ فَالْمَالُ لِلْجَدِ \ عَنْ عَطَاءِ، فِي رَجُل مَاتَ وَتَرَكَ مَوْلًى لَهُ وَجَدَّهُ وَأَخَاهُ لِمَنْ وَلَاءُ مَوْلاهُ، قَالَ عَطَاءُ: «الْوَلَاءُ بَيْنَهُمَا نِصْفَيْنِ» » (
مصنف ابن ابي شيبه، فِي رَجُلٍ مَاتَ وَتَرَكَ مَوْلًى لَهُ وَجَدَّهُ وَأَخَاهُ، لِمَنِ الْوَلَاءُ، نمبر 31532) دوجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُبَاع الْوَلَاءُ وَلَا يُوهَبُ \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما، قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ الْوَلَاءِ، وَعَنْ هِبَتِهِ»» (سنن ابوداود، بَابٌ فِي بَيْعِ الْوَلاءِ، نمبر 2919)
اصول : آزاد شده غلام کا مال عصبہ کے طور پر ملتا ہے ، اور وارثین میں بھی عصبہ کے طور پر تقسیم ہو گا نیز بیٹا پہلا
عصبہ ہو گا، پھر اس کے بعد باپ عصبہ ہو گا۔
اصول: بیٹا کے موجودگی میں باپ کو کچھ نہیں ملے گا۔
اصول: ولاء کانہ خرید و فروخت ہو سکتا ہے اور کسی کو نہ ہبہ کیا جاسکتا ہے۔
Chapter of Dhawi al-Arham. If [the deceased] leaves the grandfather of his freed slave and the brother of his freed slave, then the property goes to the grandfather according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: it is between them. Wala may not be sold nor gifted.
Wajh (2): the hadith for establishing: 'And when the freed slave leaves the father of his freed slave' from al-Hasan: 'It is for the son' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, a man died and left his son, his father, and his freed slave, then the freed slave died and left property, no. 31522).
Wajh (1): proof of Abu Yusuf: the statement of the tabi'i for establishing: 'And when the freed slave leaves the father of his freed slave' from Qatada, from Shuraih and Zayd ibn Thabit concerning a man who died and left his son, his father, and his freed slave, then the freed slave died and left property. Shuraih said: 'To his father one-sixth, and what remains is for the son.' Zayd ibn Thabit said: 'The property is for the son, and there is nothing for the father.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 31520)
Wajh (1): the statement of the tabi'i for establishing: 'If he leaves the grandfather of his freed slave and the brother of his freed slave, the property is for the grandfather' from al-Zuhri concerning a man who left his grandfather and his brother: 'Wala belongs to the grandfather because he is attributed to the grandfather, and not attributed to the brother.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 31534)
Wajh (2): the statement of the tabi'i for establishing: 'If he leaves the grandfather of his freed slave and the brother of his freed slave, the property is for the grandfather' from Ata' concerning a man who died and left a freed slave of his, his grandfather, and his brother: to whom is the wala of his freed slave? Ata' said: 'Wala is between them half and half.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, no. 31532)
Wajh (a): the hadith for establishing: 'Wala may not be sold nor gifted' from Ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) forbade the sale of wala and its gift.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, no. 2919)
Principles: The property of a freed slave is inherited as asabah, and among the heirs it is also divided as asabah, and the son is the first asabah, then after him the father is asabah.
Principle: In the presence of the son, the father gets nothing.
Principle: Wala cannot be bought or sold nor gifted to anyone.
Source pages p. 455

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's chapter on Dhawi al-Arham presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding inheritance of wala when the freed slave dies leaving a grandfather and a brother. The text first states the ruling: according to Abu Hanifa, the entire wala (and thus the inheritance from the freed slave's estate) goes to the grandfather. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad rule that it is divided equally between them. The text then provides proofs. It cites a hadith from al-Hasan that when the freed slave leaves the father of his freed slave, it goes to the son, which supports the principle that the nearer asabah excludes the more distant. For Abu Yusuf's position, it cites the opinions of Shuraih and Zayd ibn Thabit on a case involving son, father, and freed slave; Shuraih gave the father one-sixth and the rest to the son, while Zayd gave everything to the son, indicating the father does not inherit when there is a son. For Abu Hanifa's position, it cites al-Zuhri who said the wala goes to the grandfather because he is attributed to him (the grandfather) not the brother. However, Ata' said it is half and half, which supports the Sahibayn. Finally, a hadith prohibits selling or gifting wala, establishing that it is a right that cannot be transferred by contract. The Urdu commentary extracts three principles: (1) the property of a freed slave is inherited as asabah, with the son being the first asabah followed by the father; (2) in the presence of a son, the father gets nothing; (3) wala cannot be sold or gifted. This passage thus clarifies the rules of inheritance through wala and the hierarchy of asabah.

Key Terms
وَلاء (wala): The right of inheritance arising from freeing a slave; a bond of clientship.
ذَوِي الأَرْحَام (dhawil arham): Blood relatives who are not entitled to fixed shares (ashab al-faraid) nor asabah by themselves, but may inherit in the absence of those.
عَصَبَة (asabah): Residuary heirs who inherit the remainder after the fixed shares are distributed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a freed slave dies leaving his grandfather and his brother, how is the wala distributed?
A) All to the grandfather
B) All to the brother
C) Divided equally between them
D) Split 2/3 to grandfather, 1/3 to brother

Key Takeaway
The wala of a freed slave is inherited by the former master's asabah, and when both grandfather and brother are present, Abu Hanifa gives it all to the grandfather, while the Sahibayn split it equally.

Faraid — Inheritance
intermediate
8 min
Determining the Base Number and 'Awl in Inheritance
Matn on calculating asl al-mas'alah and 'awl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the asl al-mas'alah for any combination of fixed shares and apply the rule of 'awl and tashih as described in the matn.

Core Idea
The base number is the smallest denominator that works for the fractions; 'awl increases it when shares exceed the total.

This passage from Al-Quduri is the foundational matn for inheritance arithmetic. It lists the base numbers for common fraction combinations, explains when 'awl occurs, and provides the method for tashih when shares do not divide evenly among heirs. Mastering these rules is essential for accurate estate distribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fractions in the case
List all the fixed shares (e.g., 1/2, 1/3, 1/6, etc.) present in the estate.
Fractions are given as halves, thirds, fourths, sixths, etc.
2
Recall the base number for each combination
Use the matn's rules: e.g., half+half → base 2; half+third → base 6; fourth+third → base 12; eighth+two sixths → base 24.
The base is the least common multiple of the denominators of the fractions present.
3
Check if the sum of shares exceeds the base
Add the numerators. If the sum is greater than the base number, 'awl is needed. The base increases to one of the allowed values given in the matn.
e.g., half+third+sixth: sum = 3+2+1=6, not exceeding base 6, so no 'awl. But half+third+? can increase.
4
Apply tashih if shares don't divide evenly
If the shares of a group of heirs do not divide evenly among them, multiply the number of heirs into the base (or its 'awl) to get a corrected base fractionally larger.
Use the rules: equal numbers suffice; larger suffices; concordant numbers multiply.
5
Handle the case of a deceased heir before distribution
If an heir dies before receiving their share, treat their share as a new estate and recalculate using the same method.
This may require multiple rounds of tashih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حِسَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ
حِسَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - ا إذَا كَانَ فِي الْمَسْأَلَة نِصْفٌ وَنِصْفٌ أَوْ نِصْفٌ وَمَا بَقِيَ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ اثْنَيْنِ ل وَإِذَا كَانَ فِيهَا ثُلُثٌ وَمَا بَقِيَ أَوْ ثُلُثَانِ وَمَا بَقِيَ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ ثَلَاثَةٍ وَإِذَا كَانَ فِيهَا رُبْعٌ وَمَا بَقِيَ أَوْ رُبْعٌ وَنِصْفٌ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ أَرْبَعَةٍ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهَا كُمِّنْ وَمَا بَقِيَ أَوْ مِّنْ وَنِصْفٌ وَمَا بَقِيَ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ ثَمَانِيَةٍ ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهَا نِصْفٌ وَثُلُثٌ أَوْ نِصْفٌ وَسُدُسٌ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ سِتَّةٍ وَتَعُولُ إِلَى سَبْعَةٍ وَثَمَانِيَةٍ وَتِسْعَةٍ وَعَشْرَةٍ وَلَا تَعُولُ إِلَى غَيْرِ ذَلِكَ وَإِذَا كَانَ مَعَ الرُّبْعِ ثُلُثٌ أَوْ سُدُسٌ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ اثْنَيْ عَشَرَ وَتَعُولُ إِلَى ثَلَاثَةَ عَشَرَ وَخَمْسَةَ عَشَرَ وَسَبْعَةَ عَشَرَ وَإِذَا كَانَ مَعَ النُّمُنِ سُدُسَانِ أَوْ ثُلُثَانِ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ أَرْبَعَةٍ وَعِشْرِينَ وَتَعُولُ إِلَى سَبْعَةٍ وَعِشْرِينَ هي وَإِذَا انْقَسَمَتْ الْمَسْأَلَةُ عَلَى الْوَرَثَةِ فَقَدْ صَحَتْ وَإِنْ لَمْ تَنْقَسِمْ سِهَامُ كُلِّ فَرِيقٍ مِنْهُمْ عَلَيْهِمْ فَاضْرِبْ عَدَدَهُمْ فِي أَصْل الْفَرِيضَةِ وَعَوَلْها إِنْ كَانَتْ عَائِلَةً فَمَا خَرَّجَتْ صَحَتْ مِنْهُ الْمَسْأَلَهُ فَإِنْ وَافَقَ سِهَامَهُمْ عَدَدُهُمْ ضَرَبْت وَفْقَ عَدَدِهِمْ فِي أَصْلِ الْمَسْأَلَةِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْقَسِمْ سِهَامُ فَرِيقَيْنِ مِنْهُمْ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ فَاضْرِبْ أَحَدَ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ فِي الْآخَرِ
ثم مَا اجْتَمَعَ فِي الْفَرِيقِ الثَّالِثِ ثُمَّ مَا اجْتَمَعَ فِي أَصْل الْمَسْأَلَةِ فَإِنْ تَسَاوَتْ الْأَعْدَادُ أَجْزَاً أَحَدُهُمَا عَنْ الْآخَرِ كَامْرَأَتَيْنِ وَأَخَوَيْنِ فَاضْرِبْ اثْنَيْنِ فِي أَصْلِ الْمَسْأَلَةِ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُ الْعَدَدَيْنِ جُزْءًا مِنْ الْآخَرِ أَجْزَأَ الْأَكْثَرُ عَنْ الْأَقَلَ كَأَرْبَعِ نِسْوَةٍ وَأَخَوَيْنِ إِذَا ضَرَيْتِ الْأَرْبَعَةَ أَجْزَأَكَ عَنْ
عَدَدِ الْأَخَوَيْنِ فَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُ الْعَدَدَيْنِ مُوَافِقًا لِلْآخَرِ ضَرَبْت وَفْقَ أَحَدِهِمَا فِي جَمِيعِ الْآخَرِ ك فَإِذَا صَحَتْ الْمَسْأَلَةُ فَاضْرِبْ سِهَامَ كُلِ وَارِثٍ فِي التَرِكَةِ ثُمَّ اقْسِمْ مَا اجْتَمَعَ عَلَى مَا صَحَّتْ مِنْهُ الْفَرِيضَةُ يُخْرِجُ حَقَّ ذَلِكَ الْوَارِثِ فَإِنْ لَمْ تُقْسَمُ التَّرَكَةُ حَتَّى مَاتَ أَحَدُ الْوَرَثَةِ فَإِنْ كَانَ نَصِيبُهُ مِنْ الْمَيِّتِ الْأَوَّلِ يَنْقَسِمُ عَلَى عَدَدِ رُءُوسِ وَرَثَتِهِ فَاقْسِمْهُ وَقَدْ صَحَتْ مِنْهُ الْمَسْأَلَة وَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْقَسِمْ صَجَّحْت فَرِيضَةَ الْمَيِّتِ الثَّانِي بِالطَّرِيقَةِ الَّتِي ذَكَرْنَاهَا
وجه: (1)قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهَا نِصْفٌ وَثُلُثٌ \ عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، عَنْ عَلِيَّ، وَعَبْدِ اللَّهِ، وزَيْدٍ، «أَنَّهُمْ أَعَالُوا الْفَرِيضَةَ»» ) مصنف ابن ابي شيبه فِي الْفَرَائِضِ مَنْ قَالَ: لَا تَعُولُ وَمَنْ
أَعَالَهَا،نمبر 31190/السنن الكبري للبيهقي، بَابُ الْعَوْلِ فِي الْفَرَائِضِ،نمبر 12454)
Calculation of Inheritances.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: If in the case there is a half and a half, or a half and what remains, then its base is from two. If in it there is a third and what remains, or two-thirds and what remains, then its base is from three. If in it there is a fourth and what remains, or a fourth and a half, then its base is from four. If in it there is an eighth and what remains, or an eighth and a half and what remains, then its base is from eight. If in it there is a half and a third, or a half and a sixth, then its base is from six, and it increases ('awl) to seven, eight, nine, and ten, and it does not increase to other than that. If with the fourth there is a third or a sixth, then its base is from twelve, and it increases to thirteen, fifteen, and seventeen. If with the eighth there are two sixths or two thirds, then its base is from twenty-four, and it increases to twenty-seven.
When the case divides among the heirs, then it is correct. If the shares of each group among them do not divide upon them, then multiply their number into the base of the estate, and its 'awl if it is 'a'ilah (increasing), then whatever results, the case is correct from it. If the number of [heirs] agrees with their shares, you multiply the concordant number of them into the base of the case. If the shares of two groups or more do not divide, then multiply one of the groups into the other, then [multiply] the result into the third group, then the result into the base of the case. If the numbers are equal, one suffices for the other, like two wives and two brothers: multiply two into the base. If one number is a part of the other, the larger suffices for the smaller, like four women and two brothers; when you multiply the four it suffices you for the number of the two brothers. If one number is concordant with the other, you multiply the concordant number of one of them into the entire other. When the case is correct, multiply the shares of each heir into the inheritance, then divide the result by the corrected base of the estate; it gives the share of that heir. If the inheritance is not distributed until one of the heirs dies, if his share from the first deceased divides among the number of heads of his heirs, then divide it, and the case is correct from it. If it does not divide, correct the estate of the second deceased by the method we mentioned.
Wajh: (1) The statement of the tabi'i for establishing that half and third... from Ibrahim, from Ali, Abdullah, and Zayd, that they increased ('awl) the estate. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter of faraid, those who said 'awl does not occur and those who made 'awl, no. 31190 / Sunan al-Kubra al-Bayhaqi, no. 12454)
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri is a foundational matn on the arithmetic of inheritance (hisab al-faraid). It provides the standard method for determining the base number (asl al-mas'alah) of an inheritance estate based on the fractions present among the shares. For each combination of fractions (e.g., half and half, half and remainder, third and remainder, etc.), the author states the smallest base number from which the shares can be derived. He also explains the rule of 'awl (increase) when the sum of fractions exceeds one: the base number is increased to accommodate the total shares. For example, when half and third are present (1/2 + 1/3 = 5/6), the base is 6, but if it increases to 7, 8, 9, or 10, then 'awl applies. He then details the method for tashih (correction) when the shares of a group of heirs do not divide evenly among them: multiply the number of heirs into the base or its 'awl. He gives examples: if two wives and two brothers, multiply 2 (since both numbers are equal); if four women and two brothers, the larger number 4 suffices; if numbers are concordant, multiply a part of one into the other. Finally, he covers the scenario where an heir dies before distribution, requiring a new calculation. The passage ends with an athar from Ali, Abdullah, and Zayd confirming that they practiced 'awl. This matn is essential for anyone learning to compute inheritance shares accurately.

Key Terms
أصل المسألة (asl al-mas'alah): The smallest number from which all the fractional shares can be derived without fractions; the base denominator of the estate.
عول ('awl): The proportional increase of the base denominator when the sum of fixed shares exceeds the original base, to accommodate all shares.
تصحيح (tashih): The process of adjusting the base number to obtain whole numbers for the shares of each heir when the shares do not divide evenly among the members of a group.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the base number (asl al-mas'alah) when the estate contains a half and a sixth?
A) 2
B) 3
C) 6
D) 12

Key Takeaway
The base number is the LCM of the denominators; 'awl increases it when the numerator sum exceeds the base, and tashih corrects for uneven divisions among heirs.

Determining the Base Number in Faraid
Rules for finding the asl of a faraid problem when certain fractions are present.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the base number (asl al-mas'alah) for a faraid problem when given combinations of common fractions (half, third, fourth, eighth, sixth) and state the correct base number.

Core Idea
The base number is the smallest common denominator of the fractional shares.

In Hanafi faraid, the first step in solving an inheritance problem is to determine the base number (asl al-mas'alah), which is the common denominator from which all heirs' shares are derived. Imam Al-Quduri provides a clear set of rules for common fraction combinations. This lesson will guide you through applying these rules to quickly find the base number.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fractions
Look at the inheritance problem: list all fractional shares mentioned (e.g., half, third, eighth). Note the residue (asabah) if present.
2
Apply the rule for each fraction
Based on the fractions present, use Al-Quduri's rules: if only half/half or half+residue → base=2; if third or two-thirds → base=3; if fourth → base=4; if eighth → base=8; if half+third or half+sixth → base=6.
The residue (asabah) does not affect the base.
3
Verify with the sum of shares
After assigning shares, the numerators should sum to the base number. For example, if base=6, check that 3 (half) + 2 (third) = 5, leaving 1 for residue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حِسَابُ الْفَرَائِضِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - إذَا كَانَ فِي الْمَسْأَلَة نِصْفٌ وَنِصْفٌ أَوْ نِصْفٌ وَمَا بَقِيَ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ اثْنَيْنِ وَإِذَا كَانَ فِيهَا ثُلُثٌ وَمَا بَقِيَ أَوْ ثُلُثَانِ وَمَا بَقِيَ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ ثَلَاثَةٍ وَإِذَا كَانَ فِيهَا رُبْعٌ وَمَا بَقِيَ أَوْ رُبْعٌ وَنِصْفٌ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ أَرْبَعَةٍ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهَا ثُمُنٌ وَمَا بَقِيَ أَوْ ثُمُنٌ وَنِصْفٌ وَمَا بَقِيَ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ ثَمَانِيَةٍ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِيهَا نِصْفٌ وَثُلُثٌ أَوْ نِصْفٌ وَسُدُسٌ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ سِتَّةٍ
Calculation of inheritance shares. He said - may Allah have mercy on him - If in the case there is a half and a half, or a half and the remainder, then its base is from two. If in it there is a third and the remainder, or two-thirds and the remainder, then its base is from three. If in it there is a fourth and the remainder, or a fourth and a half, then its base is from four. If in it there is an eighth and the remainder, or an eighth and a half and the remainder, then its base is from eight. If in it there is a half and a third, or a half and a sixth, then its base is from six.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn on faraid opens by stating the method to determine the base number (asl al-mas'alah) for an inheritance problem. The base number is the smallest common denominator from which the shares can be derived. When the shares are half and half, or half and the residue (asabah), the base is 2. When a third or two-thirds appear, the base is 3. When a fourth appears, with or without a half, the base is 4. When an eighth appears, the base is 8. When a half with a third or a half with a sixth appear, the base is 6. These are foundational rules for setting up the problem.

Key Terms
أصل المسألة (asl al-mas'alah): The lowest common denominator from which the shares of all heirs can be derived in a faraid problem.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the base number (asl) for a case with a half and a half?
A) 2
B) 4
C) 6
D) 8

Key Takeaway
The base number is the least common multiple of the denominators of the fractional shares present.

The Limited Cases of 'Awl in Faraid
Ruling with proof explaining the limited numeric cases of 'awl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three base numbers that can undergo 'awl and list the possible increased denominators for each.

Core Idea
Only bases 6, 12, and 24 can have 'awl; other bases never require it.

In inheritance calculations, sometimes the sum of the prescribed shares exceeds the total estate. This requires 'awl — a proportional increase of the denominator. The Hanafi school, following the practice of the Companions, recognizes that 'awl only occurs for three specific base numbers. This lesson identifies those bases and their possible 'awl numbers, providing the precise cases you must know.

Guided Path
1
Recall the definition of 'awl
Define 'awl as the proportional increase of the denominator when the sum of shares exceeds the base. Understand that it preserves the ratios among heirs.
2
Identify the three base numbers
The text mentions that 'awl only occurs for bases 6, 12, and 24. Memorize these as the only possible starting points for 'awl.
These correspond to common family structures involving parents, spouse, and siblings.
3
For base 6, list the possible 'awl numbers
Base 6 can increase to 7, 8, 9, or 10. This happens when certain combinations of heirs (e.g., husband, sister, mother) cause the sum to exceed 6.
Example: husband (1/2), sister (1/2), mother (1/3) sum to 1.166 which requires base 7.
4
For base 12, list the possible 'awl numbers
Base 12 can increase to 13, 15, or 17. This occurs when a quarter is present along with a third or a sixth, as stated in the text.
Example: wife (1/4), mother (1/3), and father (1/6) sum to 3/4 which needs base 12? Actually that sums to 3/4, not exceeding. More typical: wife (1/4), two daughters (2/3), mother (1/6) sum to 1.083, base 13.
5
For base 24, list the possible 'awl number
Base 24 can only increase to 27. This happens when an eighth is present along with two sixths or two thirds.
Example: wife (1/8), mother (1/6), father (1/6), daughter (1/2) sum to 23/24, not exceeding? Wait, need an example that exceeds 24. Typically: wife (1/8), two sisters (2/3), mother (1/6) sum to 1.125, base 27.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَتَعُولُ إِلَى سَبْعَةٍ وَثَمَانِيَةٍ وَتِسْعَةٍ وَعَشْرَةٍ وَلَا تَعُولُ إِلَى غَيْرِ ذَلِكَ وَإِذَا كَانَ مَعَ الرُّبْعِ ثُلُثٌ أَوْ سُدُسٌ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ اثْنَيْ عَشَرَ وَتَعُولُ إِلَى ثَلَاثَةَ عَشَرَ وَخَمْسَةَ عَشَرَ وَسَبْعَةَ عَشَرَ وَإِذَا كَانَ مَعَ الثُّمُنِ سُدُسَانِ أَوْ ثُلُثَانِ فَأَصْلُهَا مِنْ أَرْبَعَةٍ وَعِشْرِينَ وَتَعُولُ إِلَى سَبْعَةٍ وَعِشْرِينَ
And it ('awl) increases to seven, eight, nine, and ten, and it does not increase to other than that. And when with the fourth there is a third or a sixth, then its base is from twelve, and it increases to thirteen, fifteen, and seventeen. And when with the eighth there are two sixths or two thirds, then its base is from twenty-four, and it increases to twenty-seven.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This passage addresses 'awl, the principle where the sum of prescribed shares exceeds the base number, requiring a proportional increase of the denominator. The author states that 'awl only occurs for base 6 (increasing to 7,8,9,10), base 12 (increasing to 13,15,17), and base 24 (increasing to 27). These are the only cases in standard faraid. This is based on the practice of the Companions, as indicated by the hadith that follows.

Key Terms
العول (al-'awl): Proportional increase of the denominator when the sum of prescribed shares exceeds the base number.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 13, 15, 17
B) 14, 16, 18
C) 7, 8, 9
D) 27 only

Key Takeaway
Only bases 6, 12, and 24 can undergo 'awl, and each has a fixed set of possible increased denominators.

Basic Tashih: Correcting Shares When a Group's Shares Do Not Divide
Procedure for adjusting inheritance base when shares do not divide among heirs of the same category.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi method of tashih by multiplying the base by the number of heirs or using wafq when shares do not divide evenly.

Core Idea
When heirs of one category cannot split their shares evenly, multiply the base by their count or use the greatest common divisor.

In inheritance calculations, sometimes the shares allocated to a group of heirs (e.g., multiple wives or brothers) do not divide evenly among the individuals in that group. The Hanafi school provides a clear method to adjust the base number of the inheritance (asl al-mas'alah) so that each heir receives an integer share. This rule, called tashih, ensures the estate is divided without fractions.

Guided Path
1
Identify need for correction
Check if the shares of a category (e.g., wives) divide evenly among the individuals of that category. If not, tashih is required.
For a single category, compare total shares to number of individuals.
2
Determine relationship between shares and number
If the shares and number are exactly divisible (tabaayun), multiply the base by the number. If they share a common factor (tawaafuq), multiply by the wafq (GCD). If they are equal, one number suffices.
Treat multiple categories by combining stepwise.
3
Apply correction to base
Multiply the original base (asl al-mas'alah) by the required factor (number or wafq) to obtain the corrected base.
If 'awl occurred, multiply the 'a'ilah base.
4
Distribute shares using corrected base
Each heir's share from the corrected base is multiplied by the actual estate value, then divided by the corrected base to give the final share.
The corrected base ensures integer shares for all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا انْقَسَمَتْ الْمَسْأَلَةُ عَلَى الْوَرَثَةِ فَقَدْ صَحَتْ وَإِنْ لَمْ تَنْقَسِمْ سِهَامُ كُلِّ فَرِيقٍ مِنْهُمْ عَلَيْهِمْ فَاضْرِبْ عَدَدَهُمْ فِي أَصْل الْفَرِيضَةِ وَعَوَلْها إِنْ كَانَتْ عَائِلَةً فَمَا خَرَّجَتْ صَحَتْ مِنْهُ الْمَسْأَلَهُ فَإِنْ وَافَقَ سِهَامَهُمْ عَدَدُهُمْ ضَرَبْت وَفْقَ عَدَدِهِمْ فِي أَصْلِ الْمَسْأَلَةِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْقَسِمْ سِهَامُ فَرِيقَيْنِ مِنْهُمْ أَوْ أَكْثَرَ فَاضْرِبْ أَحَدَ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ فِي الْآخَرِ ثُمَّ مَا اجْتَمَعَ فِي الْفَرِيقِ الثَّالِثِ ثُمَّ مَا اجْتَمَعَ فِي أَصْل الْمَسْأَلَةِ فَإِنْ تَسَاوَتْ الْأَعْدَادُ أَجْزَاً أَحَدُهُمَا عَنْ الْآخَرِ كَامْرَأَتَيْنِ وَأَخَوَيْنِ فَاضْرِبْ اثْنَيْنِ فِي أَصْلِ الْمَسْأَلَةِ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُ الْعَدَدَيْنِ جُزْءًا مِنْ الْآخَرِ أَجْزَأَ الْأَكْثَرُ عَنِ الْأَقَلَ كَأَرْبَعِ نِسْوَةٍ وَأَخَوَيْنِ إِذَا ضَرَيْتِ الْأَرْبَعَةَ أَجْزَأَكَ عَنْ عَدَدِ الْأَخَوَيْنِ فَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُ الْعَدَدَيْنِ مُوَافِقًا لِلْآخَرِ ضَرَبْت وَفْقَ أَحَدِهِمَا فِي جَمِيعِ الْآخَرِ ك فَإِذَا صَحَتْ الْمَسْأَلَةُ فَاضْرِبْ سِهَامَ كُلِ وَارِثٍ فِي التَرِكَةِ ثُمَّ اقْسِمْ مَا اجْتَمَعَ عَلَى مَا صَحَّتْ مِنْهُ الْفَرِيضَةُ يُخْرِجُ حَقَّ ذَلِكَ الْوَارِثِ فَإِنْ لَمْ تُقْسَمُ التَّرَكَةُ حَتَّى مَاتَ أَحَدُ الْوَرَثَةِ فَإِنْ كَانَ نَصِيبُهُ مِنْ الْمَيِّتِ الْأَوَّلِ يَنْقَسِمُ عَلَى عَدَدِ رُءُوسِ وَرَثَتِهِ فَاقْسِمْهُ وَقَدْ صَحَتْ مِنْهُ الْمَسْأَلَة وَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْقَسِمْ صَحَّحْت فَرِيضَةَ الْمَيِّتِ الثَّانِي بِالطَّرِيقَةِ الَّتِي ذَكَرْنَاهَا وَثُمَّ ضَرَبْت إِحْدَى الْمَسْأَلَتَيْنِ فِي الْأُخْرَى إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ سِهَامُ الْمَيِّتِ الثَّانِي تُوَافِقُ مَا صَحَتْ مِنْهُ فَرِيضَتُهُ فَإِنْ كَانَتْ سِهَامُهُمْ مُوَافِقَةً فَاضْرِبْ وَفْقَ الْمَسْأَلَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ فِي الْأُولَى فَمَا اجْتَمَعَ صَحَتْ مِنْهُ الْمَسْأَلَتَانِ فَكُلُّ مَنْ لَهُ شَيْءٌ مِنْ الْمَسْأَلَةِ الْأُولَى يَأْخُذُهُ مَضْرُوبًا فِي وَفْقِ الْمَسْأَلَةِ الثَّانِيَةِ وَكُلُّ مَنْ لَهُ شَيْءٌ مِنْ الْمَسْأَلَةِ يَأْخُذُهُ مَضْرُوبًا فِي وَفْقِ تَرِكَةِ الْمَيِّتِ الثَّانِي
And if the case divides among the heirs, then it is correct. If the shares of each group among them do not divide upon them, then multiply their number in the base of the inheritance and its 'awl if it is 'a'ilah. Whatever comes out, the case is correct from it. If their number agrees with their shares, multiply the concordance (wafq) of their number in the base of the case. If the shares of two groups or more do not divide, then multiply one of the two groups by the other, then what is gathered by the third group, then what is gathered in the base of the case. If the numbers are equal, one suffices for the other, like two wives and two brothers: multiply two in the base. If one of the two numbers is a part of the other, the greater suffices for the lesser, like four women and two brothers: if you multiply four, it suffices for the number of the two brothers. If one of the two numbers is consonant with the other, multiply the wafq of one of them in all of the other. And when the case is correct, multiply the shares of each heir by the estate, then divide what is gathered by what the inheritance is correct from; it gives the right of that heir. If the estate is not divided until one of the heirs dies, if his share from the first deceased divides upon the number of heads of his heirs, then divide it and the case is correct from it. If it does not divide, correct the inheritance of the second deceased by the method we mentioned. Then multiply one of the two cases by the other if the shares of the second deceased do not agree with what his inheritance is correct from. If their shares agree, multiply the wafq of the second case by the first, and what is gathered, both cases are correct from it. Everyone who has something from the first case takes it multiplied by the wafq of the second case, and everyone who has something from the case takes it multiplied by the wafq of the estate of the second deceased.
Source pages p. 456

Commentary
This lengthy passage explains the process of tashih (correction) when the shares of a category of heirs (e.g., multiple wives) do not divide evenly among them. The method involves multiplying the base by the number of heirs or using the greatest common divisor (wafq) when there is a common factor. The text also covers cases of munasakhat (successive deaths) where an heir dies before distribution. The author gives practical examples: with two wives and two brothers, multiply base by 2; with four women and two brothers, multiply by 4 (since 2 is a part of 4). When numbers are in tawaafuq (consonance), multiply the wafq. Finally, for munasakhat, adjust the second deceased's inheritance by the same principles.

Key Terms
تصحيح (tashih): Adjusting the base number so that shares can be distributed evenly among heirs of the same category.
وفق (wafq): The greatest common divisor (GCD) of two numbers, used when there is a common factor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of 4 wives with total share 4 and two brothers with total share 8, from base 12, what is the correct tashih multiplier?
A) Multiply base by 4
B) Multiply base by 2
C) Multiply base by 6
D) No correction needed

Key Takeaway
When the shares of a category of heirs do not divide evenly among its members, you must adjust the base by multiplying by the number of individuals or by their wafq, depending on the numerical relationship.
